Talaq — Divorce

Revocable Divorce and Inheritance During 'Iddah
General rule: wife inherits from every revocable divorce if husband dies during 'iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a revocably divorced wife inherits from her husband if he dies during her 'iddah, and explain the legal reason (ʿillah) why.

Core Idea
A revocable divorce does not end the marital bond; therefore inheritance rights survive during the 'iddah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a general rule: whenever a husband retains the right to take back his wife (rajʿah), the marriage is partially intact, and so the wife inherits if the husband dies during her waiting period. The author, al-Marghinani, reinforces that this applies to all revocable divorces, not just those pronounced in deathbed illness. Understanding this rule requires grasping the nature of revocable divorce as a non-final dissolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is a revocable divorce (talāq rajʿī) followed by the husband's death during the wife's ʿiddah. The ruling is that the wife inherits.
2
Locate the proof
The text gives the reason: revocable divorce does not remove the marriage completely; intercourse remains permissible, so the cause (sabab) of inheritance—marriage—still exists.
The proof is based on the nature of revocable divorce.
3
Analyze the ʿillah
The effective cause is the persistence of the marital bond. Because the husband can return to her without a new contract, the marriage is not fully severed.
4
Note the condition
The inheritance is conditional upon the husband dying during the ʿiddah. If the ʿiddah ends, the marriage is fully dissolved and she does not inherit.
5
Distinguish from irrevocable divorce
In a triple (ba'in) divorce, the marriage ends immediately, and she does not inherit even if he dies during ʿiddah.
This contrast helps reinforce the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہر وہ طلاق جس میں شوہر کو رجوع کا اختیار ہے ان تمام صورتوں میں عورت وارث ہوگی
قال رضى الله تعالى عنه والطلاق الذي يملك فيه الرجعة ترث به في جميع الوجوه لما بينا انه لايزيل النكاح حتى يحل الوطى فكان السبب قائما و كلما ذكرنا انها ترث الماترث اذامات وهي في العدة وقد بيناه ترجمہ مصنف رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ نے فرمایا کہ وہ طلاق جس میں شوہر کو رجعت کا اختیار ہے اس کی تمام صورتوں میں عورت وارث ہو گی۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی کہ طلاق رجعی نکاح کو زائل نہیں کرتی ہے ۔ حتی کہ اس سے ولی کرنا حلال ہے۔ تو سبب قائم کر دیا اور ہر وہ موقع کہ جہاں ہم نے ذکر کیا کہ عورت وارث ہوگی ۔ (اس وقت) وارث ہو گی جبکہ شوہر عورت کی عدت میں مرا ہو اور ہم اس کو ( اول باب میں ) بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح مصنف ہدایہ نے اس عبارت میں دو باتیں بیان کی ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو مرض الموت میں طلاق رجعی دی ۔ پھر عدت میں مر گیا تو یہ عورت وارث ہوگی۔ سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے کہ طلاق رجعی نکاح کو زائل نہیں کرتی حتی کہ طلاق رجعی کے بعد اق رجعی - عورت کے ساتھ وطی کرنا حلال ہے۔ پس وراثت کا سبب یعنی نکاح موجود ہے جس کی وجہ سے عورت وارث ہوگی۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ جس موقع پر عورت وارث ہوگی اسکے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جبھی وارث ہوگی جبکہ شوہر ایسی حالت میں مرا ہو کہ عورت عدت میں ہے اور ہم سابق میں یعنی شروع باب میں اس کو بالتفصیل بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب ۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ سکر ڈوی
Every divorce in which the husband has the right of return (raj'ah), in all such cases the woman will inherit. He (the author, may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'And the divorce in which he has the right of return, she inherits by it in all aspects, because we have explained that it does not remove the marriage such that intercourse becomes permissible, so the cause (of inheritance) remains. And whenever we mentioned that she inherits, she inherits when he dies while she is in the 'iddah, and we have explained it.' Translation: The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: That divorce in which the husband has the right of return, in all its forms the woman will inherit. Due to the proof we have stated that revocable divorce does not nullify the marriage, such that intercourse is permissible from her. So the cause (of inheritance) is established. And whenever we mentioned that she inherits, she inherits when the husband dies while the woman is in 'iddah, and we have already explained it in the beginning of the chapter. Explanation: The author of Hidayah stated two things in this passage: one is that if a husband gave his wife a revocable divorce in deathbed illness, then died during the 'iddah, this woman inherits – due to the prior proof that revocable divorce does not nullify the marriage, such that after revocable divorce, intercourse with the woman is permissible. So the cause of inheritance, i.e., marriage, exists, therefore the woman inherits. The second thing is that the occasion when she inherits means she inherits only when the husband dies while she is in 'iddah, and we have already explained this in detail at the beginning of the chapter. And Allah knows best what is correct. Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven, scribe.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage states a general Hanafi rule: any revocable divorce (talāq raj'ī) always results in the wife inheriting from the husband if he dies during her 'iddah period. The reason is that a revocable divorce does not completely dissolve the marriage; the husband retains the right to take her back (raj'ah) without a new contract, and intercourse remains permissible for him during 'iddah. Therefore, the marital bond (nikah) is still partially intact, and since marriage is the cause of inheritance, she inherits. The text emphasizes that this applies in all cases where the husband has the right of return – meaning one or two revocable divorces, not three irrevocable ones. The condition is that the husband must die while the wife is still in her 'iddah. This ruling is consistent with the earlier discussion in the chapter on divorce of the sick person. The commentary clarifies that the author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) is here reinforcing that the wife inherits not only in the specific case of deathbed divorce but in all revocable divorces, as long as the death occurs during 'iddah. The scribe's note at the end is a typical colophon.

Key Terms
طلاق رجعی (talāq raj'ī): A revocable divorce where the husband can take his wife back during her 'iddah without a new marriage contract.
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period after divorce or death during which the woman cannot remarry; for a divorced woman, three menstrual cycles or three months.
رجعت (raj'ah): The husband's act of taking back his wife during 'iddah after a revocable divorce, restoring marital rights without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a wife inherit from her husband after a revocable divorce?
A) Only if the divorce was pronounced in deathbed illness.
B) Only if the husband explicitly stated that he intends inheritance.
C) In all cases provided the husband dies during her 'iddah.
D) She never inherits after any divorce.

Key Takeaway
A revocable divorce preserves the marriage bond during 'iddah, so the wife inherits if the husband dies in that period.

Raj'ah: Definition, Conditions, and Proofs
Introduction to the legal chapter on Raj'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of raj'ah, list its five conditions, and cite the Quranic and hadith proofs for its legitimacy according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Raj'ah is the husband's unilateral right to resume the marriage during 'iddah without a new contract.

The chapter on Raj'ah logically follows divorce because it is the natural next step after a revocable talaq. Understanding raj'ah is crucial for anyone dealing with family law, as it defines the boundaries of marital reconciliation. In this lesson, we will unpack the linguistic and legal meaning of raj'ah, its essential conditions, and the solid textual proofs that establish its validity.

Guided Path
1
Define raj'ah linguistically and legally
Start with the Arabic root r-j-‘ meaning 'to return'. Then move to the Shariah definition: maintaining the marriage ownership as before after a revocable divorce during ‘iddah.
The commentary notes the pronunciation nuances (fatha vs kasra) – the fatha version is more correct.
2
List the five conditions for valid raj'ah
From the passage, extract: (1) divorce with explicit or certain allusive words, (2) no compensation, (3) less than three divorces, (4) wife must be consummated (madhūl bihā), (5) ‘iddah must still be ongoing.
Condition (4) ensures the divorce is revocable; non-consummated divorces are bā'in.
3
Identify the Quranic proof for raj'ah
Find the verse ‘And their husbands are more entitled to take them back’ (2:228) – this directly grants the husband the right to raj'ah. Also ‘fa-imsikūhunna bi-ma'rūf’ (2:229) which commands retention with kindness.
Both verses are Qur'anic, hence qat'ī al-thubūt and qat'ī al-dalāla.
4
Note the hadith and ijma proof
The Prophet (SAW) told 'Umar to command his son to take back his wife, and the Prophet himself made raj'ah to Sawdah. Ijma of the companions also confirms its validity.
The passage states there is no dispute about the legitimacy of raj'ah itself.
5
Understand the unilateral nature of raj'ah
The matn from Al-Hidayah explicitly says the husband may take her back whether she agrees or not. Raj'ah is a continuation of ownership, not a new contract.
This distinguishes Hanafi view from any possible claim that consent is required.

Source Text

تشریح چونکہ رجعت طلاق سے طبعا موخر ہے اسلئے وضعا اور ذکر ابھی مؤخر کر دیا گیا تا کہ وضع طبع کے موافق ہو جائے۔ رجعت ، راء کے فتحہ اور کسرہ کے ساتھ ہے۔ مگر فتح کے ساتھ پڑھنا انصح ہے۔ رَجَعَ يَرجِعُ ضرب سے ہے۔ معنی ہیں واپس آنا ، لوٹنا، کہا جاتا ہے الی الله مرجک ۔ رجع لازم اور متعدی دونوں طرح مستعمل ہے۔ پس رجوع مصدر لازم ہے۔ جیسے قعود اور جلوس ۔ لازم کی نظیر باری تعالى كا قول لئن رجعنا الى المدينة (اگر لوٹے ہم شہر کی طرف) فلما رجعوا الى ابيهم (پس جب وہ اپنے باپ کی طرف لوٹے ) و انا الیه راجعون (اور ہم اسی کی طرف لوٹیں گئے ) اور متعدی میں استعمال کی مثال باری تعالیٰ کا قول فان رجعك الله الى طائفة منهم (اگر لوٹا دے تجھ کو اللہ ان میں سے ایک جماعت کی طرف) ثم ارجع البصر (پھر لوٹا تو اپنی نگاہ)۔
شریعت کی اصطلاح میں رجعت کہتے ہیں ملک نکاح کو برابر بدستور رکھنا اور رجعت کیلئے چند شرطیں ہیں ان کو بھی ملاحظہ کر نیچے : ۱) لفظ صریحی کے ساتھ طلاق دینا یا بعض الفاظ کنایہ کے ساتھ جن کا ذکر سابق میں گذر کا۔ یعنی اعتدی، استقبر کی رحمک ، انت واحدة ) طلاق کے عوض میں مال نہ ہو۔ ۳) تین طلاقیں نہ واقع کرے۔
(۴) عورت مدخول بہا ہو۔
(۵) عدت موجود ہو۔
رجعت کا ثبوت کتاب اللہ، حدیث اور اجماع نینوں سے ہے۔ اسلئے اسکی مشروعیت میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ کتاب سے ثبوت کی مثال و بُعولتهنَّ أَحَقُّ بِرَدَهنَ اى برجُعَتهنَّ اور حدیث سے ثبوت کی مثال حضرت عمر سے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول مر ابنک فليراجعها اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت سودہ سے مراجعت فرمائی اور رجعت کی صحت پر اجماع بھی منعقد ہوا ہے۔ (مینی شرح کنز ) مرد نے بیوی کو ایک طلاق یا دو طلاقیں رجعی دیں شوہر عدت میں رجوع کر سکتا ہے عورت رضا مند ہو یا نہ ہو

ترجمہ اور جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی کو ایک طلاق رجعی یا دو طلاقیں دیں تو مرد کو اختیار ہے کہ عدت میں عورت سے مراجعت کر لے (خواہ ) اس پر عورت راضی ہو یا نہ ہو۔ باری تعالیٰ کے قول فامسكوهن بمعروف کی وجہ سے ( روک لوان کو دستور شرع کے مطابق )
Chapter of Raj'ah. Translation: (This) chapter is about the ruling of Raj'ah. (Incorrectly labeled 'باب طلاق المريض' in OCR) Explanation: Since Raj'ah is naturally later than divorce, therefore it is postponed in placement and discussion to match natural order. Raj'ah is with fatha and kasra on the ra', but reading with fatha is more correct. Raj'a yarji'u is from the pattern of daraba. Meaning: to come back, to return. It is said: 'To Allah is your return.' Raj'a is used as both intransitive and transitive. So rujū' is an intransitive infinitive like qu'ūd and julūs. Examples of intransitive: Allah's saying 'If we return to the city,' 'When they returned to their father,' 'And to Him we return.' Examples of transitive: Allah's saying 'Then if Allah returns you to a group of them,' 'Then return your gaze.' In Shariah terminology, Raj'ah means maintaining ownership of marriage as before. And there are several conditions for Raj'ah, observe them below: 1) The divorce must be with a clear word or with some allusive words mentioned before, i.e., i'taddī, istabrī, etc. 2) No compensation (mal) in exchange for the divorce. 3) Must not be three divorces. 4) The woman must be consummated (madhūl bihā). 5) The 'iddah must exist. The proof of Raj'ah is from the Book of Allah, Sunnah, and Ijma. Therefore, there is no dispute about its legitimacy. Example from the Book: 'And their husbands are more entitled to take them back' (2:228). Example from Sunnah: The Prophet's (SAW) statement to 'Umar: 'Command your son to take her back.' And the Prophet (SAW) made raj'ah to Sawdah. And Ijma has occurred on the validity of Raj'ah. (From Minhat al-Kanz) The man gives one or two revocable divorces; the husband can take her back during her 'iddah whether she agrees or not. And when a man divorces his wife with one revocable divorce or two, then he has the right to take her back in her 'iddah, whether she agrees or not, due to the statement of Allah: 'Then retain them with kindness' (2:229) without distinction. And the existence of 'iddah is necessary because raj'ah is continuation of ownership. Do you not see that it is called 'imsaak' (retention) which is keeping? And the continuation is only realized within 'iddah because there is no ownership after its expiry. Translation: And when a man gave his wife one revocable divorce or two, then the man has the option to take her back during 'iddah, whether she agrees or not, due to Allah's saying 'fa-imsikūhunna bi-ma'rūf' (then retain them with kindness).
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Raj'ah (the husband's right to take back his wife after a revocable divorce). The commentary explains that the chapter is placed after divorce because Raj'ah naturally follows divorce. It then gives a linguistic definition of 'raj'ah' and its usage in the Quran. In Shariah, Raj'ah means maintaining the marriage bond as it was before the divorce. The conditions for Raj'ah are listed: (1) the divorce must have been pronounced with explicit words or certain allusive words (like 'i'taddī', 'istabrī', 'anta wāḥidah'), (2) there must be no compensation (i.e., it is not a khul' divorce), (3) it must not be three divorces, (4) the wife must have been consummated, and (5) her 'iddah must still be ongoing. The legitimacy of Raj'ah is proven by Quran (2:228: 'And their husbands are more entitled to take them back'), Hadith (the Prophet's instruction to 'Umar regarding his son's divorce), and Ijma (consensus). Finally, the matn from al-Hidayah clarifies that the husband can take her back during 'iddah regardless of her consent, based on the verse 'fa-imsikūhunna bi-ma'rūf' (2:229). The reason is that Raj'ah is a continuation of the existing marital ownership, not a new contract, and this continuation is only possible while the 'iddah remains; after 'iddah, the marriage is completely dissolved and a new contract would be needed.

Key Terms
رجعت (raj'ah): In Shariah, maintaining the marriage ownership as before after a revocable divorce; taking the wife back during 'iddah.
مدخول بہا (madhūl bihā): A woman with whom the husband has consummated the marriage (actual intercourse).
امساک (imsāk): Retaining the wife in marriage with kindness; used in the Quran for raj'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following conditions is necessary for a valid raj'ah?
A) The wife must consent to the return.
B) The divorce must have been pronounced three times.
C) The wife must have been consummated (madhūl bihā).
D) The husband must pay a new dower.

Key Takeaway
Raj'ah is the husband's unilateral right to resume the marriage during 'iddah after a revocable divorce, proven by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, requiring specific conditions including consummation and ongoing 'iddah.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
10 min
The Definition and Proofs of Raj'ah (Revocation of Divorce)
Defines raj'ah, condition of 'iddah, and agreed verbal form

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of raj'ah, identify its essential conditions, and explain why the husband's consent alone is sufficient based on the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Raj'ah is the husband's unilateral right to retain the marriage during 'iddah without the wife's consent — confirmed by Quran and consensus.

In this lesson, we unpack the Hanafi ruling on raj'ah (revocable divorce revocation). The passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah establishes raj'ah as a continuation of the marriage contract, not a new one, and explains that it requires the wife to be in her 'iddah. The verbal formula 'I take you back' is explicit and agreed upon by all four Imams. We will examine the Quranic and hadith proofs and understand why the wife's consent is not a condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Raj'ah is the husband's act of taking back his wife during her 'iddah after a revocable divorce. The ruling is that it is valid and effective, restoring the marriage without a new contract.
The Hanafi school considers raj'ah as istidāma (continuation), not a fresh contract.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse al-Baqarah 2:231 is the key proof: 'So when they have [almost] reached their term, hold them back with kindness or part with them with kindness.' The imperative 'amsikūhunna' indicates the permission and practice of raj'ah.
The verse addresses the husband directly, affirming his right to retain the wife during 'iddah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'hold them back' is absolute; it does not condition raj'ah on the wife's consent. Therefore, the Hanafi ruling is that the husband can revoke unilaterally.
The dalālah is considered zanni because the absolute command could be qualified by other texts, but here no such qualification exists.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (difference)
There is no disagreement among the four Imams regarding the explicit verbal form (saying 'I take you back' or 'I take back my wife'). All consider it valid for raj'ah.
This consensus (ijmā') strengthens the binding nature of the ruling.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position for fatwa
The mufta bihi position is that raj'ah is valid with or without witnesses; witnesses are only for proof. The presence of 'iddah is essential.
Witnesses are not a condition (shart), only a means of evidence if the wife later denies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب طلاق المريض
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد بینیم بغیر کسی تفصیل کے اور عدت کا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ رجعت (کے معنی) ملک کو برقرار رکھنا ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتا کہ اس کا نام امساک رکھا گیا ہے اور امساک باقی رکھنا ہے اور برابر باقی رکھنا تو عدت ہی میں ہو سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ عدت گذر جانے کے بعد ملک نکاح نہیں رہتی۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب مرد نے اپنی مدخول بہا بیوی کو ایک طلاق رجعی یا دو طلاقیں دے دیں تو مرد کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اس سے اسکی عدت میں مراجعت کر لے۔ عورت اس پر راضی ہو یا نہ ہو ۔ دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَإِذَا بَلَغْنَ أَجَلَهُنَّ فَأَمْسِكُوهُنَّ بِمَعْرُوفٍ أَوْ فَارِقُوهُنَّ بِمَعْرُوف یعنی جب عورتوں کی عدت قریب اتم ہو جائے تو تم کو اختیار ہے۔ اگر رجعت کو اختیار کرنا چاہوتو بغیر ضرر پہنچائے ان کو روک لو اور اگر جدا کرنے کا ارادہ ہو تو بغیر ضرر پہنچائے ان کو جدا کر دو ۔ اس آیت میں مطلقا مراجعت کا ذکر ہے۔ عورت کی رضاء یا عدم رضاء کی تفصیل نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے رجعت کا حکم مطلق رکھا گیا۔
دوسری دلیل ابوداؤد کی روایت ہے: عن عمر رضی الله تعالى عنه ان النبى طلق حفصة رضى الله تعالى عنها ثم
راجعها اور حدیث ابن عمر میں ہے انه علیه السلام قال له مر ابنك فليراجعها الحديث (متفق عليه ) اور رجعت کیلئے عدت کا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رجعت نام ہے ملک نکاح کو برقرار رکھنا۔ چنانچہ آپ دیکھئے کہ قرآن پاک میں رجعت کا نام امساک ہے اور امساک کے معنی ہیں باقی رکھنا اور ملک نکاح کو برابر باقی رکھنا عدت میں ہوسکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ عدت گذر جانے کے بعد ملک نکاح ہی نہیں رہتی تو باقی رکھنا کہاں سے ہو گا۔ پس جب عدت پوری ہو گئی تو محل امساک نہیں
رہے گا۔
رجوع قولی اور فعلی
والرجعة ان يقول راجعتک او راجعت امرأتي وهذا صريح في الرجعة ولا خلاف بين الائمة
ترجمہ اور رجعت یہ ہے کہ عورت کو خطاب کر کے یوں کہے کہ میں نے تم سے رجعت کر لی۔ یالوگوں کے سامنے کہے کہ میں نے اپنی بیوی سے رجعت کر لی۔ اور رجعت کے مسئلہ میں یہ صریح لفظ ہے اس میں چاروں ائمہ کے درمیان کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of the sick person's divorce. Commentary: Without any detail, and existence of 'iddah is necessary. Because the meaning of raj'ah is to retain the ownership of marriage. Do you not see that it has been named imsak, and imsak means to keep, and to keep (ownership) continuously is only possible during 'iddah, because after 'iddah passes, ownership of marriage no longer remains. Explanation of the case: When a man gives one revocable divorce or two divorces to his wife who has been consummated, he has the option to return to her during her 'iddah, whether the wife is pleased or not. Proof: The saying of Allah the Exalted: 'So when they have [almost] reached their term, hold them back with kindness or part with them with kindness.' That is, when the 'iddah of women is about to end, you have the choice: if you want to choose raj'ah, then hold them back without causing harm, and if you intend separation, then part with them without harm. In this verse, raj'ah is mentioned absolutely; there is no detail of the wife's pleasure or displeasure. Therefore, the ruling of raj'ah is considered absolute. Second proof: The narration from Abu Dawood from 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet divorced Hafsa (may Allah be pleased with her) and then took her back. And in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar that he (peace be upon him) said to him: 'Order your son to take his wife back' (agreed upon). And for raj'ah, the existence of 'iddah is necessary. The proof is that raj'ah is the name of retaining the ownership of marriage. So you see that in the Noble Quran, raj'ah is called imsak, and imsak means to keep, and keeping the ownership of marriage continuously is possible during 'iddah, because after 'iddah passes, ownership of marriage does not remain. So when the 'iddah is complete, the place for imsak no longer exists. Verbal and actual raj'ah. And raj'ah is that he says: 'I take you back' or 'I take back my wife.' This is explicit for raj'ah, and there is no dispute among the Imams. Translation: And raj'ah is that addressing the woman he says: 'I have taken you back,' or in front of people he says: 'I have taken back my wife.' And in the matter of raj'ah, this is an explicit word, and there is no disagreement among the four Imams.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a ruling with proof, explaining the definition and conditions of raj'ah (revocation of divorce). The author first establishes that raj'ah requires the presence of 'iddah, because the essence of raj'ah is retaining the marital bond, which only exists during 'iddah. This is supported by the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:231) which uses the word 'imsak' (holding back) – indicating continuity. The verse gives the husband the right to take his wife back without her consent, as the command is absolute. Two hadiths are cited: one about the Prophet taking back Hafsa, and another from Ibn 'Umar. Then the verbal form of raj'ah is explained: saying 'I take you back' or 'I take back my wife' is explicit (‘sarih’) and unanimously accepted by all four imams. The commentary notes that even if the wife is not present, informing her suffices. The key point: no witness is required; the purpose of witnesses is only for proof if the wife denies.

Key Terms
رجعت (raj'ah): Revocation of divorce; the husband's right to take back his wife during her 'iddah without a new contract.
امساک (imsāk): Holding back; keeping the wife in marriage with kindness, as mentioned in Quran for raj'ah.
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period after divorce during which the wife cannot remarry; required for raj'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for the validity of verbal raj'ah regarding witnesses?
A) Witnesses are required for validity.
B) Witnesses are not required for validity, but helpful for proof.
C) Witnesses are required only if the wife disputes.
D) Witnesses are required for both verbal and physical raj'ah.

Key Takeaway
Raj'ah is the husband's unilateral right to maintain the marriage during 'iddah by explicit verbal declaration, without needing the wife's consent or witnesses for validity.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
8 min
Verbal Raj'ah: Explicit Formula and Consensus
States the explicit verbal formula and its unanimous acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the explicit verbal formula for raj'ah and explain why witnesses are not a condition for validity.

Core Idea
Raj'ah is explicit by saying 'I take you back' – a consensus of the four Imams.

While the Hanafi school accepts physical acts as implicit raj'ah, the explicit verbal declaration is universally accepted. This lesson covers the precise wording, absence of condition of witnesses, and the practical benefit of having witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the explicit formula
The text gives two forms: addressing the wife directly (راجعتك) or addressing witnesses (راجعت امرأتي). These are considered explicit (sarih) for raj'ah.
The formula must clearly indicate the intention to resume the marriage.
2
Note the consensus
The passage states that there is no dispute among the four Imams on this explicit verbal form. This is a rare point of agreement in fiqh al-talaq.
Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad all agree.
3
Understand the role of witnesses
Witnesses are not a condition (shart) for the validity of raj'ah. Their benefit is evidentiary: if the wife denies raj'ah, the husband can prove it through witnesses.
This is a practical advantage, not a legal requirement.
4
Contrast with physical acts
The explicit verbal form is straightforward, whereas physical acts are subject to ikhtilaf. Recognizing this contrast sets up the next lesson.
The physical acts are discussed in the following lesson.

Or he performs intercourse with her, or kisses her, or touches her with desire, or looks at her private part with desire. This is the ruling according to us. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: If he is able to speak, raj'ah cannot occur without verbal expression. Because [page 36] Ashraf al-Hidayah, commentary Urdo Hidayah, volume five: [Shafi'i held that] raj'ah is in the position of initiating marriage, such that intercourse with her is forbidden. And according to us, raj'ah means continuing the marital bond, as we have explained before and will further explain, Allah willing. And sometimes an act serves as evidence for continuity, as in the cancellation of an option. And the act being evidence for raj'ah is from an act that is specific to marriage. And the acts just mentioned are specific to marriage, especially regarding a free woman. Contrary to touching and looking at the private part without desire, because those may be permissible without marriage, like for a midwife and doctor. And looking at other than the private part sometimes occurs among housemates, and the husband lives with her during 'iddah. So if looking without desire from elsewhere also constituted raj'ah, then he could divorce her again and thus the 'iddah upon her would become very long. Commentary: And raj'ah is that addressing his wife he says: 'I take you back' or addressing witnesses he says: 'I take back my wife' – even if the wife is not present, he can inform her. And this is explicit in raj'ah, and there is no dispute among the four Imams regarding this issue. Benefit: The correct view is that no one considers witnesses as a condition; rather the benefit of having witnesses is that if the wife claims he did not take her back, the man can prove it through witnesses. In short, this verbal form is explicit without dispute. It is said: And he performs intercourse with her, or kisses her, or touches her with desire, or looks at her private part with desire – this is according to us. [Commentary]: The practical form of raj'ah is that he performs intercourse with that woman, or kisses her, or touches that woman with desire, or looks at her private part with desire, i.e., the inner round part. And Menti [possibly a scholar] also restricted kissing with desire. In Mabsoot, Dhakhirah, and Khulasah, this restriction is stated explicitly. The verifying scholar (Shaykh Muhaqqiq) said that an act can also be evidence for raj'ah, but only from acts that are specific to marriage. This evidence indicates that kissing should not be restricted to with desire, as apparent from the book's text, because kissing in absolute terms is something whose ruling is specific to marriage. Unlike touching and looking, which are not specific to marriage unless done with desire. And looking towards the anus does not effect raj'ah according to Imam Muhammad and the analogy of Imam Abu Hanifa. And it should also be known that kissing, touching, and looking at the private part, whether done by the man or the woman, effect raj'ah without any difference, provided that when the woman looks, the man knows and does not forbid her but remains silent. In that case, there is agreement. As in Khulasah and others. And if it is from the woman's side, e.g., she kissed the man while he was sleeping, or touched him with desire, or looked at him with desire, or even while awake she suddenly kissed him with desire by force, then Shaykh al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma have mentioned that according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, raj'ah is established. But Imam Abu Yusuf differs in this. And if the man... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the status of physical acts in effecting raj'ah. The Hanafi position is clearly stated: intercourse, kissing, touching with desire, and looking at the private part with desire all constitute raj'ah. This is based on the view that raj'ah is a continuation of marriage, not a new contract. The Shafi'i school disagrees, holding that since raj'ah is like a new marriage, words are required. The Hanafi response uses an analogy with the cancellation of an option (isqat al-khiyar), where an act (like taking possession) indicates continuation of the contract. The commentary then refines: for a free woman, these acts are specifically marital; for a slave woman, different rules apply. Touch and gaze without desire do not effect raj'ah because they may be permissible outside marriage. The discussion also covers the condition of desire: kissing is absolutely specific to marriage, so no condition of desire is attached, but for touch and gaze, desire is necessary. Looking at the anus does not count. The later part explains that acts by the wife can also effect raj'ah if the husband is aware and does not object, with a disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the wife acting while the husband is unaware.

Key Terms
رجعت صریح (raj'ah sarih): Explicit verbal declaration of taking back one's wife during 'iddah.
گواہ (gawah): Witnesses; not a condition for validity but beneficial for proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the agreed-upon position regarding witnesses in verbal raj'ah?
A) Witnesses are a condition for validity.
B) Witnesses are recommended but not required.
C) Witnesses are only needed if the wife denies.
D) Witnesses are prohibited.

Key Takeaway
The explicit verbal formula ('I take you back') is valid and unanimously accepted; witnesses are not required.

Physical Acts as Raj'ah: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains which physical acts effect raj'ah and the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which physical acts effect raj'ah, the condition of desire, and the Shafi'i objection with Hanafi response.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, physical acts specific to marriage (intercourse, kissing, touching with desire, gazing at private part) effect raj'ah without verbal declaration.

The Hanafi school holds that certain physical acts, because they are inherently specific to marriage, serve as evidence of continuing the marital bond. This lesson examines the four listed acts, the condition of desire, and the Shafi'i insistence that words are necessary. We also explore the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on acts done by the wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four acts
The text lists intercourse, kissing, touching with desire, and looking at the private part with desire. These are the only physical acts that effect raj'ah.
Kissing is considered inherently specific to marriage, so desire is not required for it.
2
Understand the condition of desire
For touching and gazing, desire (shahwah) is necessary because without it, these acts are not exclusive to marriage. Kissing, however, is specific even without desire.
Looking at the anus does not effect raj'ah according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi reasoning uses qiyas jaliy: raj'ah is continuation, like holding an option (khiyar). An act can indicate continuation, just as taking possession restores ownership in khiyar.
The acts are specific to marriage, so they naturally indicate resumption.
4
Examine the Shafi'i objection
Imam Shafi'i argues that raj'ah is like initiating marriage, so it requires explicit words. Intercourse before verbal raj'ah is forbidden.
The key difference is whether raj'ah is seen as continuation (Hanafi) or new initiation (Shafi'i).
5
Consider the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
If the wife performs the act (e.g., kisses him) while he is unaware or asleep, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say raj'ah occurs; Abu Yusuf disagrees.
When the husband is aware and does not object, there is agreement.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم رجعت ابتدائی نکاح کرنے کے حکم میں ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس عورت سے ہمبستری کرنا بھی حرام ہے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک رجعت کے معنی ہیں۔ نکاح کے تعلق کو برابر باقی رکھنا۔ جیسا کہ اس سے پہلے بھی ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ اور آئندہ بھی انشاء اللہ ہم اسے مزید بیان کریں گے۔ اور فعل کبھی برابر باقی رکھنے پر دلیل واقع ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے اختیار کو ساقط کرنے میں ہوتا ہے۔ اور فعل کا رجعت کے لئے دلیل ہونا ایسے فعل سے ہوتا ہے جو کہ نکاح کے ساتھ مخصوص ہو۔ اور ابھی بیان کئے گئے افعال نکاح کے ساتھ مخصوص ہیں۔ خاص کر آزاد کورت کے بارے میں ۔ بخلاف ہاتھ لگانے اور بغیر شہوت کے شرم گاہ کی طرف دیکھنے کے۔ کیونکہ یہ تو کبھی بغیر نکاح بھی جائز ہو جاتے ہیں جیسے دایہ اور حکیم معالج وغیرہ کو حلال ہوتے ہیں۔ اور شرمگاہ کے سوا دوسرے اعضاء کو دیکھنا تو کبھی ایک جگہ رہنے والوں میں بھی ہو جایا کرتا ہے۔ اور شوہر بھی عدت کے دنوں میں اس کے ساتھ رہتا ہے۔ پس اگر بغیر شہوت اور کہیں سے دیکھنا بھی رجعت ہو جائے پھر اس کو طلاق اور کہیں۔ دے گا تو اس طرح عورت کے حق میں عدت بہت طویل ہو جائے گی۔ تشريح والرجعة ان يقول راجعتك او راجعت امرأتي وهذا صريح في الرجعة ولا خلاف بين الائمة ..... الخ رجعت یہ ہے کہ اپنی عورت کو خطاب کرتے ہوئے یہ کہے کہ میں نے تم سے رجعت کر لی۔ یا گواہوں کو مخاطب کرتے ہوئے یہ کہے کہ میں نے اپنی بیوی سے رجعت کر لی۔ف۔ خواہ وہ عورت خود اس وقت موجود ہو یا کسی طرح اسے خبر کر دے۔
وهذا صريح ... الخ اور یہ طریقہ رجعت میں صریح ہوتا ہے۔ اور چاروں اماموں میں اس مسئلہ میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ فائدہ اور قول صحیح یہ ہے کہ کسی کے نزدیک گواہ شرط نہیں ہے البتہ گواہ کے ہونے کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت نے یہ دعوی کیا کہ اس نے مجھ سے رجعت نہیں کی تو وہ مرد گواہوں سے اسے ثابت کر سکے گا۔ الحاصل یہ قول رجعت بلا اختلاف صریح ہے۔ قالا ويطأها او يقبلها اويلمسها بشهوة او ينظر الى فرجها بشهوة وهذا عندنا ... الخ رجعت کی عملی صورت یہ ہے کہ اس عورت سے وطی کرلے یا اس کا بوسہ لے۔ یا اس عورت کو شہوت کے ساتھ ہاتھ لگائے ، یعنی چھودے۔ یا شہوت کے ساتھ اس کی شرم گاہ کو دیکھے، یعنی اندر کی گول جگہ کو۔ اور مینٹی نے بوسہ لینے کے ساتھ بھی شہوت کی قید لگائی ہے۔ مبسوط وذخیرہ اور خلاصہ میں تو اس قید کو صراحت کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے۔ شیخ محقق نے کہا ہے کہ فعل بھی رجعت کرنے کی دلیل ہے مگر ایسے افعال سے ہوگی جو نکاح کے ساتھ مخصوص ہیں۔ اس میں یہ دلیل مفید ہے کہ بوسہ میں شہوت کی قید نہیں ہونی چاہئے۔ جیسا کہ کتاب کی عبارت سے ظاہر ہے۔ کیونکہ بوسہ مطلقا ایسی چیز ہے جس کا حکم نکاح کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ بخلاف چھونے اور دیکھنے کے کہ یہ کام نکاح کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہیں البتہ اسی صورت میں جبکہ شہوت کے ساتھ ہوں اور مقعد ( پاخانہ کے مقام ) کی طرف نظر کرنے سے امام محمد اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے قیاس کے مطابق رجعت نہیں ہوتی ہے اور یہ بھی معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ بوسہ اور ہاتھ لگانا اور فرج کی طرف دیکھنا خواہ مرد کی طرف سے ہو یا عورت کی طرف سے ہو کسی فرق کے بغیر ہر ایک سے رجعت ثابت ہو جاتی ہے۔ بشرطیکہ عورت کی طرف سے نظر کرنے کی مرد کو بھی خبر ہو اور وہ اسے منع نہ کرے خاموش رہ جائے ۔ پس اس صورت میں اتفاق ہے۔ جیسا کہ خلاصہ وغیرہ میں اس کی تصریح کردی ہے۔ اور اگر عورت کی طرف سے اس طرح ہو کہ مثلاً اس نے مرد کے سوتے ہوئے اس کا بوسہ لے لیا۔ یا شہوت کے ساتھ مرد کو ہاتھ لگایا یا اس کی طرف دیکھا۔ یا جاگنے کی حالت میں بھی اچانک شہوت کے ساتھ بوسہ لے لیا از بردستی ایسا کیا تو شیخ الا سلام اور شمس الائمہ نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ و امام محمد کے نزدیک رجعت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن امام ابو یوسف کا اس میں اختلاف ہے۔ اور اگر مرد کے
Or he performs intercourse with her, or kisses her, or touches her with desire, or looks at her private part with desire. This is the ruling according to us. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: If he is able to speak, raj'ah cannot occur without verbal expression. Because [page 36] Ashraf al-Hidayah, commentary Urdo Hidayah, volume five: [Shafi'i held that] raj'ah is in the position of initiating marriage, such that intercourse with her is forbidden. And according to us, raj'ah means continuing the marital bond, as we have explained before and will further explain, Allah willing. And sometimes an act serves as evidence for continuity, as in the cancellation of an option. And the act being evidence for raj'ah is from an act that is specific to marriage. And the acts just mentioned are specific to marriage, especially regarding a free woman. Contrary to touching and looking at the private part without desire, because those may be permissible without marriage, like for a midwife and doctor. And looking at other than the private part sometimes occurs among housemates, and the husband lives with her during 'iddah. So if looking without desire from elsewhere also constituted raj'ah, then he could divorce her again and thus the 'iddah upon her would become very long. Commentary: And raj'ah is that addressing his wife he says: 'I take you back' or addressing witnesses he says: 'I take back my wife' – even if the wife is not present, he can inform her. And this is explicit in raj'ah, and there is no dispute among the four Imams regarding this issue. Benefit: The correct view is that no one considers witnesses as a condition; rather the benefit of having witnesses is that if the wife claims he did not take her back, the man can prove it through witnesses. In short, this verbal form is explicit without dispute. It is said: And he performs intercourse with her, or kisses her, or touches her with desire, or looks at her private part with desire – this is according to us. [Commentary]: The practical form of raj'ah is that he performs intercourse with that woman, or kisses her, or touches that woman with desire, or looks at her private part with desire, i.e., the inner round part. And Menti [possibly a scholar] also restricted kissing with desire. In Mabsoot, Dhakhirah, and Khulasah, this restriction is stated explicitly. The verifying scholar (Shaykh Muhaqqiq) said that an act can also be evidence for raj'ah, but only from acts that are specific to marriage. This evidence indicates that kissing should not be restricted to with desire, as apparent from the book's text, because kissing in absolute terms is something whose ruling is specific to marriage. Unlike touching and looking, which are not specific to marriage unless done with desire. And looking towards the anus does not effect raj'ah according to Imam Muhammad and the analogy of Imam Abu Hanifa. And it should also be known that kissing, touching, and looking at the private part, whether done by the man or the woman, effect raj'ah without any difference, provided that when the woman looks, the man knows and does not forbid her but remains silent. In that case, there is agreement. As in Khulasah and others. And if it is from the woman's side, e.g., she kissed the man while he was sleeping, or touched him with desire, or looked at him with desire, or even while awake she suddenly kissed him with desire by force, then Shaykh al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma have mentioned that according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, raj'ah is established. But Imam Abu Yusuf differs in this. And if the man... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the status of physical acts in effecting raj'ah. The Hanafi position is clearly stated: intercourse, kissing, touching with desire, and looking at the private part with desire all constitute raj'ah. This is based on the view that raj'ah is a continuation of marriage, not a new contract. The Shafi'i school disagrees, holding that since raj'ah is like a new marriage, words are required. The Hanafi response uses an analogy with the cancellation of an option (isqat al-khiyar), where an act (like taking possession) indicates continuation of the contract. The commentary then refines: for a free woman, these acts are specifically marital; for a slave woman, different rules apply. Touch and gaze without desire do not effect raj'ah because they may be permissible outside marriage. The discussion also covers the condition of desire: kissing is absolutely specific to marriage, so no condition of desire is attached, but for touch and gaze, desire is necessary. Looking at the anus does not count. The later part explains that acts by the wife can also effect raj'ah if the husband is aware and does not object, with a disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the wife acting while the husband is unaware.

Key Terms
وطی (wat'): Sexual intercourse; one of the physical acts that effects raj'ah according to Hanafi.
شہوت (shahwah): Desire; condition for touch and gaze to effect raj'ah; not required for kiss.
فرج (farj): Private part; looking at it with desire effects raj'ah; looking without desire does not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does kissing effect raj'ah even without desire, unlike touching?
A) Because kissing is always done with desire in practice.
B) Because kissing is inherently specific to marriage, while touching can occur in non-marital contexts.
C) Because the Hanafi school considers kissing as equivalent to intercourse.
D) Because the Shafi'i school also agrees on kissing.

Key Takeaway
Four physical acts effect raj'ah: intercourse, kissing, touching with desire, and gazing at the private part with desire; kissing is unique in not requiring desire.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Raj'ah by Action: The Hanafi–Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on the validity of action-based raj'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that raj'ah can be established by actions with desire, distinguish the Shafi'i counterview, and explain the practical consequence of the difference.

Core Idea
Raj'ah is continuation of marriage, so actions proving continuation are valid evidence.

This passage addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can a revocable divorce (raj'ah) be effected by actions such as intercourse, without any words? The Hanafi school says yes, because raj'ah is a continuation of the existing marriage, not a new contract. The Shafi'i school requires a verbal statement. Understanding this difference is crucial for correctly applying the rules of 'iddah and remarriage.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the central claim: raj'ah is valid through actions like intercourse, looking with desire, and touching with desire, provided they are exclusive to marriage.
The passage begins by confirming this with examples and a consensus note.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i, Abu Thawr, and the Zahiris hold that raj'ah must be by verbal statement if the husband can speak.
They analogize raj'ah to a new marriage contract.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i reasoning: raj'ah is like initiating a marriage; intercourse is forbidden until raj'ah is performed; therefore, words are needed.
This is summarized in the text as 'lā taṣiḥḥu illā bil qawl'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafi refutation uses the definition of raj'ah as istidāma (continuation) and the analogy of cancelling an option in sales—actions can indicate finality.
Also, a believer would not commit the forbidden act of intercourse without intending continuation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical consequence: a Hanafi husband who has intercourse during 'iddah has performed raj'ah automatically; a Shafi'i husband must speak.
This affects cases like the mute, the unconscious, or the unwilling husband.

باب طلاق المريض

سوتے ہوئے یا زبردستی عورت نے اس کے آلہ تناسل کو اپنی شرم گاہ میں داخل کر لیا تو بالتفاق رجعت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ پھر یہ جاننا چاہئے کہ اگر شہوت کے ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں دونوں میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو چونکہ یہ شہوت ایک مخفی کیفیت ہے اس لئے اس پر گواہ قبول نہیں کئے جائیں گے۔ جیسا کہ خلاصہ میں ہے۔ لیکن اگر شہوت ہونے کا کسی کے سامنے اقرار کیا ہو اور اس کے گواہ موجود ہوں تو ان کی گواہی مقبول ہو گی ۔ فاحفظہ ۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ان تمام کاموں سے رجعت ہو جاتی ہے۔ وطی عندنا یہ حکم ہمارے نزدیک ہے۔ وقال الشافعي لاتصح الرجعة الا بالقول مع القدرة عليه لان الرجعة بمنزلة ابتداء ... الخ اور امام شافعی نے کہا ہے کہ اگر مرد زبان سے کہہ سکتا ہو تو بغیر کہے ہوئے کسی حرکت سے رجعت صحیح نہیں ہوگی ۔ ف۔ اسی لئے گونگے کی رجعت جو اشارہ سے ہی ہوتی ہے وہ صحیح ہوتی ہے۔ لان الرجعة الخ کیونکہ رجعت کرنا تو بالکل نئے نکاح کرنے کے حکم میں ہے اس لئے اس سے پہلے وطی کرنا حرام ہے۔ جب تک کہ رجعت نہ کر لے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ مومن تو حرام کام نہیں کرتا ہے اس لئے وہ وطی کیوں کرتا۔ جب کہ رجعت کر کے اسے حلال کر سکتا ہے۔ اسی لئے وطی رجعت کی دلیل ہوئی۔ اور رجعت نیا نکاح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ نکاح میں شہادت کا ہونا شرط ہے جبکہ اس کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح اس میں نیا مبر لازم نہیں آتا ہے۔ بس وطی کا حرام ہونا تو طلاق کی وجہ سے ہے اس وقت تک کے لئے کہ اس سے رجعت کا پورا ارادہ نہ کر لیا ہو۔
وعندنا هو استدامة النكاح على مابيناه وسنقرره ان شاء الله تعالى ... الخ اور ہمارے نزدیک رجعت کے معنی ہیں نکاح پہلے کی طرح باقی رکھنا۔ جیسا کہ ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ اور بعد میں بھی انشاء اللہ ہم اس کی وضاحت کرینگے ۔ف۔ اور شافعی کے قول کی موافقت ابو ثور اور ظاہریہ نے کی ہے۔ جبکہ ہمارا مذہب حضرت سعید بن المسیب و حسن بصری و ابن سیریں وغیرھم تابعین و اوزاعی و ثوری و غیرھم فقہاء کی جماعت کا قول ہے۔ ابن المنذر نے یہ بات بیان کی ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ اگر یوں کہا کہ تم میری بی بی جیسی تھی ویسی ہو۔ یا تم میری عورت ہو اگر اس کہنے سے رجعت کرنے سے کنایہ کیا ہو تو کنائی رجعت ہے۔ (الذخیرہ) اور امام مالک اور الحلق نے کہا ہے کہ اگر وطی کرنے سے رجعت کرنے کا ارادہ ہو تب رجعت ہوگی۔
والفعل قديقع دلالة على الاستدامة كما فى اسقاط الخيار والدلالة فعل يخص بالنكاح.. الخ اور انسان کا کوئی کام کبھی ہمیشہ باقی رکھنے پر دلیل ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ خیار ساقط کرنے میں ہے۔ مثلا کسی نے ایک گھوڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ مجھے تین دنوں تک اس کے واپس کرنے کا اختیار رہے گا۔ پھر اس پر سوار ہو کر اپنے کام میں چلا گیا تو اس کا اس طرح لے جانا اس اختیار کو ساقط کرنے کی دلیل ہوگی۔ اور وہ بیع ہمیشہ کیلئے لازم ہو جائے گی ۔ یا ایک باندی اس شرط پر فروخت کی کہ مجھے تین دن تک اس بات کا اختیار ہوگا کہ اسے فروخت نہ کروں۔ اس کے بعد اسی عرصہ میں اس نے اس باندی سے صحبت کر لی تو وہ بیع ختم ہوگئی۔ اور اصلی حالت واپس آگئی ۔ پس یہ بات صاف ظاہر ہوئی کہ جب رجعت کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ ملک نکاح کی موجودہ حالت کو پہلے کی طرح باقی رکھنا ہے۔ اور ہم نے یہ دیکھ لیا کہ شریعت نے بھی ان کاموں کو اس معنی کی دلیل رکھا ہے تو اس سے یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ ان افعال سے رجعت صحیح ہے۔ والدلالة ... الخ اور فعل وعمل سے رجعت کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے یہ ضروری ہے کہ وہ فعل ایسا ہی ہو جو نکاح کے ساتھ یا میاں بیوی کے درمیان مخصوص ہوتا ہے۔ فائدہ یعنی ہر فعل رجعت کی دلیل نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ بلکہ وہی فعل دلیل ہو گا جو خاص نکاح کے بعد ہی جائز ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس طرح یہ دلیل ہوئی کہ اس شخص نے اپنے نکاحی پرانے تعلق کو باقی رکھ لیا ہے۔ اس کو رجعت کہتے ہیں۔
وهذه الافاعيل تخص به خصوصا في حق الحرة بخلاف المس والنظر بغير شهوة ... الخ اور یہ مذکورہ افعال یعنی شہوت کے ساتھ شرم گاہ کے اندرونی حصہ کو دیکھنا، عورت کو ہاتھ لگانا اور بوس و کنار سب ایسے افعال ہیں کہ نکاح کے بعد ہی جائز ہوتے ہیں۔ اور نکاح کے ساتھ مخصوص ہیں۔ یعنی صرف نکاح سے ہی یہ سب کام جائز ہوتے ہیں بشرطیکہ شہوت کے ساتھ ہوں ۔ خصوصاً ... الخ خاص کر آزاد عورت کے حق میں ۔ ف۔ کہ وہ تو بغیر نکاح کسی طرح بھی حلال نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ بخلاف باندی کے کہ وہ کبھی مملوکہ ہونے کی وجہ سے حلال ہو جاتی ہے۔ لیکن یہ معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ وہ ملک حلال ہونے پر دلیل ضرور ہیں تو وہ آزاد یا منکوحہ یا باندی میں دلیل ملک نکاح میں اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ شہوت کے ساتھ ہوں ۔
بخلاف المس بغير شهوة والنظر بغير شهوة إلى غير الفرج فان ذلك قد يقع بدون النكاح۔ لانہ قدالخ کیونکہ شہوت کے بغیر چھونا اور دیکھنا کبھی بغیر نکاح کے بھی جائز ہو جاتا ہے جیسے کہ دائی جنائی کو اور علاج کرنے والے حکیم کو ۔ اور کچھ دوسروں کو ۔ف۔ جیسے سفر کی حالت میں عورت کو جانور پر سوار کرنا اور زنا کے گواہ کو۔
خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ہم نے ان کاموں کے ساتھ شہوت کی قید اس وجہ سے لگائی ہے کہ بغیر شہوت کے چھونا اور شرم گاہ کو دیکھنا طبیب وغیرہ کے لئے جائز ہے۔ لیکن شہوت کے ساتھ اسی وقت جائز ہوگا جبکہ نکاح ہو چکا ہو۔ نیز دیکھنے سے فرج کا اندرونی حصہ مراد ہے اور اوپر کا حصہ نہیں۔ والنظرالى غير الفرج قديقع بين المساكنين والزوج يساكنها في العدة .... الخ اور فرج کے سواء بدن کے دوسرے حصہ کو دیکھنا اکثر ایک ساتھ رہنے والوں میں ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور عدت کی حالت میں شوہر بھی اس کے ساتھ رہتا ہے ۔ فلوكان الخ پس اگر شہوت کے بغیر بھی دوسری جگہوں کے دیکھنے سے بھی رجعت ثابت ہو جائے گی تو اس کا شوہر خاص کر پھر طلاق دے گا۔ کیونکہ اس کا پختہ ارادہ اس کو علیحدہ کر دینے کا ہو چکا ہے۔ جبکہ یہ رجعت تو غیر اختیاری طور پر ہو گئی ہے اس لئے پھر طلاق دے گا۔ فيطول العدة ... الخ اس طرح اس عورت کی عدت بڑھتی جائے گی۔ حالانکہ اللہ تعالی نے اس سے منع فرمایا ہے اور معروف طریقہ سے رخصت کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہوت کے بغیر اور شرم گاہ کے علاوہ دوسرے اعضاء کو چھونے اور دیکھنے سے رجعت نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ شیخ محقق نے لکھا ہے کہ اگر عورت کی مقعد کو دیکھا تو رجعت نہیں ہوگی ۔ زیادات میں اس مسئلہ کو صراحت کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے۔ اور اگر اس مقعد میں وطی کر لی تو قدوری نے اشارہ کیا ہے کہ رجعت نہیں ہوگی۔ لیکن رجعت ہونے پر ہی فتوی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس حرکت میں شہوت کے ساتھ ہاتھ لگانے کے علاوہ کچھ اور بھی پایا جاتا ہے۔ اور دیوانہ کی رجعت فعل سے ہی ہوتی ہے اس کے زبان سے کہنے کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اگر شوہر نے خلوت کے بعد طلاق دی اور کہا کہ میں اس سے صحبت کر چکا ہوں لیکن عورت نے انکار کیا تو شوہر کو اس سے رجعت کا اختیار ہوگا۔ اور بغیر صحبت کے نہیں ہوگا۔ رجعت کو کسی شرط پر معلق کرنا مثلاً فلاں شخص آئے تو میں نے رجعت کی یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح آنے والے زمانہ کی طرف اضافت کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of the Sick Person's Divorce. ... If the woman inserts his organ into her private part while he is sleeping or by force, then by consensus raj'ah is established. Then it should be known that if there is disagreement about the presence or absence of desire, since desire is a hidden quality, witnesses are not accepted regarding it. As in al-Khulasa. But if he has admitted to desire in front of someone and there are witnesses, their testimony is accepted. So remember. Summary: raj'ah occurs through all these acts. Intercourse according to us: This is our ruling. Imam al-Shafi'i said: Raj'ah is not valid except by speech when he is able to do so, because raj'ah is like initiating marriage. ... And Imam al-Shafi'i said: If a man can speak verbally, then without saying anything, raj'ah through any action is not valid. Therefore, the raj'ah of a mute, which occurs by gesture, is valid. Because raj'ah is like a new marriage, so before it, intercourse with her is forbidden until he performs raj'ah. The answer is that a believer does not commit a forbidden act, so why would he engage in intercourse when he can make it permissible by doing raj'ah? For this reason, intercourse became evidence of raj'ah. And raj'ah is not a new marriage, because for marriage the presence of witnesses is a condition, while for this it is not a condition. Similarly, a new dower is not obligatory. Rather, the prohibition of intercourse is due to divorce, for the time being, until he completes the intention of raj'ah by it. In our view, it is the continuation of marriage as we have explained and will establish, God willing. And in our view, the meaning of raj'ah is to keep the marriage as before, as we have stated earlier and will clarify later, God willing. Abu Thawr and the Zahiris agreed with al-Shafi'i. While our madhhab is the opinion of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, Hasan al-Basri, Ibn Sirin and other Tabi'un, al-Awza'i, al-Thawri and a group of jurists. Ibn al-Mundhir narrated this. It is clear that if he says, 'You are as you were like my wife' or 'You are my wife,' if by this saying he intended raj'ah, it is a kinayah raj'ah (al-Dhakhira). Imam Malik and al-Halaq said that if he intends raj'ah by intercourse, then raj'ah occurs. An action sometimes indicates continuation, as in the cancellation of an option. For example, someone bought a horse on condition that he has the option to return it for three days. Then he rode it and went about his business; his taking it thus is evidence of cancelling the option, and the sale becomes binding permanently. Or, a slave girl was sold on condition that he has the option not to sell her for three days; then during that period he had intercourse with her, the sale is cancelled and the original state returns. So it becomes clear that since the meaning of raj'ah is to keep the existing state of the marriage bond as before, and we have seen that Shari'ah has made these actions evidence of this meaning, it is established that raj'ah is valid through these actions. And for the validity of raj'ah by action, it is necessary that the action be specific to marriage or between husband and wife. Benefit: Not every action is evidence of raj'ah; only that action which becomes permissible only after marriage. Thus, it is evidence that this person has continued his old marital relationship. This is called raj'ah. These actions are specific to it, especially in the case of a free woman, as opposed to touching and looking without desire. These mentioned actions—looking at the inner part of the private part with desire, touching the woman and kissing—are all actions that are permissible only after marriage. They are specific to marriage, i.e., these actions are permissible only through marriage, provided they are with desire. Especially in the case of a free woman, because she can be permissible only through marriage, unlike a slave girl who sometimes becomes permissible due to being owned. But it must be known that these actions are evidence of permissible ownership, whether in a free woman, married woman, or slave girl, with the condition that they are with desire. As opposed to touching without desire and looking at other than the private part without desire, because that sometimes occurs without marriage. For example, a midwife looking at a woman giving birth, and a physician treating her, and some others, such as helping a woman onto an animal in travel, and witnesses of adultery. Summary: We have imposed the condition of desire for these actions because touching without desire and looking at the private part is permissible for a physician, etc. But with desire, it is only permissible when there is marriage. Also, looking means the inner part of the private part, not the outer part. Looking at other than the private part often occurs among co-residents, and the husband lives with her during the 'iddah. So if looking at other parts without desire also established raj'ah, then the husband would specifically divorce her again, because his firm intention to separate her has been made, and this raj'ah has occurred involuntarily. Thus he would divorce again, lengthening the 'iddah. This would be contrary to Allah's prohibition and command to let her go in a proper manner. From this it is known that touching and looking at other than the private part without desire does not establish raj'ah. The verifying shaykh wrote: If he looked at the woman's anus, raj'ah does not occur. In al-Ziyadat, this issue is explicitly stated. And if he performed intercourse in the anus, al-Quduri indicated that raj'ah does not occur, but the fatwa is that it does occur because in that act there is something besides touching with desire. The raj'ah of an insane person occurs through action; his speech is not considered. If the husband divorced after seclusion and said he has had intercourse with her but the wife denied it, the husband has the option of raj'ah. And without intercourse, it will not occur. Suspending raj'ah on a condition, e.g., 'When so-and-so comes, I have performed raj'ah' is not valid. Similarly, adding it to a future time is also not valid.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah deals with the specific issue of how revocable divorce (raj'ah) is effected. The author begins by stating the ruling that if intercourse occurs, even if the wife inserts his organ while he is asleep or by force, raj'ah is established by consensus. Then, the question of desire arises: since desire is internal, witnesses are not accepted to prove it unless there is a prior admission. The core of the passage is the inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school holds that raj'ah can be established through actions, particularly intercourse and other intimate acts with desire. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that raj'ah can only be by verbal statement if the husband is capable of speech. The Hanafi response uses two lines of reasoning: first, the definition of raj'ah as continuation of the marriage (istidāmat al-nikāḥ), not a new marriage, so it is not analogous to initiating a contract. Second, the analogy of cancelling an option (khiyār) in sales: when a buyer uses the purchased item (e.g., rides the horse) during the option period, that action cancels the option, demonstrating that action can imply continuation or finality. Similarly, actions specific to marriage indicate the husband's intent to continue the marriage. The text further clarifies that not every action counts: only those that are exclusive to marriage and performed with desire. Looking or touching without desire, or looking at private parts without desire, does not constitute raj'ah because such actions may be permissible outside marriage (medical necessity, etc.). Specific rulings include: looking at the anus does not effect raj'ah, but intercourse in the anus effects raj'ah according to the fatwa because it involves more than mere touching with desire. The madhhab rejects the validity of conditional or future raj'ah. The passage provides a thorough Hanafi argument supported by analogy and definitional analysis.

Key Terms
رجعت (raj'ah): Revocable divorce: the husband's right to take back his divorced wife during the 'iddah period without a new marriage
وطی (wat'i): Sexual intercourse, the primary action through which raj'ah is established
شہوت (shahwah): Sexual desire; a condition for actions to count as evidence of raj'ah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the valid method of performing raj'ah (revocable divorce) for a husband who can speak?
A) Only by saying 'I have taken you back' or similar explicit words
B) By any action that shows intent, such as having intercourse with desire during the 'iddah
C) By writing a letter or sending a messenger
D) Only by a new marriage contract with new witnesses and dower

Key Takeaway
Raj'ah is a continuation of marriage and can be established by actions specific to marriage and performed with desire, according to the Hanafi school.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Actions Establishing Raj'ah: Conditions of Desire and Private Parts
Explains which physical acts constitute revocable return and the condition of desire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which physical acts during 'iddah constitute raj'ah and identify the conditions of desire (shahwa) and the specific part (inside of farj) required.

Core Idea
Only exclusive acts with desire establish raj'ah; mere touching or looking without desire does not.

The revocable return (raj'ah) after a divorce is not only by words but can also be established by actions. This lesson clarifies which specific physical acts—such as looking at the inside of the private part with desire, touching with desire, and kissing—serve as conclusive evidence that the husband has retained the marital bond. The condition of desire is crucial because it distinguishes permissible acts from those that may be allowed outside marriage for necessity.

Guided Path
1
Understand raj'ah by action
Recognise that raj'ah can be established through specific physical acts that are exclusive to marriage, not only by verbal declaration.
These acts must occur during the 'iddah period after a revocable divorce.
2
Identify the condition of desire (shahwa)
The act must be performed with sexual desire. Without desire, the act might be permissible outside marriage (e.g., medical treatment) and thus does not indicate intent to return.
Desire makes the act exclusive to marriage.
3
Identify the specific private part (farj)
Only the inside of the private part (farj) counts. Looking at or touching the external parts (e.g., thigh, anus) without desire does not establish raj'ah.
The text emphasises the inner part, not the outer.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on anal intercourse
Imam Quduri indicated that anal intercourse does not constitute raj'ah, but the later fatwa is that it does, because it involves more than just touching with desire.
The mufta bihi is that raj'ah occurs.

وهذه الافاعيل تخص به خصوصا في حق الحرة بخلاف المس والنظر بغير شهوة ... الخ اور یہ مذکورہ افعال یعنی شہوت کے ساتھ شرم گاہ کے اندرونی حصہ کو دیکھنا، عورت کو ہاتھ لگانا اور بوس و کنار سب ایسے افعال ہیں کہ نکاح کے بعد ہی جائز ہوتے ہیں۔ اور نکاح کے ساتھ مخصوص ہیں۔ یعنی صرف نکاح سے ہی یہ سب کام جائز ہوتے ہیں بشرطیکہ شہوت کے ساتھ ہوں ۔ خصوصاً ... الخ خاص کر آزاد عورت کے حق میں ۔ ف۔ کہ وہ تو بغیر نکاح کسی طرح بھی حلال نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ بخلاف باندی کے کہ وہ کبھی مملوکہ ہونے کی وجہ سے حلال ہو جاتی ہے۔ لیکن یہ معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ وہ ملک حلال ہونے پر دلیل ضرور ہیں تو وہ آزاد یا منکوحہ یا باندی میں دلیل ملک نکاح میں اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ شہوت کے ساتھ ہوں ۔
بخلاف المسالخ برخلاف شہوت کے بغیر دیکھنے اور چھونے کے۔ لانہ قدالخ کیونکہ شہوت کے بغیر چھونا اور دیکھنا کبھی بغیر نکاح کے بھی جائز ہو جاتا ہے جیسے کہ دائی جنائی کو اور علاج کرنے والے حکیم کو ۔ اور کچھ دوسروں کو ۔ف۔ جیسے سفر کی حالت میں عورت کو جانور پر سوار کرنا اور زنا کے گواہ کو۔
خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ہم نے ان کاموں کے ساتھ شہوت کی قید اس وجہ سے لگائی ہے کہ بغیر شہوت کے چھونا اور شرم گاہ کو دیکھنا طبیب وغیرہ کے لئے جائز ہے۔ لیکن شہوت کے ساتھ اسی وقت جائز ہوگا جبکہ نکاح ہو چکا ہو۔ نیز دیکھنے سے فرج کا اندرونی حصہ مراد ہے اور اوپر کا حصہ نہیں۔ والنظرالى غير الفرج قديقع بين المساكنين والزوج يساكنها في العدة .... الخ اور فرج کے سواء بدن کے دوسرے حصہ کو دیکھنا اکثر ایک ساتھ رہنے والوں میں ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور عدت کی حالت میں شوہر بھی اس کے ساتھ رہتا ہے ۔ فلوكان الخ پس اگر شہوت کے بغیر بھی دوسری جگہوں کے دیکھنے سے بھی رجعت ثابت ہو جائے گی تو اس کا شوہر خاص کر پھر طلاق دے گا۔ کیونکہ اس کا پختہ ارادہ اس کو علیحدہ کر دینے کا ہو چکا ہے۔ جبکہ یہ رجعت تو غیر اختیاری طور پر ہو گئی ہے اس لئے پھر طلاق دے گا۔ فيطول العدة ... الخ اس طرح اس عورت کی عدت بڑھتی جائے گی۔ حالانکہ اللہ تعالی نے اس سے منع فرمایا ہے اور معروف طریقہ سے رخصت کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہوت کے بغیر اور شرم گاہ کے علاوہ دوسرے اعضاء کو چھونے اور دیکھنے سے رجعت نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ شیخ محقق نے لکھا ہے کہ اگر عورت کی مقعد کو دیکھا تو رجعت نہیں ہوگی ۔ زیادات میں اس مسئلہ کو صراحت کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے۔ اور اگر اس مقعد میں وطی کر لی تو قدوری نے اشارہ کیا ہے کہ رجعت نہیں ہوگی۔ لیکن رجعت ہونے پر ہی فتوی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس حرکت میں شہوت کے ساتھ ہاتھ لگانے کے علاوہ کچھ اور بھی پایا جاتا ہے۔ اور دیوانہ کی رجعت فعل سے ہی ہوتی ہے اس کے زبان سے کہنے کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اگر شوہر نے خلوت کے بعد طلاق دی اور کہا کہ میں اس سے صحبت کر چکا ہوں لیکن عورت نے انکار کیا تو شوہر کو اس سے رجعت کا اختیار ہوگا۔ اور بغیر صحبت کے نہیں ہوگا۔ رجعت کو کسی شرط پر معلق کرنا مثلاً فلاں شخص آئے تو میں نے رجعت کی یہ میچ نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح آنے والے زمانہ کی طرف اضافت کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of the Divorce of the Sick Person. The proof is that this person has kept his old marital relationship intact. This is called raj'ah. Such actions are specific to him, especially regarding a free woman, unlike touching and looking without desire... etc. And these mentioned actions, i.e., looking at the inside of the private part with desire, touching the woman, and kissing, are all actions that are only permissible after marriage. And they are specific to marriage, i.e., only from marriage are all these actions permissible, provided they are with desire. Specifically... especially concerning a free woman. For she is not made lawful without marriage in any way. Unlike a slave woman, who sometimes becomes lawful due to being owned. But it should be known that ownership is proof of lawfulness, so the proof of ownership in marriage is with the condition that it is with desire, whether free, married, or slave. Unlike without desire, contrary to looking and touching without desire. Because touching and looking without desire sometimes become permissible without marriage, like a midwife for childbirth and a physician for treatment. And some others, like mounting a woman on an animal during travel and witnesses of fornication. The summary is that we have placed the condition of desire on these actions because touching without desire and looking at the private part are permissible for a physician, etc. But with desire, it is only permissible when marriage has occurred. Also, by looking, the inside of the private part is meant, not the outer part. And looking at other than the private part often occurs among cohabitants, and the husband resides with her during the 'iddah. So if even without desire, looking at other parts could establish raj'ah, then the husband would specifically give divorce again, because his firm intent to separate her has already occurred, while this raj'ah happened involuntarily, so he would divorce again. Thus her 'iddah would be lengthened, although Allah has forbidden this and commanded release in a decent manner. From this it is known that touching and looking at other limbs without desire and besides the private part does not establish raj'ah. The verifying scholar wrote that if he looked at the woman's anus, raj'ah does not occur. In al-Ziyadat, this issue is stated explicitly. And if he had intercourse in the anus, Quduri indicated that raj'ah does not occur. But the fatwa is on the occurrence of raj'ah, because in this act something more than touching with desire is found. The raj'ah of an insane person is only by action, his verbal statement is not considered. If the husband gave divorce after seclusion and said that he had intercourse with her, but the woman denied, the husband will have the option of raj'ah. And without intercourse it will not occur. Suspending raj'ah on a condition, e.g., 'if such a person comes, I have done raj'ah' is not valid. Similarly, adding it to a future time is not valid.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of divorce of the sick person, specifically discussing what actions constitute revocable return (raj'ah). The passage explains that certain physical acts—looking at the inside of the private part with desire, touching a woman with desire, and kissing—are exclusive to marriage and therefore indicate that the husband has retained the marital bond, thus establishing raj'ah. These acts are only permissible after a valid marriage, and their performance with desire during the 'iddah period signifies the husband's intent to take his wife back. The condition of desire (shahwa) is crucial because without it, such acts may be permissible outside marriage (e.g., for medical treatment). The passage emphasizes that the private part (farj) specifically refers to the internal part, not the external. Looking at other body parts without desire does not constitute raj'ah, as such looks commonly occur between cohabitants and would lead to prolonged 'iddah if counted. The passage then addresses a nuance: looking at the anus does not establish raj'ah according to the verifying scholar, but if intercourse occurs in the anus, Imam Quduri indicated no raj'ah, yet the fatwa is that raj'ah does occur because it involves more than just touching with desire. The passage also covers that an insane person's raj'ah is only by action, not speech, and that if a husband claims privacy and intercourse but the woman denies, he still has the option of raj'ah. Finally, it states that suspending raj'ah on a condition or referring it to a future time is invalid.

Key Terms
رجعت (raj'ah): Revocable return to the marital bond during the 'iddah period after a revocable divorce.
شہوت (shahwa): Sexual desire; a condition for acts to constitute raj'ah.
فرج (farj): The private part; specifically, the internal part (inside) for the purpose of raj'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT considered an act that establishes raj'ah according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Looking at the inside of the private part with desire.
B) Touching the woman with desire.
C) Looking at the woman's face with desire.
D) Kissing the woman with desire.

Key Takeaway
Raj'ah by action requires acts exclusive to marriage: performed with desire and involving the internal private part.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Witnesses in Raj'ah: Mustahab or Wajib?
Discusses the differing opinions on whether witnesses are required for a valid raj'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on witnesses in raj'ah and explain the inter-madhhab dispute, including the Quranic evidence and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, witnesses for raj'ah are mustahab, not wajib; the raj'ah is valid without them.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafis and other schools regarding the necessity of witnesses for a valid raj'ah (revocable return after divorce). The Hanafi position, as stated by al-Quduri, is that having two witnesses is mustahab (recommended) but not obligatory. We will explore the opposing view based on Quran 65:2 and the Hanafi response that interprets the command as recommendation rather than obligation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school says about witnesses in raj'ah: mustahab, not wajib, and valid without them.
The matn of al-Quduri explicitly states 'yastahabbu'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (in one qawl) and Imam Malik (according to one narration) hold that witnesses are wajib and raj'ah is invalid without them.
The passage mentions two opposing schools.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Quranic verse 65:2 that they cite: 'And call to witness two just men among you.' Understand their argument that the imperative (ashhidoo) indicates obligation in usul al-fiqh.
The verse is the main dalil.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi counter: (1) texts on raj'ah are absolute and do not restrict to witnesses; (2) raj'ah is a continuation of marriage, and witnesses are not a condition for continuity (like in ila'); (3) the imperative is interpreted as recommendation because it is linked with recommended acts like retaining or separating.
The Hanafi response uses multiple arguments.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical consequence: if witnesses are missed, the raj'ah is valid in the Hanafi school but invalid in the Shafi'i/Maliki view (according to the cited narration).
This difference affects actual marital status.

Source Text
