باب طلاق المريض
ترجمہ اور جب باندی کے شوہر نے اس کی عدت گزر جانے کے بعد کہا میں اس سے ( عدت میں ) رجوع کر چکا تھا اور مولیٰ نے اس کی تصدیق کی اور باندی نے اس کو جھٹلایا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک باندی کا قول ( معتبر ) ہوگا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مولی کاقول ( قبول ) ہوگا۔ کیونکہ باندی کا بضع مولیٰ کا مملوک ہے۔ پس مولی نے شوہر کیلئے ایسی چیز کا اقرار کیا ہے۔ جو خالص مولیٰ کا مملوک ہے۔ پس مشابہ ہو گیا ( مولی کے ) باندی پر نکاح کا اقرار کرنے کے اور امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ رجعت کا حکم عدت پر مبنی ہے اور عدت میں عورت کا قول ( قبول ) ہوتا ہے۔ پس ایسے ہی اس چیز میں جو عدت پر مبنی ہو اور اگر معاملہ برعکس ہو جائے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک مولی کا قول ( معتبر ) ہوگا اور ایسے ہی امام صاحب کے نزدیک صحیح روایت میں۔ کیونکہ باندی فی الحال عدت کو پورا کرنے والی ہے اور مولی کیلئے ملک متعہ ظاہر ہوگئی ہے۔ پس باندی کا قول مولی کے (حق کو باطل کرنے میں قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا بخلاف وجہ اول کے۔ کیونکہ مولی رجعت میں تصدیق کرنے کی وجہ سے رجعت کے وقت وجود عدت کا اقرار کرنے والا ہے اور مولی کی ملک عدت کے ساتھ ظاہر نہیں ہوتی ( پس مولی کا قول معتبر نہیں ہو گا ) اور اگر باندی نے کہا کہ میری عدت گزر گئی ہے اور شوہر اور مولیٰ نے کہا کہ تیری عدت نہیں گذری تو باندی کا قول ( معتبر ) ہوگا۔ کیونکہ باندی اپنے اس قول ( انقضت عدتی) میں امین ہے۔ اس لئے کہ باندی ہی انقضاء عدت کو جاننے والی ہے۔ تشریح . اگر باندی کے شوہر نے اس کی عدت گزرنے کے بعد کہا کہ میں تجھ سے عدت میں مراجعت کر چکا ہوں ۔ تو اس کی چار صورتیں ہیں ۔ (1) مولیٰ اور باندی دونوں اس کی تصدیق کر دیں۔ یا دونوں اس کی تکذیب کر دیں۔ (4) یا مولیٰ تصدیق کرے اور باندی تکذیب کرے۔ بر عکس یعنی مولی تکذیب کرے اور باندی تصدیق کرے۔ صورت اوّل میں بالا تفاق رجعت صحیح ہے اور صورت ثانی میں بالاتفاق رجعت صحیح نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ شوہر بینہ پیش کر دے اور تیسری صورت میں اگر شوہر کے پاس بینہ نہ ہو تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک باندی کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اسی کے قائل امام زفر ، امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مولی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عدت گزر جانے کے بعد منافع بضع مولی کے مملوک ہیں۔ پس شوہر کے لئے منافع بضع کا اقرار خالص اپنے حق کا اقرار کرنا ہے۔ لہذا اس کو رد نہیں کیا جا سکتا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ مولیٰ نے اپنی باندی پر نکاح کا اقرار کیا ہو۔ مثلاً کہا کہ میں نے اپنی باندی کا فلاں سے نکاح کر دیا تو اس اقرار میں مولی کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ پس ایسے ہی یہاں بھی مولیٰ کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رجعت کا حکم بقاء عدت اور انقضاء عدت پر مبنی ہے۔ (یعنی اگر عدت باقی ہے تو رجعت ثابت ہو جائے گی اور اگر عدت گزرگئی تو حکم رجعت ثابت نہیں ہو گا ) اور عدت کی بقاء اور عدم بقاء میں عورت کا قول معتبر ہے۔ پس جو چیز عدت پر مبنی ہوگی یعنی رجعت اس میں بھی عورت ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
اور چوتھی صورت جس کو مصنف ہدایہ نے ولو كان على القلب سے تعبیر فرمایا ہے۔ یعنی باندی نے شوہر کی تصدیق کی اور مولیٰ نے تکذیب کی تو اس صورت میں صاحبین کے نزدیک مولی کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع بضع خالص مولی کا حق ہیں اور شوہر مولی پر ان کا مدعی ہے اور مولیٰ منکر ہے اور چونکہ مفروض یہ ہے کہ مدعی کے پاس بعینہ موجود نہیں لہذا منکر یعنی مولی کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی بھی صحیح روایت یہ ہے کہ مولیٰ کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بالفعل تو یہ باندی ایسی حالت میں ہے کہ ایام عدت گزر چکے ہیں اور مولی کے واسطے اپنی باندی سے تمتع حاصل کرنے کی ملک بظاہر ثابت ہو چکی ۔ پس اگر باندی اور اس کے شوہر کے قول سے رجعت ثابت ہو جائے تو مولیٰ کی ملک تمتع باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ حالانکہ محض کسی کا اقرار حق غیر کو باطل کرنے میں قابل نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا یہاں بھی باندی کا قول مولی کے حق کو باطل کرنے میں قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ برخلاف پہلی صورت کے یعنی وہ صورت جس میں مولیٰ نے شوہر کی تصدیق کی ہے اور باندی نے تکذیب ، تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس صورت میں باندی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مولیٰ نے جب رجعت میں شوہر کی تصدیق کی تو اس سے مولیٰ اس باندی [؟] کا مقر ہو گیا کہ رجعت کے وقت عدت موجود تھی اور عدت کے ہوتے ہوئے مولیٰ کے لئے ملک تمتع حاصل نہیں ہوسکتی۔ پس چونکہ اس صورت میں باندی کا قول قبول کرنے میں مولی سے حق کو باطل کرنا لازم نہیں آتا۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں باندی کا قول معتبر ہو گا نہ کہ مولی کا۔ اور اگر باندی نے کہا کہ میری عدت گزر چکی اور ایام اتنے ہیں کہ عدت گزرنا ناممکن ہے اور شوہر اور مولی نے کہا کہ تیری عدت نہیں گزری تو باندی ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ باندی انقضاء عدت کے سلسلہ میں امین ہے۔ اس لئے کہ باندی ہی عدت کے گزرنے کا علم رکھتی ہے۔ واللہ اعلم۔
Chapter of Talaq of the Sick. Translation: And when the slave woman's husband said after her 'idda had passed, 'I had returned to her (during the 'idda),' and the master confirmed him and the slave woman denied him, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the slave woman's statement (is accepted), and the Sahibayn said that the master's statement (is accepted). Because the slave woman's pudendum is owned by the master. So the master affirmed for the husband something that is purely owned by the master. So it became similar to (the master's) affirmation of marriage upon his slave woman. And Imam Sahib says that the ruling of raj'a is based on the 'idda, and in the 'idda the woman's statement (is accepted). So likewise in this matter which is based on the 'idda. And if the situation were reversed, then according to the Sahibayn the master's statement (is accepted), and likewise according to Imam Sahib in the correct narration. Because the slave woman is currently completing the 'idda, and the master's ownership of enjoyment (tamattu') becomes apparent. So the slave woman's statement is not accepted (in voiding the master's right), unlike the first reason. Because by confirming the raj'a, the master admits the existence of the 'idda at the time of raj'a, and the master's ownership is not apparent with the 'idda (so the master's statement is not accepted). And if the slave woman said, 'My 'idda has passed,' and the husband and master said, 'Your 'idda has not passed,' then the slave woman's statement (is accepted). Because the slave woman is trustworthy (ameen) in her statement 'my 'idda has passed' (inqada't 'iddati), because the slave woman is the one who knows the expiry of the 'idda. Explanation: If the slave woman's husband said after her 'idda had passed, 'I have returned to you during the 'idda,' there are four scenarios: (1) Both the master and the slave woman confirm him; (2) Both deny him; (3) The master confirms and the slave woman denies; (4) The reverse, i.e., the master denies and the slave woman confirms. In the first scenario, by consensus, the raj'a is valid. In the second scenario, by consensus, the raj'a is not valid unless the husband brings evidence. In the third scenario, if the husband has no evidence, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the slave woman's statement is accepted, and Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad also hold this view; according to the Sahibayn, the master's statement is accepted. The Sahibayn's evidence is that after the 'idda has passed, the benefits of the pudendum (manafi' al-bud') are owned by the master. So the husband's affirmation of the benefits of the pudendum is an affirmation of his own right. Therefore it cannot be rejected, and this becomes similar to the master affirming marriage upon his slave woman. For example, if he said, 'I have married my slave woman to so-and-so,' then in that affirmation the master's statement is accepted. So likewise here, the master's statement is accepted. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the ruling of raj'a is based on the continuation or expiry of the 'idda (i.e., if the 'idda remains, raj'a is established; if the 'idda has passed, the ruling of raj'a is not established). And regarding the continuation or non-continuation of the 'idda, the woman's statement is accepted. So whatever is based on the 'idda, i.e., raj'a, the woman's statement is accepted as well. The fourth scenario, which the author of Hidayah expressed as 'and if it were the reverse' (wa law kana 'ala al-qalb), i.e., the slave woman confirmed the husband and the master denied, then according to the Sahibayn the master's statement is accepted. The evidence is that the benefits of the pudendum are purely the master's right, and the husband is the claimant against the master, and the master is the denier. And since it is assumed that the claimant does not have present evidence, the denier's (i.e., the master's) statement is accepted. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the correct narration is also that the master's statement is accepted. The evidence is that currently the slave woman is in a state where the days of 'idda have passed, and the master's ownership of enjoyment (tamattu') from his slave woman has become apparently established. So if raj'a were established by the statement of the slave woman and her husband, the master's ownership of enjoyment would be voided, whereas mere affirmation of someone cannot void another's right. Therefore here too, the slave woman's statement is not accepted in voiding the master's right. Unlike the first scenario, i.e., the scenario where the master confirmed the husband and the slave woman denied: according to Imam Sahib, in that scenario the slave woman's statement is accepted. Because when the master confirmed the husband in raj'a, he (the master) thereby admitted that at the time of raj'a the 'idda existed, and with the existence of the 'idda, the master's ownership of enjoyment cannot be obtained. So since in this scenario accepting the slave woman's statement does not necessitate voiding the master's right, therefore in this scenario the slave woman's statement is accepted, not the master's. And if the slave woman said, 'My 'idda has passed,' and the days are such that the 'idda cannot possibly have passed, and the husband and master said, 'Your 'idda has not passed,' then the slave woman's statement is accepted. Because the slave woman is trustworthy regarding the expiry of the 'idda, because she is the one who knows the passing of the 'idda. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute from the chapter on Talaq of the Sick, dealing with a specific case: after a slave woman's 'idda has expired, her husband claims he had already returned to her (raj'a) during the 'idda. The question is whose word is accepted when the master (mawlā) and the slave woman disagree. The text outlines four scenarios. In the first, both master and slave woman confirm the husband; by consensus raj'a is valid. In the second, both deny; by consensus raj'a is invalid unless the husband brings proof. The third scenario is when the master confirms but the slave woman denies. Here, Imam Abu Hanifa and others (Imam Zufar, Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) accept the slave woman's word, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) accept the master's word. The Sahibayn argue that after 'idda, the benefits of the slave woman's pudendum (manafi' al-bud') belong to the master, so the master's affirmation regarding his own property cannot be rejected. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the ruling of raj'a depends on the 'idda, and regarding the 'idda the woman's word is accepted, so the same applies to what depends on it. The fourth scenario is when the slave woman confirms the husband and the master denies. Here, the Sahibayn and also the correct narration from Imam Abu Hanifa accept the master's word, because the master is the owner and the husband is a claimant; accepting the slave woman's word would void the master's right without proof. Finally, the text adds that if the slave woman claims her 'idda has passed but it is impossible (e.g., not enough time), her word is accepted because she is the one who knows her own cycles. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi approach of balancing ownership rights with the woman's knowledge of her own 'idda.

Key Terms
رجعت (raj‘ah): The husband's right to take back his wife during her 'idda after a revocable divorce without a new marriage contract.
بضع (bud‘): The pudendum/vulva; used metonymically for the right of sexual access. In the context of a slave woman, it is owned by the master.
مولیٰ (mawlā): The master or owner of a slave. In this passage, the mawlā owns the slave woman (bāndī).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third scenario (master confirms husband's claim of raj'a, slave woman denies), whose statement is accepted according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The husband's, because he is the one making the claim
B) The master's, because he owns the slave woman
C) The slave woman's, because raj'a is based on 'idda and her word is accepted regarding 'idda
D) No one's; a judge must investigate

Key Takeaway
In disputes over raj'a after a slave woman's 'idda, the acceptance of testimony hinges on whether the master admits the 'idda existed: if he confirms, the slave woman's denial is taken; if he denies, his word prevails.

Talaq — Divorce

When the Right of Raj'a Ends After the Third Menstruation
Ruling on when raj'a terminates after third menstruation: based on cessation for ten days or less, and the effect of tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which raj'a ends after the third menstruation and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tayammum.

Core Idea
Raj'a ends definitively when blood stops for ten days; with shorter cessation, it requires confirmation by ghusl or prayer time passage.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we examine the precise moment when a husband's right to return (raj'a) terminates after a revocable divorce. The ruling hinges on the duration of menstrual bleeding and the nature of purification. We will also explore an important intra-Hanafi difference between Imam Muhammad and the two masters (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the effect of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on cessation for ten days
Find the explicit rule: if blood stops for a full ten days, raj'a ends even without ghusl. What is the basis?
Ten days is the maximum menstrual period in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Analyze the ruling for cessation less than ten days
When bleeding stops for less than ten days, raj'a continues until ghusl or a complete prayer time passes. Why? Because bleeding may return.
This shows the principle of istishab (continuity) until certainty.
3
Understand the special case of a Kitabiyya
For a non-Muslim woman, cessation alone suffices because no further signs are expected.
This is an exception based on custom.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum
Compare the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf (istihsan) and Muhammad (qiyas) regarding tayammum cutting raj'a.
Note the different views on tayammum's purifying effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا انقطع الدم من الحيضة الثالثة لعشرة ايام انقطعت الرجعة وان لم تغتسل وان انقطع لاقل من عشرة ايام لم ينقطع الرجعة حتى تغتسل او يمضى عليها وقت صلوة كامل لان الحيض لامزيد له على العشرة فبمجرد الانقطاع خرجت من الحيض فانقضت العدة وانقطعت الرجعة وفيما دون العشرة يحتمل عود الدم فلابدان يعتضد الانقطاع بحقيقة الاغتسال اوبلزوم حكم من احكام الطاهرات بمضى وقت الصلاة بخلاف ما اذا كانت كتابية لانه لايتوقع فى حقها امارة زائدة فاكتفى بالانقطاع وتنقطع اذا تيممت وصلت عند ابي حنيفة وابى يوسف وهذا استحسان وقال محمد اذا تيممت انقطعت وهذا قياس لان التيمم حال عدم الماء طهارة مطلقة حتى يثبت به من الاحكام ما يثبت بالاغتسال فكان بمنزلته ولهما انه ملوث غیر مطهر وانما اعتبر طهارة ضرورة ان لاتتضاعف الواجبات وهذه الضرورة تتحقق حال اداء الصلوة لا فيما قبلها من الاوقات والاحكام الثابتة ايضا ضرورية اقتضائية ثم قيل تنقطع ينفس الشروع عندهما وقيل بعد الفراغ ليتقرر حكم جواز الصلوة
And when blood stops from the third menstruation for ten days, the raj'a is cut off even if she has not performed ghusl. And if it stops for less than ten days, the raj'a is not cut off until she performs ghusl or a complete prayer time passes over her. Because menstruation does not exceed ten days, so with mere cessation she exits from menstruation, thus the 'idda ends and raj'a is cut off. In the case of less than ten days, there is probability of the return of blood, so it is necessary that the cessation be strengthened by the actuality of ghusl or by the obligation of one of the rulings of purity (tahirat) by the passing of prayer time. Unlike if she is a Kitabiyya (Jewish or Christian), because no additional sign is expected in her regard, so cessation suffices. And it (raj'a) is cut off if she performs tayammum and prays, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; this is istihsan. And Muhammad said: if she performs tayammum, it is cut off; this is qiyas, because tayammum in the absence of water is an absolute purification, such that it establishes the same rulings as ghusl, so it is like ghusl. And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): tayammum is contaminated (mulawwith) and not purifying (ghayr mutahhir); it is only considered a purification out of necessity so that obligations do not multiply, and this necessity is realized at the time of performing prayer, not before that in times and rulings. Those rulings are also necessary and contingent. Then it is said: it (raj'a) is cut off upon beginning (tayammum) according to them, and it is said: after completion, so that the ruling of permissibility of prayer becomes established.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This is a ruling on when the right of raj'a (return to marriage during 'idda) terminates after the third menstruation. The text is from the chapter on Talaq of the Sick in Al-Hidayah. The ruling: If the bleeding of the third menstruation stops for a full ten days (the maximum length of menstruation), the raj'a ends immediately, even if the woman has not performed ghusl. Because the cessation of blood for ten days definitively ends the menstrual period, thus the 'idda is complete and raj'a no longer possible. If the bleeding stops for less than ten days, however, raj'a does not end until she either performs ghusl or a complete prayer time passes without bleeding. The reason is that since the maximum menstruation is ten days, bleeding could return, so cessation alone is not conclusive. Strengthening is needed either by actual purification (ghusl) or by the passage of a full prayer time (which implies purity). For a Kitabiyya (Jewish or Christian woman), the cessation alone suffices because no further signs (like subsequent purity) are expected from her. The text then discusses the case of tayammum: according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a woman performs tayammum and prays, raj'a is cut off—this is istihsan. Imam Muhammad says that tayammum alone is sufficient, based on qiyas with ghusl. The other two argue that tayammum is not a full purification; it is only valid for the necessity of prayer, so the ruling of cutting raj'a requires either actually praying or reaching the stage where prayer becomes permissible. There is a further discussion on whether raj'a is cut off at the start of tayammum or after completion. The passage illustrates how Hanafi jurisprudence uses principles of maximum menstrual period, istihsan, and distinguishing between types of purification.

Key Terms
رجعة (raj‘ah): The husband's right to return to his wife during the 'idda of a revocable divorce.
حیض (hayḍ): Menstruation; the maximum duration according to Hanafis is ten days.
تیمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth or dust as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does raj'a end if the third menstruation's bleeding stops for less than ten days?
A) Immediately upon stopping, regardless of ghusl
B) Only after she performs ghusl or a complete prayer time passes
C) After ten days from the start of bleeding
D) Only if she performs tayammum

Key Takeaway
The termination of raj'a after the third menstruation depends on the duration of cessation and the nature of purification, with an intra-Hanafi dispute on the role of tayammum.

Testimony in Disputes Over Slave Woman's 'Iddah Revocation
Explaining whose testimony is accepted in dispute over slave woman's 'iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for whose testimony is accepted in each of three scenarios of dispute between a slave woman's husband and master over 'iddah revocation, and explain the rational proof for the master's priority.

Core Idea
A mere claim cannot invalidate an established right of another, so the master's statement is preferred unless he confirms revocation.

When a slave woman's husband claims he revoked the divorce during her 'iddah, but the master denies it, whose word counts? This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah unpacks a nuanced Hanafi ruling based on the principle that a mere claim cannot nullify another's established right. We will trace three distinct scenarios and the rational proof behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The husband claims he revoked the divorce (raj'ah) during the 'iddah. The master denies it. The 'iddah is assumed to have expired, so the master's right to enjoy his slave is apparently established.
This sets up the conflict between the husband's claim and the master's established right.
2
Apply the principle of avoiding harm to an established right
Since accepting the husband's claim would invalidate the master's right of enjoyment, and a mere claim cannot override another's right, the master's denial is accepted. The correct narration from Imam Abu Hanifa supports this.
Rational proof: a claim cannot nullify a pre-existing right.
3
Contrast with the second scenario (master confirms)
If the master confirms the husband's revocation, then the slave woman's denial is accepted. This is because the master's own admission that revocation occurred during the 'iddah means his right was never established.
No conflict with the master's right arises from accepting the slave woman's statement.
4
Contrast with the third scenario (timeframe impossible)
If the slave woman claims her 'iddah has passed but the elapsed time makes it impossible, her statement is accepted because she is the trusted authority (amin) on her own 'iddah.
This follows the principle that the one with direct knowledge is believed.
5
Derive the practical outcome (thamarah al-khilaf)
In scenario 1, the master retains his right; in scenario 2, the revocation is valid; in scenario 3, the slave woman's 'iddah is considered complete.
The ruling depends on who is the denier and whether an established right is at stake.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب طلاق المريض
اشرف الہدایہ شرح ار ہدایہ جلد پنجم ان کا مدعی ہے اور مولیٰ منکر ہے اور چونکہ مفروض یہ ہے کہ مدعی کے پاس بعینہ موجود نہیں لہذا منکر یعنی مولی کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی بھی صحیح روایت یہ ہے کہ مولیٰ کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بالفعل تو یہ باندی ایسی حالت میں ہے کہ ایام عدت گزر چکے ہیں اور مولی کے واسطے اپنی باندی سے تمتع حاصل کرنے کی ملک بظاہر ثابت ہو چکی ۔ پس اگر باندی اور اس کے شوہر کے قول سے رجعت ثابت ہو جائے تو مولیٰ کی ملک تمتع باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ حالانکہ محض کسی کا اقرار حق غیر کو باطل کرنے میں قابل نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا یہاں بھی باندی کا قول مولی کے حق کو باطل کرنے میں قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ برخلاف پہلی صورت کے یعنی وہ صورت جس میں مولیٰ نے شوہر کی تصدیق کی ہے اور باندی نے تکذیب ، تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس صورت میں باندی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مولیٰ نے جب رجعت میں شوہر کی تصدیق کی تو اس سے مولیٰ اس بانگلا مقر ہو گیا کہ رجعت کے وقت عدت موجود تھی اور عدت کے ہوتے ہوئے مولیٰ کے لئے ملک تمتع حاصل نہیں ہوسکتی۔ پس چونکہ اس صورت میں باندی کا قول قبول کرنے میں مولی سے حق کو باطل کرنا لازم نہیں آتا۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں باندی کا قول معتبر ہو گا نہ کہ مولی کا۔ اور اگر باندی نے کہا کہ میری عدت گزر چکی اور ایام اتنے ہیں کہ عدت گزرنا ناممکن ہے اور شوہر اور مولی نے کہا کہ تیری عدت نہیں گزری تو باندی ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ باندی انقضاء عدت کے سلسلہ میں امین ہے۔ اس لئے کہ باندی ہی عدت کے گزرنے کا علم رکھتی ہے۔ واللہ اعلم۔ ا
Chapter of Divorce of the Sick. Ashraf al-Hidayah, commentary on al-Hidayah, volume five: He (the husband) is the claimant and the master (mawla) is the denier. And since it is assumed that the claimant does not have the actual evidence, therefore the statement of the denier, i.e., the master, will be considered valid. And the correct narration from Imam Abu Hanifa is also that the master's statement will be considered valid. The proof is that currently this slave woman is in a state where the days of 'iddah have passed, and the master's ownership to enjoy his slave woman is already established apparently. So if the 'iddah revocation is proven by the statement of the slave woman and her husband, then the master's right of enjoyment would become void. Whereas a mere confession (iqrar) of someone cannot invalidate the right of another. Hence here too, the slave woman's statement will not be accepted to invalidate the master's right. Contrary to the first case, i.e., the case in which the master confirmed the husband's statement and the slave woman denied it, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, in that case the slave woman's statement will be considered valid. Because when the master confirmed the husband's revocation, the master thereby admitted that the 'iddah was present at the time of revocation, and with the 'iddah present, the master cannot have the right of enjoyment. So since in that case accepting the slave woman's statement does not necessitate invalidating the master's right, therefore in that case the slave woman's statement is valid, not the master's. And if the slave woman says, 'My 'iddah has passed and the days are such that passing the 'iddah is impossible,' and the husband and master say, 'Your 'iddah has not passed,' then the slave woman's statement is valid. Because the slave woman is trustworthy (amin) regarding the completion of the 'iddah. For she alone knows the passing of the 'iddah. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and commentary on a ruling regarding testimony in a dispute over the 'iddah and revocation (رجعت) of a slave woman. The scenario: a slave woman's husband claims he revoked the divorce during her 'iddah, but the master denies it. Since the 'iddah is assumed to have expired and the master's right to enjoy his slave is established, accepting the husband's claim would invalidate the master's right, which cannot be done based solely on a claim. Therefore, the master's statement is accepted. The correct narration from Imam Abu Hanifa supports this. However, if the master confirms the husband's claim, then the slave woman's denial is accepted because there is no conflict with the master's right — the master himself admitted the 'iddah existed at the time of revocation, so his right was never established. In a third scenario where the slave woman claims the 'iddah has passed (but the time frame makes it impossible), her statement is accepted because she is the trusted authority (amin) on her own 'iddah. This follows the principle that the one who has direct knowledge is trusted.

Key Terms
رجعت (Raj'ah): Revocation of divorce during the 'iddah period, allowing the husband to take his wife back without a new marriage contract.
عدت ('Iddah): Waiting period after divorce or death during which a woman cannot remarry. Here it refers to the 'iddah of a slave woman (two menstrual cycles).
مولی (Mawla): Master or owner of a slave woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct narration of Imam Abu Hanifa, whose statement is accepted when a slave woman's husband claims revocation (raj'ah) and the master denies it?
A) The husband's, because he is the claimant.
B) The slave woman's, because she knows her 'iddah.
C) The master's, because accepting the husband's claim would invalidate the master's established right.
D) The qadi's, based on external evidence.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the master's statement is preferred over the husband's claim of revocation because a claim cannot invalidate an established right, but if the master confirms the claim, the slave woman's denial is accepted.

End of Revocation After Third Haydah: Basic Conditions
Ruling with proof: conditions for the end of revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the right to revoke divorce ends after the third menstruation, and apply them to cases where blood stops exactly at ten days or before ten days.

Core Idea
Revocation ends when 'iddah is certain; certainty of purification requires full ten days or a confirmation act.

This lesson examines the precise moment when a husband loses his right to take back his wife (raj‘ah) during the waiting period after a revocable divorce. The key factor is the completion of the third menstruation. However, completion is not simply when bleeding stops; it depends on whether the blood ceases at the maximum possible duration (ten days) or earlier. We will explore the reasoning behind these rules and the special case of a Kitabiyyah woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the right and its termination condition
The right to revoke (raj‘ah) exists only during the 'iddah. The 'iddah for a free woman ends with the completion of three menstrual cycles. This lesson focuses on the end of the third cycle: when exactly does the 'iddah complete, and with it the right to revoke?
The ruling hinges on the definition of 'completion of hayd'.
2
Differentiate the two scenarios of blood cessation
If the blood from the third menstruation stops exactly after ten days (the maximum), revocation ends immediately even without ghusl. If it stops before ten days, revocation continues until a sign of purification appears: either ghusl or the passage of a full prayer time.
The ten-day cap is unique to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the underlying rationale
The reason for the distinction: when blood stops at ten days, there is no possibility of return (since hayd cannot exceed ten days), so certainty of completion is established. When it stops earlier, blood may return within the ten-day window, so mere cessation is not enough.
Certainty (yaqīn) is needed to end the right.
4
Define the confirmation acts
The confirmation acts are ghusl (full body wash) or the passing of a complete prayer time (from its earliest permissible entry to its exit). Both establish that the woman is in a state of purity (tahārah) from hayd, as prayer only becomes obligatory on a pure woman.
Ghusl is an actual purification; prayer time is a proxy sign.
5
Note the exception for a Kitabiyyah
If the woman is Jewish or Christian (Kitabiyyah), since she is not obliged to pray and no extra sign is expected, mere cessation of blood suffices to end revocation, even if less than ten days.
This exception confirms that the rule for Muslim women relies on the expectation of prayer as a marker of purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجوع کا حق کون سے حیض کے بعد ختم تصور کیا جائے گا
واذا انقطع الدم من الحيضة الثالثة لعشرة ايام انقطعت الرجعة وان لم تغتسل وان انقطع لاقل من عشرة ايام لم ينقطع الرجعة حتى تغتسل او يمضى عليها وقت صلوة كامل لان الحيض لامزيد له على العشرة فبمجرد الانقطاع خرجت من الحيض فانقضت العدة وانقطعت الرجعة وفيما دون العشرة يحتمل عود الدم فلابدان يعتضد الانقطاع بحقيقة الاغتسال اوبلزوم حكم من احكام الطاهرات بمضى وقت الصلاة بخلاف ما اذا كانت كتابية لانه لايتوقع فى حقها امارة زائدة فاكتفى بالانقطاع وتنقطع اذا تيممت وصلت عند ابي حنيفة وابى يوسف وهذا استحسان وقال محمد اذا تيممت انقطعت وهذا قياس لان التيمم حال عدم الماء طهارة مطلقة حتى يثبت به من الاحكام ما يثبت بالاغتسال فكان بمنزلته ولهما انه ملوث غیر مطهر وانما اعتبر طهارة ضرورة ان لاتتضاعف الواجبات وهذه الضرورة تتحقق حال اداء الصلوة لا فيما قبلها من الاوقات والاحكام الثابتة ايضا ضرورية اقتضائية ثم قيل تنقطع ينفس الشروع عندهما وقيل بعد الفراغ ليتقرر حكم جواز الصلوة
ترجمہ اور جب تیسرے حیض سے خون بند ہوا پورے دس یوم پر تو رجعت منقطع ہو گئی اگر عورت نے غسل نہیں کیا اور دس روز سے کم میں (خون) منقطع ہوا ہو تو رجعت منقطع نہ ہوگی ، یہاں تک کہ عورت غسل کرلے۔ یا اس پر نماز کا پورا وقت گزر جائے کیونکہ حیض کے واسطے دس روز پر زیادتی ( متصور ) نہیں۔ تو ( خون منقطع ہوتے ہی وہ حیض سے نکل گئی پھر عدت گزرگئی اور رجعت منقطع ہوگئی اور دس روز سے کم میں احتمال ہے خون کے لوٹ آنے کا۔ پس ضروری ہوا کہ منقطع ہو جانے کے احتمال کو قوت دی جائے حقیقت انفنسال کے ساتھ ۔ یا
پاک عورتوں کے احکام میں سے کوئی حکم ( اس پر لازم ہونے کے ساتھ نماز کا وقت گزر جانے کی وجہ سے۔ برخلاف اس کے جب عورت کتابیہ ہو۔ کیونکہ اس کے حق میں کسی زائد علامت کی امید نہیں تو صرف خون ) منقطع ہونے پر اکتفا کیا گیا اور ( رجعت ) منقطع ہو جائے گی جب تیم کر کے نماز پڑھے ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اور یہ استحسان ہے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ جب اس نے تمیم کیا تو عدت و رجعت منقطع ہو گئی اور یہ قیاس ہے۔کیونکہ تیم پانی نہ ہونے کی حالت میں مطلقا طہارت ہے ۔ حتی کہ جو احکام غسل کرنے سے ثابت ہوتے ہیں تیم کرنے سے ثابت ہو جائیں گے۔ پس تیم کرنا بمنزلہ فسل کر لینے کے ہوا۔
اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تیم ملوث کرنے والا ہے نہ کہ پاک کرنے والا اور تیم کو طہارت اس ضرورت سے معتبر مانا گیا ہے کہ واجبات کئی گنا نہ ہو جائیں اور یہ ضرورت نماز ادا کرنے کی حالت میں متحقق ہوگی نہ کہ اس سے پہلے اوقات میں اور احکام جو ثابت ہوئے ہیں وہ بھی (نماز کے ) مقتضی ہونے کی ضرورت سے ثابت ہوئے ہیں۔ پھر کہا گیا کہ شیخین کے نزدیک نماز شروع کرتے ہی حکم رجعت منقطع ہو جائے گا اور کہا گیا کہ نماز سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد ( منقطع ہوگا ) تا کہ جواز صلوۃ کا حکم متقر رہو جائے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر پورے دس روز پر تیسرے حیض سے خون منقطع ہو گیا تو رجعت منقطع ہوگئی ۔ اگر چہ عورت نے غسل نہیں کیا اور اگر دس روز سے کم میں خون منقطع ہوا ہے تو محض خون منقطع ہونے سے رجعت منقطع نہیں ہوگی ، یہاں تک کہ وہ عورت غسل کرلے یا اس پر نماز کا ایک پورا وقت گزر جائے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ رجعت کا منقطع ہونا موقوف ہے عدت کے گزر جانے پر اور عدت کا گزر جانا موقوف ہے تیسرے حیض سے فارغ ہونے پر اور تیسرے حیض سے فارغ ہونا موقوف ہے حصول طہارت پر ۔ پس اگر ایام حیض پورے دس دن ہیں تو طہارت محض انقطاع دم سے حاصل ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ حیض دس دن سے زیادتی کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا۔ لہذا دس دن پورے ہونے کی صورت میں خون کے منقطع ہونے سے اس عورت کو حیض سے فراغت ہوگئی اور اس کی عدت بھی گزرگئی اور رجعت کا حکم بھی منقطع ہو گیا، خواہ یہ عورت غسل کرے یا نہ کرے۔ اور دس دن نے کم میں اگر تیسرے حیض کا خون منقطع ہو گیا تو چونکہ اس صورت میں خون کے لوٹ آنے کا احتمال ہے اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ انقطاع دم کو قوت دی جائے یا حقیقت میں غسل کر لینے کے ساتھ اور یا پاک عورتوں کے احکام میں سے کوئی حکم اس پر لازم ہونے کے ساتھ مثلاً جب اس عورت پر نماز کا کامل وقت گزر گیا تو نماز اس کے ذمہ میں دین ہوگئی اور یہ پاک عورتوں کے احکام میں سے ہے۔
اس کے برخلاف اگر عورت کتابیہ ( یہودی یا نصرانیہ ) ہے اور دس دن سے کم میں خون منقطع ہو گیا تو بغیر فسل کئے اور بغیر نماز کا وقت گزرے صرف انقطاع دم سے اس کی رجعت منقطع ہوگئی اس لئے کہ اس کے حق میں انقطاع حیض پر کسی علامت زائدہ کی توقع نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کتابی پرنہ نماز واجب ہے اور نہ نسل اس وجہ سے محض انقطاع پر اکتفا کیا گیا ہے۔ اور اگر معدہ رجعیہ کے تیسرے حیض کا خون دس دن سے کم میں منقطع ہو گیا پھر اس عورت نے تمیم کر کے نماز پڑھ لی فرض یا نفل تو شیخین کے نزدیک رجعت منقطع ہوگئی۔ یعنی انقطاع رجعت تیمیم اور نماز دونوں سے ہوگا اور یہ حکم استحسانا ہے اور امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر تیم کر لیا تو محض تیم کر لینے سے رجعت منقطع ہو گئی۔ اسی کے قائل امام زفر اور امام احمد ہیں اور یہی قیاس بھی ہے۔
After which menstruation is the right to revocation considered ended? And when the blood from the third menstruation stops for ten days, the revocation ends, even if she has not performed ghusl. And if it stops for less than ten days, the revocation does not end until she performs ghusl or a complete prayer time passes over her. Because menstruation does not exceed ten days. So by mere cessation, she exits menstruation, the 'iddah is completed, and revocation ends. For less than ten days, there is a possibility of blood returning. So it is necessary to support the cessation by the actual act of ghusl or by the imposition of a ruling of the pure women through the passing of a prayer time. Contrary to if she is a Kitabiyyah (Jewish/Christian), because no additional indication is expected regarding her, so cessation alone suffices. And it ends if she performs tayammum and prays according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and this is istihsan. Muhammad said: if she performs tayammum, it ends, and this is qiyas, because tayammum in the absence of water is an absolute purification, so the rulings established by ghusl are established by it, so it is like ghusl. And the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) have the proof that tayammum is soiled, not purifying; it is only considered purification out of necessity so that obligations are not doubled, and this necessity is realized at the time of performing prayer, not before. And the rulings established are also necessitated by necessity. Then it is said: according to them, it ends with the commencement (of prayer), and it is said after completion to establish the ruling of permissibility of prayer. (Urdu commentary follows: Translation of the above with further elaboration: If on the third menstruation the blood stops at ten days, revocation ends even without ghusl. If less than ten days, it doesn't end until ghusl or a full prayer time passes. Reason: hayd max 10 days. So at ten days, cessation means exit from hayd, 'iddah completes. Less than ten, blood may return, so need confirmation by ghusl or prayer time. For Kitabiyyah, no expectation of extra sign, so cessation suffices. If she performs tayammum and prays, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (istihsan), revocation ends; according to Muhammad, tayammum alone ends it (qiyas). The two argue tayammum is not fully purifying but allowed out of necessity, which is only at prayer time. Dispute on whether revocation ends at start or completion of prayer. Then detailed explanation: Revocation depends on 'iddah, which depends on completion of third hayd, which depends on purification. At ten days, purification by cessation alone; less than ten, need ghusl or prayer time. For Kitabiyyah, no prayer or other sign, so cessation suffices. If woman does tayammum and prays (fard or nafl), according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), revocation ends; this is istihsan. Muhammad, Zufar, and Ahmad say tayammum alone ends it, and this is qiyas.)
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions under which the right to revoke divorce (رجعت) ends after the third menstruation. The core ruling: if blood stops upon completing ten days (maximum hayd), revocation ends immediately even without ghusl, because no possibility of return. If blood stops before ten days, revocation does not end until the woman performs ghusl or a full prayer time (from its entry to its end) passes, because blood may return. For a Kitabiyyah (Jewish/Christian woman), since she is not obliged to pray and no other sign is expected, mere cessation suffices even if less than ten days. Then the text discusses the role of tayammum: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (istihsan), revocation ends only if she performs tayammum and prays; according to Muhammad (qiyas), tayammum alone suffices because tayammum is a complete purification in absence of water. The text also notes a further ikhtilaf among the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) on whether revocation ends at the start of prayer or after completion. The commentary elaborates the reasoning: revocation is tied to completion of 'iddah, which requires purification from hayd. At full ten days, cessation itself indicates purification; less than ten, need confirmation by ghusl or a sign from the rules of pure women (e.g., obligation of prayer).

Key Terms
رجعة (Raj'ah): Revocation of divorce during the 'iddah period; the husband's right to take back his wife without a new marriage.
عدة ('Iddah): The waiting period after divorce, here specified as three menstrual cycles (or two for a slave woman). It ends with the completion of the third haydah.
كتابية (Kitabiyyah): A Jewish or Christian woman who is not Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim woman's third menstrual blood stops after 8 days, when does her right to revoke divorce end?
A) Immediately upon cessation of blood
B) Only after she performs ghusl or a full prayer time passes
C) Only after she prays two rak'ahs
D) When she performs tayammum

Key Takeaway
The key point is that the right to revoke divorce ends only when certainty of the third hayd's completion is established; for cessation before ten days, a confirming act (ghusl or prayer time) is required.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
12 min
The Tayammum Dispute: Does It Alone End Revocation?
Ruling with proof: intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (istihsan) with Muhammad (qiyas) on whether tayammum alone ends the right to revoke divorce, and explain the underlying usul principle.

Core Idea
Tayammum is a purification of necessity, not a full purifier – thus its effect on ending 'iddah requires the additional act of prayer.

When a woman in her 'iddah has no access to water, she may perform tayammum. But does this dry ablution alone complete her purification from hayd and thus end the husband's right to revoke? The Hanafi school is divided. This lesson examines the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (who require both tayammum and prayer) against Muhammad (who holds tayammum alone suffices). We will see how the two sides differ on the legal nature of tayammum, and the practical outcome of their ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario triggering the dispute
The dispute arises when a woman in her 'iddah experiences the third menstruation, the blood stops before ten days, and she performs tayammum due to lack of water. The question is: does tayammum alone end the right to revoke, or must she also pray?
This is a sub-scenario of the general rule that cessation before ten days requires a confirming sign.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) say: revocation ends only if she performs tayammum and prays (istihsan). Muhammad says: tayammum alone ends revocation (qiyas).
Note that Zufar and Ahmad ibn Hanbal agree with Muhammad.
3
Trace the proof of each position
Muhammad's proof (qiyas): Tayammum is a complete purification (tahārah mutlaqah) in the absence of water; the same rulings that apply to ghusl apply to tayammum. Therefore, just as ghusl ends revocation, so does tayammum. The Shaykhayn's proof (istihsan): Tayammum is not a true purifier (it is mulawwith, not mutahhir); it is only considered purification out of necessity to avoid repeating obligations (lā tatadā‘af al-wājibāt). This necessity exists only at the time of performing prayer, not before.
The difference is rooted in the epistemological weight of qiyas versus istihsan.
4
Analyze the basis of ikhtilaf
The core issue is the nature of tayammum: Is it a full substitute for ghusl in all respects (Muhammad) or a limited dispensation only for prayer (Shaykhayn)? The Shaykhayn argue that because tayammum is not genuinely purifying, its effect is restricted to the act of prayer; therefore, the ruling of purity that ends revocation requires prayer, not just tayammum.
This reflects the Hanafi usul principle that istihsan can override qiyas when the analogical result conflicts with a stronger principle.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, if a woman performs tayammum but does not pray, according to Muhammad the husband loses the right to revoke immediately; according to the Shaykhayn, the husband retains the right until she prays or until a full prayer time passes (if she was unable to pray).
The text also reports a sub-ikhtilaf among the Shaykhayn on whether revocation ends at the start or completion of prayer.

After which menstruation is the right to revocation considered ended? And when the blood from the third menstruation stops for ten days, the revocation ends, even if she has not performed ghusl. And if it stops for less than ten days, the revocation does not end until she performs ghusl or a complete prayer time passes over her. Because menstruation does not exceed ten days. So by mere cessation, she exits menstruation, the 'iddah is completed, and revocation ends. For less than ten days, there is a possibility of blood returning. So it is necessary to support the cessation by the actual act of ghusl or by the imposition of a ruling of the pure women through the passing of a prayer time. Contrary to if she is a Kitabiyyah (Jewish/Christian), because no additional indication is expected regarding her, so cessation alone suffices. And it ends if she performs tayammum and prays according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and this is istihsan. Muhammad said: if she performs tayammum, it ends, and this is qiyas, because tayammum in the absence of water is an absolute purification, so the rulings established by ghusl are established by it, so it is like ghusl. And the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) have the proof that tayammum is soiled, not purifying; it is only considered purification out of necessity so that obligations are not doubled, and this necessity is realized at the time of performing prayer, not before. And the rulings established are also necessitated by necessity. Then it is said: according to them, it ends with the commencement (of prayer), and it is said after completion to establish the ruling of permissibility of prayer. (Urdu commentary follows: Translation of the above with further elaboration: If on the third menstruation the blood stops at ten days, revocation ends even without ghusl. If less than ten days, it doesn't end until ghusl or a full prayer time passes. Reason: hayd max 10 days. So at ten days, cessation means exit from hayd, 'iddah completes. Less than ten, blood may return, so need confirmation by ghusl or prayer time. For Kitabiyyah, no expectation of extra sign, so cessation suffices. If she performs tayammum and prays, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (istihsan), revocation ends; according to Muhammad, tayammum alone ends it (qiyas). The two argue tayammum is not fully purifying but allowed out of necessity, which is only at prayer time. Dispute on whether revocation ends at start or completion of prayer. Then detailed explanation: Revocation depends on 'iddah, which depends on completion of third hayd, which depends on purification. At ten days, purification by cessation alone; less than ten, need ghusl or prayer time. For Kitabiyyah, no prayer or other sign, so cessation suffices. If woman does tayammum and prays (fard or nafl), according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), revocation ends; this is istihsan. Muhammad, Zufar, and Ahmad say tayammum alone ends it, and this is qiyas.)
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions under which the right to revoke divorce (رجعت) ends after the third menstruation. The core ruling: if blood stops upon completing ten days (maximum hayd), revocation ends immediately even without ghusl, because no possibility of return. If blood stops before ten days, revocation does not end until the woman performs ghusl or a full prayer time (from its entry to its end) passes, because blood may return. For a Kitabiyyah (Jewish/Christian woman), since she is not obliged to pray and no other sign is expected, mere cessation suffices even if less than ten days. Then the text discusses the role of tayammum: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (istihsan), revocation ends only if she performs tayammum and prays; according to Muhammad (qiyas), tayammum alone suffices because tayammum is a complete purification in absence of water. The text also notes a further ikhtilaf among the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) on whether revocation ends at the start of prayer or after completion. The commentary elaborates the reasoning: revocation is tied to completion of 'iddah, which requires purification from hayd. At full ten days, cessation itself indicates purification; less than ten, need confirmation by ghusl or a sign from the rules of pure women (e.g., obligation of prayer).

Key Terms
تيمم (Tayammum): Dry ablution with dust in place of wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
استحسان (Istihsan): A method of juristic preference that deviates from strict qiyas due to a stronger evidence or necessity. Used here by the Shaykhayn to require prayer.
قياس (Qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause (illah). Used by Muhammad to analogize tayammum to ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, when does the right to revoke divorce end for a woman who performs tayammum due to lack of water?
A) Immediately after performing tayammum
B) Only after she performs a prayer (fard or nafl) after tayammum
C) Only after a complete prayer time passes
D) Tayammum never ends revocation; she must use water

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's internal disagreement on tayammum's effect on revocation illustrates the tension between qiyas and istihsan, and shows that tayammum is not legally equivalent to ghusl for all purposes.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Effect of Tayammum on Termination of 'Iddah and Raj'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum and 'iddah termination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when tayammum ends the 'iddah and explain the dispute between Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Tayammum alone does not end the 'iddah; prayer must follow, because tayammum is a necessary purification limited to prayer.

In Hanafi fiqh, the 'iddah after a revocable divorce ends with complete purity from the third menstruation. But what if a woman cannot perform ghusl and uses tayammum instead? Does that count as complete purity? This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) and Imam Muhammad on whether tayammum alone suffices to terminate the right of return (raj'ah).

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling on 'iddah termination
Identify the conditions under which the third menstruation ends: if blood stops after 10 days, purity is immediate; if before 10 days, ghusl or passage of a full prayer time is needed.
This sets the baseline before considering tayammum.
2
Introduce the tayammum scenario
A woman in 'iddah performs tayammum instead of ghusl due to water unavailability. The question is whether this tayammum alone ends the 'iddah and cuts off raj'ah.
The dispute arises from the nature of tayammum's purifying effect.
3
Present the Shaykhayn's position and proof
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that tayammum is contaminating in essence; it is only considered purifying out of necessity for prayer. Therefore, raj'ah ends only after tayammum followed by prayer (either during or after).
They rely on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas.
4
Present Imam Muhammad's position and proof
Imam Muhammad holds that tayammum in the absence of water is absolute purity, analogical to ghusl. Thus, tayammum alone suffices to end the 'iddah and raj'ah.
He relies on qiyas (analogy) with ghusl.
5
Analyze the tarjih and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that of Shaykhayn: raj'ah ends only after tayammum and prayer. The preferred view is after completing the prayer. The practical difference: if a woman performs tayammum without praying, according to Shaykhayn her husband retains the right of return.
This thamarah al-khilaf directly affects the woman's marital status.

والا حكام الثابتة سے امام محمد کی اصل ( کہ جو احکام نسل سے ثابت ہوتے ہیں وہ تیم سے بھی ثابت ہو جائیں گے ) کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تیم سے ان احکام کا ثبوت جو از صلوۃ کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہے۔ چنانچہ جواز صلوۃ کے لئے قرآت قرآن تو اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ قرآن کا پڑھنا نماز کا رکن ہے اور مسجد اس لئے کہ وہ مکان صلوۃ ہے اور سجدہ تلاوت اس لئے کہ وہ قرآت کے توابع میں سے ہے۔ کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ نمازی نماز میں آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کر دے اور قرآن کا چھوٹا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ اگر ما یجوز بہ الصلوۃ قرآت کرنے سے پہلے بھول گیا تو یہ شخص قرآن کھول کر دیکھنے کی طرف محتاج ہوگا اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ بغیر مس مصحف کے نہیں ہوسکتا۔ بعض حضرات نے شیخین کی دلیل پر اشکال کیا ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ تیم طہارت ضرور یہ ہے اور ضرورت متحقق ہوتی ہے ادا صلوۃ کے وقت نہ کہ اس سے پہلے اور یہ اصول بھی ثابت شدہ ہے کہ الثابت بالضرورة لا يتعدى موضعها یعنی جو چیز ضرورۃ ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ اپنی جگہ سے متجاوزہ نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ پس اس اصول کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ تیم سے رجعت کا حکم منقطع نہ ہوا گر چہ وہ عورت تیم کے بعد نماز بھی پڑھ لے تا وقتیکہ وہ نسل نہ کر لے یا اس پر نماز کا وقت نہ گزر جائے۔
جواب ...... بلاشبه الثابت بالضرورة لا يتعدى موضعها اصول ہے لیکن یہ بھی اصول ہے کہ الضروری متی ماثبت ثبت بجميع لوازمہ یعنی جو چیز ضرور تا ثابت ہو وہ جب ثابت ہوتی ہے تو اپنے تمام لوازم کے ساتھ ثابت ہوتی ہے اور ادا صلوۃ کے وقت ثبوت طہارت کے لوازم سے حیض کا منقطع ہو جانا ہے اور مدت عدت کے لوازم میں سے رجعت کا منقطع ہونا ہے اور قاعدہ لازم الازم لازم ، یعنی لازم کا لازم لازم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اداء صلوۃ کے وقت ثبوت طہارت سے انقطاع رجعت کا حکم ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ عنایه بینی شرح بدانید )
پھر شیخین کے نزدیک بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ نماز شروع کرتے ہی رجعت کا حکم منقطع ہو جائے گا اور بعض کی رائے یہ ہے کہ نماز سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد منقطع ہو گا تا کہ جو از نماز کا حکم ثابت ہو جائے ۔ یہی قول صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ نماز شروع کرنے کے بعد کی حالت ایسی ہے جیسے شروع کرنے سے پہلے تھی۔ چنانچہ اگر دوران نماز پانی دیکھ لیا اور اس کے استعمال پر قدرت بھی ہے تو تھیم کا اثر باقی نہیں رہتا۔ بر خلاف نماز سے فارغ ہونے کے۔
Chapter of the divorce of the sick. Ashraf al-Bidaya sharh Urdu Hidaya volume five. From the rulings of pure women, a ruling (with the obligation upon her and the passing of the time of prayer due to it. Contrary to when the woman is a kitabiyya, because in her right there is no hope of any additional sign, so merely (the blood) stopping sufficed, and the (raj'ah) will be severed when she performs tayammum and prays according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and this is istihsan. And Imam Muhammad said: When she performed tayammum, the 'iddah and raj'ah are severed, and this is qiyas. Because tayammum in the absence of water is absolute purity, such that the rulings that are established from ghusl will be established from tayammum. So tayammum became like performing ghusl. And the proof of the two shaykhs is that tayammum is contaminating, not purifying, and tayammum is considered purity due to necessity so that obligations do not become multiplied, and this necessity is realized at the time of performing the prayer, not in the times before it. And the rulings that are established are also established due to the necessity of being requisite (for prayer). Then it was said that according to the two shaykhs the ruling of raj'ah is severed as soon as prayer is begun, and it was said that it is severed after finishing the prayer so that the ruling of permissibility of prayer becomes established. Explanation of the picture of the case: If the blood of the third menstruation stops after ten full days, then the raj'ah is severed even if the woman did not perform ghusl. And if the blood stops before ten days, then the raj'ah is not severed by merely the stopping of blood, until the woman performs ghusl or a full time of prayer passes upon her. The proof is that the severance of raj'ah depends on the passing of the 'iddah, and the passing of the 'iddah depends on finishing the third menstruation, and finishing the third menstruation depends on attaining purity. So if the days of menstruation are a full ten days, purity is attained by merely the cessation of blood, because menstruation cannot exceed ten days. Therefore, in the case of completion of ten days, by the cessation of blood the woman has finished menstruation and her 'iddah has passed and the ruling of raj'ah is severed, whether she performs ghusl or not. And if the blood of the third menstruation stops before ten days, then because there is a possibility of blood returning in this case, it is necessary to strengthen the cessation of blood either by actually performing ghusl, or by a ruling from the rulings of pure women becoming obligatory upon her, for example, when a complete time of prayer has passed upon her, then prayer becomes a debt upon her, and this is from the rulings of pure women. Contrary to this, if the woman is a kitabiyya (Jewish or Christian) and the blood stops before ten days, then without performing ghusl and without a time of prayer passing, merely by the cessation of blood her raj'ah is severed, because in her right there is no expectation of any additional sign for the end of menstruation. Since prayer is not obligatory upon the kitabiyya nor ghusl, therefore mere cessation sufficed. And if a woman under raj'ah the blood of the third menstruation stops before ten days, then she performs tayammum and prays, whether obligatory or voluntary, then according to the two shaykhs the raj'ah is severed. That is, the severance of raj'ah occurs by both tayammum and prayer, and this ruling is istihsan. And Imam Muhammad says: If she performed tayammum, then merely performing tayammum severs the raj'ah. Imam Zufar and Imam Ahmad hold this view, and this is qiyas. The proof of Imam Muhammad is that tayammum when unable to use water is absolute purity, so all the rulings that are established from ghusl are established from tayammum, such as entering the mosque, reciting the Quran, touching the Quran, performing prayer, and performing the prostration of recitation. Thus tayammum became like the rank of ghusl. Therefore, whatever ruling was for ghusl, the same ruling is for tayammum. And the proof of the two shaykhs is that the reality of tayammum is contaminating, not purifying, but the Shari'ah has considered it as purifying out of necessity. The necessity is that if for some days he does not have power over water and the Shari'ah did not permit tayammum, then obligations and duties would multiply upon the person, making their performance difficult. Therefore, tayammum is legislated due to this necessity, and the necessity is realized at the time of performing the prayer, not before it. So it became clear that if after tayammum the prayer is performed, then purity is attained by tayammum; otherwise not. For this reason we said: If she performed tayammum and then prayed, then due to the attainment of purity the ruling of raj'ah is severed; and if she did not pray, then due to the non-attainment of purity the ruling of raj'ah is not severed. The objection to Imam Muhammad's principle (that the rulings established from ghusl are also established from tayammum) from the phrase 'and the established rulings' is answered. The summary of the answer is that the establishment of these rulings from tayammum is due to the necessity for prayer. Thus, for the permissibility of prayer, recitation of the Quran is necessary because the recitation of the Quran is a pillar of prayer; and the mosque because it is the place of prayer; and the prostration of recitation because it is among the accessory parts of recitation, since it is possible that the worshipper may recite a verse of prostration during prayer; and the touching of the Quran is necessary because if he forgets the amount that makes prayer valid before reciting, this person will need to open the Quran and look, and it is obvious that this cannot be done without touching the mushaf. Some people have objected to the proof of the two shaykhs. The objection is that tayammum is a necessary purification, and necessity is realized at the time of performing prayer, not before it, and there is also the established principle that 'what is established by necessity does not extend beyond its place.' So the requirement of this principle would be that the ruling of raj'ah should not be severed by tayammum even if the woman prayed after tayammum, until she performs ghusl or a time of prayer passes upon her. The answer: Undoubtedly, 'what is established by necessity does not extend beyond its place' is a principle, but there is also the principle that 'when something is established by necessity, it is established with all its necessary consequences.' So at the time of performing prayer, the attainment of purity (taharah) is established, and from its necessary consequences is the cessation of menstruation, and from the necessary consequences of the completion of the 'iddah is the severance of raj'ah, and the rule is that the necessary of a necessary is necessary. Therefore, at the time of performing prayer, the ruling of severance of raj'ah is established by the establishment of purity. (From 'Inayah, as explained). Then, some people say that according to the two shaykhs the ruling of raj'ah is severed as soon as prayer is begun, and some hold the view that it is severed after finishing the prayer so that the ruling of permissibility of prayer becomes established. This is the correct saying, because the state after beginning prayer is like the state before beginning; thus if during prayer he sees water and has the ability to use it, the effect of tayammum does not remain. Unlike after finishing the prayer.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the termination of the 'iddah (waiting period) and the effect of tayammum on the right of return (raj'ah) in the context of the chapter on divorce of the sick. The text begins by stating the general ruling: for a Muslim woman in her third menstruation, if the blood stops after ten full days, the 'iddah ends immediately even without ghusl, because menstruation cannot exceed ten days. If the blood stops before ten days, the 'iddah does not end until she performs ghusl or a complete prayer time passes (so that she becomes obliged to pray). For a Kitabiyyah (Jewish or Christian woman), since prayer is not obligatory, mere cessation suffices. The central dispute arises when a woman performs tayammum during her 'iddah. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn), tayammum is not a complete purification; it is only considered purifying out of necessity for prayer. Therefore, the right of return is severed only after she performs tayammum and then prays (either during or after the prayer). Imam Muhammad holds that tayammum in the absence of water is absolute purity, so it alone severs the right of return. The commentary then presents the proofs: Imam Muhammad relies on qiyas—since tayammum substitutes for ghusl, all rulings of ghusl apply. Shaykhayn rely on istihsan—tayammum's reality is contaminating, but Shari'ah allows it only to avoid hardship in performing obligations. The necessity only applies at the time of prayer, so purification is only attained when prayer is performed. The text then addresses an objection: if tayammum's effect is limited to prayer necessity, it should not affect the 'iddah even after prayer. The answer invokes the principle that when something is established by necessity, it is established with all its necessary consequences. Thus, when purity is established at the time of prayer, its consequences—including the end of menstruation and 'iddah—follow. Finally, there is a difference within the Shaykhayn's own position: whether the raj'ah ends at the start of prayer or after completion. The preferred view is after completion, because during prayer the tayammum can still be invalidated if water becomes available.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using clean earth or dust, performed in the absence of water or when water is harmful.
رجعت (raj'ah): The right of a husband to take back his wife during the 'iddah after a revocable (raj'i) divorce without a new marriage contract.
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before she can remarry.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that gives preference to the stronger, more appropriate ruling over the apparent analogy (qiyas).
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause ('illah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn), when does the right of return (raj'ah) terminate for a woman who performs tayammum during her 'iddah?
A) Immediately upon performing tayammum
B) Only after she performs prayer with that tayammum
C) When she performs ghusl with water
D) When she completes one full day without menstruation

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, tayammum alone does not end the 'iddah; prayer must follow because tayammum's purifying effect is limited to prayer necessity (mufta bihi position of Shaykhayn).

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
When a Dry Limb Affects Ruj'ah: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istihsan vs qiyas regarding ruj'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ruj'ah when a part of the body is left dry in ghusl, explain the istihsan reasoning, and compare the qiyas positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas when certainty is impossible; a dry limb leaves ruj'ah intact, a dry spot cuts it.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah tackles a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens to a woman's right of return (ruj'ah) if she forgets to wash a part of her body during ghusl after hayd? The answer depends on whether the unwashed area is a full limb or less. Understanding the interplay between qiyas and istihsan is key to grasping the Hanafi approach to legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base situation
A woman in 'iddah after a revocable divorce performs ghusl after hayd ends but forgets to wash a part of her body. Determine the nature of the unwashed part: is it a complete limb (e.g., hand, foot) or less than a limb (e.g., a spot on the finger)?
The ruling depends on this distinction.
2
State the relied-upon ruling (istihsan)
According to the Hidayah, if the unwashed part is a complete limb or more, ruj'ah remains valid. If it is less than a limb, ruj'ah is cut – she cannot take back her husband and may not marry another until a new 'iddah or marriage. This ruling is based on istihsan.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Trace the qiyas arguments of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Abu Yusuf's qiyas: For a complete limb left dry, she washed the majority, so ruj'ah should be cut. For less than a limb, the majority is washed but the remaining impurity is negligible? Actually his qiyas also says ruj'ah remains? Wait: the text says Abu Yusuf's qiyas: for a complete limb, ruj'ah cut; for less than a limb, ruj'ah remains. Muhammad's qiyas: for a complete limb, ruj'ah cut; for less than a limb, ruj'ah remains. They both reach the same conclusion but for different reasons? Actually the text states: 'Abu Yusuf: for a complete limb, qiyas would cut ruj'ah; for less than a limb, qiyas would leave ruj'ah. Muhammad: for a complete limb, qiyas cuts ruj'ah; for less than a limb, qiyas leaves ruj'ah.' So both agree on the qiyas outcome, but the istihsan gives the opposite. The imams' qiyas differs in reasoning: Abu Yusuf uses 'majority takes the ruling of the whole' (akthar yanzilu manzilat al-kull) for limb case; Muhammad uses 'indivisibility of hadath' for less than limb case. Confirm with source.
The key point is that both imams' qiyas would produce rulings opposite to istihsan.
4
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Less than a limb dries quickly, so it is uncertain whether water actually reached it – she might have washed it but it dried. To avoid the risk of intercourse during 'iddah without full purity, we rule that ruj'ah is cut (precaution). For a limb, drying is slow and one is usually heedful, so certainty of non-washing exists, thus ruj'ah remains.
The istihsan is based on practical certainty (yaqin) and precaution (ihtiyat).
5
Apply to madmadah/istinshaq
The passage discusses the case of leaving madmadah (mouth rinse) and istinshaq (sniffing water). Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one treats them as a complete limb (ruj'ah remains), the other as less than a limb (ruj'ah cut). Muhammad agrees with the second. The reason: there is disagreement among schools on whether these acts are obligatory (fard) in ghusl. This variation creates uncertainty, so they are treated like less than a limb.
The second narration (with Muhammad) is likely the stronger position.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
عورت نے غسل کر لیا اور بدن کے کسی عضو پر پانی پہنچانا بھول گئی اگر عضو کامل یا ایک عضو سے زیادہ پر پانی نہیں پہنچار جوع کا حق منقطع نہیں ہوگا اور اگر ایک عضو سے کم ہے منقطع ہو جائے گا
واذا اغتسلت ونسيت شيئا من بدنهالم يصبه الماء فان كان عضوا فما فوقه لم تنقطع الرجعة وان كان اقل من عضو انقطعت قال وهذا استحسان والقياس فى العضو الكامل ان لا تبقى الرجعة لانها غسلت الاكثر والقياس فيما دون العضوان تبقى لان حكم الجنابة والحيض لايتجزى ووجه الاستحسان وهو الفرق ان مادون العضو يتسارع اليه الجفاف لقلته فلايتيقن بعدم وصول الماء اليه فقلنا انه تنقطع الرجعة ولا تحل لها التزوج اخذا بالاحتياط فيهما بخلاف العضو الكامل لانه لا يتسارع اليه الجفوف ولا يغفل عنه عادة فافتر قاو عن أبي يوسف ان ترك المضمضة والاستنشاق کترک عضو کامل و عنه وهو قول محمد بمنزلة مادون العضولان فى فرضيته اختلافا بخلاف غيره من الاعضاء
ترجمہ اور اگر عورت نے غسل کیا، حالانکہ اپنے بدن میں سے ایسا کوئی جن بھول گئی جس کو پانی پہنچا ہے۔ پس اگر وہ جزا ایک عضو ہے یا اس سے زائد تو رجعت منقطع نہیں ہوگی اور اگر ایک عضو سے کم چھوٹا ہے تو رجعت منقطع ہوگئی ۔ مصنف نے کہا کہ یہ استحسان ہے اور پورے عضو میں قیاس یہ ہے کہ رجعت ( کا حکم ) باقی نہ رہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے (بدن کا ) اکثر ( حصہ ) دھولیا ہے اور ایک عضو سے کم میں قیاس یہ ہے کہ ( رجعت کا حکم ) باقی رہے کیونکہ جنابت اور حیض کا حکم منجزی اور ٹکڑے ٹکڑے نہیں ہوتا ہے اور وجہ استحسان اور وہی فرق ہے یہ ہے کہ عضو سے کم کو اس کی قلت کی وجہ سے خشکی بہت جلد آ جاتی ہے۔ پس اس تک پانی نہ پہنچنے کا یقین نہیں ہو سکتا ہے تو ہم نے حکم دیا کہ رجعت منقطع ہو جائے گی اور اس عورت کے لئے ( دوسرے شوہر سے) نکاح کرنا بھی حلال نہیں ہے۔ دونوں میں احتیاط پر عمل کرتے ہوئے ۔ برخلاف پورے عضو کے۔ کیونکہ اس کی طرف خشکی جلدی نہیں آتی اور اس سے عاد تا غافل بھی نہیں رہتا۔ ( پس عضو کامل اور جزء عضو میں ) فرق واضح ہو گیا اور ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ کلی کرنے اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنے کا چھوٹ جانا ایسا ہے جیسے پورے عضو کا چھوٹ جانا اور ابو یوسف سے ایک روایت اور یہی امام محمد کا قول ہے کہ عضو سے کم کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ کلی کرنے اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنے کی فرضیت میں اختلاف ہے۔ برخلاف دیگر اعضاء کے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر دس روز سے کم میں خون منقطع ہونے کے بعد عورت نے غسل کیا۔ حالانکہ بدن میں سے کوئی ایسا جز بھول گئی جس کو پانی نہیں پہنچا تو اگر وہ جزء ایک عضو یا اس سے بڑھ کر ہے تو رجعت منقطع نہیں ہوگی ۔ یعنی تقسل نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے عدت باقی ہے۔ پس اگر ایسی حالت میں مراجعت کر لی تو صحیح ہوگی اور اگر وہ جز ایک عضو سے کم ہے تو رجعت منقطع ہو جائے گی ۔ یعنی ایسی حالت میں رجعت صحیح نہیں ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ حکم استحسانا ہے اور قیاس کا تقاضا اس کے برعکس ہے یعنی عضو کامل میں رجعت باقی نہ رہنی چاہیے اور مادون العضو میں رجعت باقی رہنی چاہیے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا کہ امام محمد نے اپنی کتابوں میں یہ ذکر نہیں کیا کہ محل قیاس کیا ہے عضو کامل ہے یا مادون العضو ہے ۔ البتہ یہ روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک محل قیاس عضو اور مافوق العضو ہے چنانچہ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ عضو کامل میں قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ رجعت باقی نہ رہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت نے اپنے اکثر بدن کو دھولیا ہے اور قاعدہ ہے للاكثر حکم الکل یعنی اکثر کل کے حکم میں ہوتا ہے۔ تو گویا پانی جمیع بدن کو پہنچ گیا ہے اور جب پانی جمیع بدن کو پہنچ گیا ہے تو عدت گزرگئی اور عدت کے گزر جانے کے بعد رجعت کا حکم باقی نہیں رہتا اس لئے قیاس کا مشخصی یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں رجعت باقی نہ رہے اور استحسان یہ ہے کہ عضو یا ما فوق العضو خشک رہ جانے کی صورت میں رجعت منقطع نہ ہو ۔ کیونکہ عدم طہارت کی وجہ سے عدت باقی ہے اور عدت میں رجعت کا حکم باقی رہتا ہے۔
اور امام محمد کے نزدیک محل قیاس ما دون العضو ہے۔ چنانچہ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ مادون العضو میں قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ رجعت باقی رہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مادون العضو خشک رہنے کی صورت میں بھی حدث باقی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جنابت اور حیض کا حکم متجری اور ٹکڑے ٹکڑے نہیں ہوتا پس جب ایک جز میں حدث باقی ہے اگر چہ مادون العضو ہے تو ہم کہیں گے کہ پورے بدن میں حدث ہے اور جب پورے بدن میں حدث ( حیض) باقی ہے تو عدت باقی ہے اور جب عدت باقی ہے تو رجعت کا حکم بھی باقی ہے۔ اور وجہ استحسان اور یہی عضو کامل اور مادون العضو میں وجہ فرق ہے کہ عضو سے کم قلت کی وجہ سے بہت جلد خشک ہو جاتا ہے تو اس حصہ تک پانی نہ پہنچنے کا یقین نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس حصہ کو دھویا ہومگر جلد ہی خشک ہو گیا اس لئے ہم نے احتیاط پر عمل کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ رجعت کا حکم منقطع ہو گیا اور احتیاط ہی کے پیش نظر یہ حکم ہے کہ یہ عورت ایسی حالت میں دوسرے شوہر سے نکاح نہ کرے اگر کر لیا تو حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ اس حصہ تک حقیقتا پانی نہ پہنچا ہو اور حدث باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے عدت باقی ہو تو ایسی صورت میں یہ نکاح معتدة الغیر کے ساتھ ہوگا اور یہ نا جائز ہے۔
اس کے برخلاف اگر عضو کامل خشک رہا تو رجعت کا حکم منقطع نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عضو کامل بہت جلد خشک نہیں ہوتا اور عادتا عضو کامل سے انسان غافل بھی نہیں رہتا۔ لہذا یہی کہا جائے گا کہ ابھی تک اس حصہ کو دھویا نہیں گیا اور جب ایسا ہے تو غسل نا مکمل ہونے کی وجہ سے عدت باقی ہے اور عدت میں رجعت کا حکم باقی رہتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس صورت میں حکم رجعت منقطع نہیں ہو گا ۔ پس عضو کامل اور مادون العضو میں فرق واضح ہو گیا۔ اور اگر دس روز سے کم میں کوئی عورت تیسرے حیض سے فارغ ہوئی اور غسل کر لیا لیکن کی کرنا یا ناک میں پانی ڈالنا چھوڑ دیا تو اس میں امام ابو یوسف سے دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک روایت میں ہے کہ رجعت منقطع نہیں ہوگی۔ جیسا کہ عضو کامل کو چھوڑ نے سے رجعت منقطع نہیں ہوتی۔ اس روایت کے مطابق کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا ان میں سے ہر ایک عضو کامل کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف سے اس کو ہشام نے روایت کیا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف سے دوسری روایت جس کو امام کرخی نے روایت کیا یہ ہے کہ رجعت منقطع ہو جائے گی اور کلی کرنے یا ناک میں پانی ڈالنے کو چھوڑنا مادون العضو کو چھوڑنے کے مانند ہے۔ کیونکہ غسل میں کلی کرنے اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنے کی فرضیت میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا غسل اور وضو دونوں میں سنت ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک غسل میں فرض اور وضو میں سنت ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف دوسرے اعضاء کہ ان کی فرضیت میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں۔ یہ دوسری روایت امام محمد کا بھی قول ہے۔
And if she performed ghusl and forgot something of her body that water did not reach, then if it was a limb or more, the return (ruj'ah) is not cut; and if it was less than a limb, it is cut. He said: This is istihsan. And the qiyas regarding the complete limb: that the return does not remain, because she washed the majority. And the qiyas regarding less than a limb: that it remains, because the ruling of janabah and hayd is not divisible. And the aspect of istihsan, which is the difference: that less than a limb dries quickly due to its small amount, so one is not certain of water not reaching it. So we said that the return is cut, and it is not permissible for her to marry, taking precaution in both. Unlike the complete limb, because it does not dry quickly and one is not usually heedless of it. So they differed. From Abu Yusuf: that leaving madmadah and istinshaq is like leaving a complete limb. And from him (another narration), and it is the saying of Muhammad: it is in the position of less than a limb, because there is disagreement on its fardiyyah, unlike other limbs.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of leaving a part of the body unwashed during ghusl on the right of return (ruj'ah) for a woman in her 'iddah period after a revocable divorce. The base ruling (from the Hidayah) states: if a woman performs ghusl after her hayd ends within ten days, but forgets to wash a part of her body, if the unwashed part is a complete limb or more, her ruj'ah is not cut (ruj'ah remains valid). If the unwashed part is less than a limb, then her ruj'ah is cut (she cannot take back her husband during that 'iddah). The author (al-Marghinani) clarifies that this ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas (analogy) would suggest the opposite: for a complete limb left dry, the woman has washed the majority of her body, and the principle 'al-akthar yanzilu manzilat al-kull' (the majority takes the ruling of the whole) applies, so the ghusl would be complete and 'iddah would end, cutting ruj'ah. For less than a limb, since the ruling of janabah/hayd is indivisible, any remaining impurity should mean the whole body is impure, so 'iddah continues and ruj'ah should remain. However, istihsan departs from qiyas due to a practical difference: less than a limb dries quickly, so it is uncertain whether water actually reached it; a woman might have washed it but it dried. To be cautious, we rule that ruj'ah is cut (so she cannot claim return unless certain), and also forbid her from marrying another. For a whole limb, it does not dry quickly and one is not usually heedless, so certainty of non-washing is high; thus ruj'ah remains. Then the passage presents a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the specific case of leaving madmadah (mouth rinsing) and istinshaq (sniffing water) during ghusl. Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one equates leaving them to leaving a complete limb (ruj'ah not cut); the other equates them to less than a limb (ruj'ah cut). Muhammad agrees with the second. The reason for the difference is that there is a dispute (among schools) on whether madmadah and istinshaq are fard (obligatory) in ghusl. In the Hanafi school, they are fard in ghusl but sunnah in wudu. This variation in obligation creates uncertainty, so they are treated like less than a limb. Other limbs are unquestionably fard.

Key Terms
رجعت (ruj'ah): The right of a husband to take back his wife during her 'iddah period after a revocable divorce without a new marriage contract.
عضو کامل (‘udw kamil): A complete limb, such as a hand, foot, or forearm. The passage distinguishes it from less than a limb (mā dūn al-‘udw).
مادون العضو (mā dūn al-‘udw): Less than a limb, e.g., a finger or a small area. Due to its small size, it dries quickly, creating uncertainty.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference deviating from qiyas due to a stronger consideration, here the precaution against uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (istihsan) in this passage, what is the effect on ruj'ah if a woman in 'iddah forgets to wash less than a limb during ghusl?
A) Ruj'ah remains valid because the ruling of hayd is indivisible.
B) Ruj'ah is cut because of the uncertainty of water reaching that part.
C) Ruj'ah remains valid because the majority was washed.
D) Ruj'ah is cut only if the unwashed part is a complete limb.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when practical certainty is unattainable, istihsan overrides qiyas to achieve precaution; for ruj'ah, a dry limb leaves it intact, a dry spot cuts it.
