Second Birth as Raj'ah in Conditional Divorce
Ruling on conditional divorce with multiple births

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a second birth after a conditional divorce linked to the first birth is a valid raj'ah and explain the qiyas proof that establishes it.

Core Idea
The second birth after a conditional divorce is a revocation, not a new divorce, because it indicates cohabitation during iddah.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from Al-Hidayah on conditional divorce linked to childbirth. The passage clarifies that if a husband declares, 'When you give birth, you are divorced,' and the wife later gives birth to a second child, that second birth is legally interpreted as the husband's revocation of the divorce (raj'ah). This ruling is derived through qiyas khafi (hidden analogy), linking the birth to presumed intercourse during the iddah period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The husband says 'When you give birth, you are divorced.' The wife gives birth to a first child, then later a second child. The ruling: the second birth is a raj'ah (revocation), not a new divorce.
This applies only if the second child is from a different pregnancy (another womb) and born at least six months after the first.
2
Understand the condition for raj'ah
The second birth is considered raj'ah as long as the wife does not affirm that her iddah (waiting period) has expired. The iddah begins with the first divorce (first birth).
Even if more than two years pass, as long as she doesn't admit iddah ended, the presumption holds.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogical reasoning)
Asl: A revocably divorced woman who has intercourse with her husband during iddah — this establishes raj'ah. Far': The wife gives birth to a second child after the first birth-triggered divorce. Illa (effective cause): The presence of a second child indicates cohabitation during the iddah, because the child is presumed to be conceived from that intercourse. Conclusion: Raj'ah is established.
This is qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because the cohabitation is inferred from the birth, not directly observed.
4
Note the evidentiary presumption
The law presumes that the second child is from the husband's intercourse during the iddah, since the wife does not confirm the iddah's expiry. This presumption is key to the ruling.
If the wife admitted iddah ended, the reasoning would change.
5
Summarize the proof structure
The ruling combines textual evidence (the conditional divorce) and analogical reasoning (qiyas) to establish that the second birth operates as raj'ah. The proof lies in the logical inference that a child born later must have been conceived during the iddah, thus implying intercourse which revokes the divorce.
This demonstrates how Hanafi fiqh uses qiyas to extend rulings to new cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قال لها اذا ولدت فانت طالق فولدت ثم اتت بولد أخر فهى رجعة معناه من بطن آخر وهو ان يكون بعد ستة اشهروان كان اكثر من سنتين أذا لم تقر بانقضاء العدة لانه وقع الطلاق عليها بالولد الاول ووجبت العدة فيكون الولد الثانى من علوق حادث منه فى العدة لانهالم تقربا نقضاء العدة فيصير مراجعا
ترجمہ لپس اگر مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا اذا ولدت فانت طالق ۔ پھر اس نے بچہ جنا پھر دوسرا بچہ لائی تو یہ ولادت ثانیہ رجعت ہے۔ اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ ( دوسرا بچہ ) طن آخر سے ہو اور بطن آخر یہ ہے کہ چھ ماہ کے بعد ہو ۔ اگر چہ دو سال سے زیادہ ہو جب تک کہ عورت نے عدت گزرنے کا اقرار نہیں کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس پر دلد اول سے طلاق واقع ہوگئی اور عدت واجب ہو گئی ۔ پس ولید ثانی ایسے علوق سے ہو گا جو شوہر سے عورت کی عدت میں پیدا ہوا۔ کیونکہ عورت نے عدت گزرنے کا اقرار نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس وہ (شومر ) رجعت کرنے والا ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا ذا ولدت فانت طالق ۔ پس اس نے ایک بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ پھر دوسرا بچہ چھ ماہ کے بعد پیدا ہوا تو یہ دوسرے بچہ کا پیدا ہوتار جمعت ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ دونوں بچوں کے درمیان چھ ماہ کا فاصلہ ہے برابر ہے کہ ولادت ثانیہ دو سال سے کم میں ہو یا دو سال سے زیادہ میں دونوں صورتوں میں رجعت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ پہلے بچہ کی ولادت سے اس عورت پر طلاق ہوئی اور عدت واجب ہوگئی ۔ پس دوسرے بچہ کی ولادت کے بارے میں کہا جائے گا کہ شوہر نے عدت کے زمانے میں اس عورت سے جماع کیا تھا اس کے نتیجے میں یہ دوسرا بچہ پیدا ہوا ہے اور عورت نے عدت گزرنے کا اقرار بھی نہیں کیا ہے ۔ پس یہ شخص مطلقہ رعیہ کے ساتھ اس کی عدت میں جماع کرنے کی وجہ سے رجعت کرنے والا شمار ہوگا ۔
If he said to her, 'When you give birth, you are divorced,' and she gave birth then brought another child, then it (the second birth) is a raj'ah, meaning from another womb, and that is after six months, even if more than two years, as long as she does not affirm that the iddah has expired. Because the divorce occurred upon her with the first child and the iddah became obligatory, so the second child is from a recent cohabitation by him during the iddah, because she did not affirm the expiration of the iddah, so he becomes a revoker.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Al-Hidayah on conditional divorce linked to childbirth, expanded by the Urdu commentary. The ruling: If a man tells his wife, 'When you give birth, you are divorced,' and she gives birth to a child, then later another child is born, the second birth is considered a raj'ah (revocation of divorce) by the husband. This is provided the second child is from a different pregnancy (another womb) and is born at least six months after the first, even if more than two years have passed, as long as the wife does not admit that her iddah has ended. The reasoning: The first birth triggers the divorce and starts the iddah. The second child is presumed to be conceived from a cohabitation by the husband during the iddah, because the wife does not confirm the iddah's expiry. This cohabitation constitutes a revocation (raj'ah). The Urdu clarifies that if she bears a second child after six months, it is a sign of raj'ah, regardless of whether it happens within two years or later. The proof (dalil) is based on this presumption: the first birth caused divorce and iddah; the second birth indicates intercourse during iddah, which establishes raj'ah.

Key Terms
رجعة (rajʿah): The revocation of a revocable divorce by the husband during the iddah period, by word or action.
عدة (ʿiddah): The waiting period after divorce or death, during which remarriage is prohibited and paternity is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a second divorce.
B) It is a revocation (raj'ah) of the first divorce.
C) It is evidence that the iddah has expired.
D) It has no legal effect.

Key Takeaway
The second birth after a conditional divorce is a revocation (raj'ah), not a new divorce, as it indicates cohabitation during the iddah.

Conditional Divorce with 'Kullama' and Multiple Births
Ruling on repetitive conditional divorce with multiple births and interposing raj'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of divorce and raj'ah when a husband uses 'kullama' in a conditional divorce and the wife bears children from separate pregnancies.

Core Idea
Kullama repeats both condition and consequence; each birth triggers a divorce but proves intercourse during iddah, establishing raj'ah before the next divorce.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Al-Hidayah where a husband conditions divorce on each childbirth using 'kullama' (whenever). The wife gives birth to three children from distinct pregnancies. We will see how the first birth initiates divorce, the second birth both confirms raj'ah (via presumed intercourse) and triggers the next divorce, and so on. The key is the interplay between the conditional particle kullama and the evidential value of a child born after six months.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and condition
The husband says: 'Whenever you give birth to a child, you are divorced.' The wife subsequently gives birth to three children from separate wombs (pregnancies), each at least six months apart. Note that each birth is a separate occurrence of the condition.
The condition is phrased using 'kullama', which in Hanafi usul implies repetition of both condition and consequence.
2
Determine the ruling for the first birth
The first birth triggers the first divorce (talaq) immediately. The wife enters the iddah of a revocable divorce.
No ambiguity: the condition is satisfied and the consequence follows.
3
Analyse the second birth – establish raj'ah
The birth of a child after at least six months from the first birth is evidence (qarīna) that the husband had intercourse with her during the iddah. This intercourse constitutes a valid raj'ah (revocation) of the first divorce. Therefore, just before the second birth occurs, the marriage is restored.
The qiyas: the original case is a revocable divorcee who has intercourse during iddah – that establishes raj'ah. The new case is the birth of a second child – the effective cause is the evidence of intercourse.
4
Apply the consequence of the second birth
Immediately after the raj'ah, the second birth itself occurs. Since the condition (kullama) is once again fulfilled, the second divorce takes effect. The wife is now in the iddah of a second revocable divorce.
The temporal order: raj'ah precedes the birth, but the birth triggers the divorce.
5
Repeat for the third birth
The third birth follows the same pattern: the birth after six months indicates intercourse during the second iddah, leading to raj'ah, and then the birth triggers the third and final divorce. After the third divorce, the iddah is observed by menstruation because the woman is no longer pregnant.
After three divorces, the woman becomes forbidden (harām) to the husband until she marries another and is divorced (tahlīl).

Source Text

ترجمہ او را گر مرد نے کہا جب جب تو نے بچہ جنا تو تو طالقہ ہے۔ پس اس نے مختلف تین بطون میں تین بچے بنے تو پہلا بچہ طلاق ہے اور دوسرا بچہ رجعت ہے اور ایسے ہی تیسرا بچہ۔ کیونکہ وہ جب پہلا بچہ لائی تو طلاق واقع ہوگئی اور معتدہ ہوگئی اور دوسرے بچہ سے وہ رجعت کرنے والا ہو گیا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے کہ علوق ایسی ولی سے قرار پائے گا جو عدت کے اندر واقع ہوئی اور دوسرے بچہ کی ولادت سے دوسری طلاق واقع ہوگی کیونکہ یمین کلمہ کلما کے ساتھ منعقد کی گئی ہے اور عدت واجب ہوگئی اور تیسرے بچہ کے ساتھ وہ مراجعہ کرنے والا ہو گیا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور تیسرے بچہ کی ولادت سے تیسری طلاق واقع ہوگی اور عدت واجب ہوئی حیضوں کے ساتھ کیونکہ یہ عورت حاملہ وقوع طلاق کے وقت ذوات الحیض میں سے ہے۔

And if he said, 'Whenever you give birth to a child, you are divorced,' and she gave birth to three children in different wombs, then the first child is a divorce, and the second child is a raj'ah, and similarly the third. Because when she brought the first child, the divorce occurred and she became a woman in iddah. And with the second child, he becomes a revoker, as we explained, that the pregnancy is attributed to recent intercourse during the iddah. And the second divorce occurs by the birth of the second child because the oath is tied with the word 'kullama' and the iddah became obligatory. And with the third child, he becomes a revoker for the reason we mentioned, and the third divorce occurs by the birth of the third child, and the iddah becomes obligatory by menstruation because she was pregnant, and she is among those who menstruate at the time the divorce occurred.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Al-Hidayah on a conditional divorce using the word 'kullama' (whenever), expanded by the Urdu commentary. The scenario: A husband says, 'Whenever you give birth to a child, you are divorced.' The wife bears three children from separate pregnancies (at least six months apart). The ruling: The first birth triggers the first divorce and she enters iddah. The second child, being born after a minimum interval of six months, indicates that the husband had intercourse with her during the iddah. This intercourse constitutes a raj'ah (revocation) of the first divorce. However, immediately after the raj'ah, the birth of the second child itself triggers the second divorce, due to the word 'kullama' which repeats the condition. The same sequence occurs with the third child: raj'ah before birth, then third divorce upon birth. After the third divorce, the iddah is observed by menstruation (three cycles) because the woman was pregnant at the time of the third divorce but now is no longer pregnant (since the child is born). The proof is based on the presumption that a child born after six months from the previous birth is from intercourse during the iddah, and the word 'kullama' requires repetition of both condition and consequence.

Key Terms
كلما (kullamā): Every time; used as a conditional particle requiring repetition of the consequence upon each occurrence of the condition.
بطن (baṭn): A pregnancy or womb; here meaning a separate gestation period between births.

Key Takeaway
The word 'kullama' in a conditional divorce causes each birth to trigger both a raj'ah (via the presumption of intercourse during iddah) and a new divorce, leading to a maximum of three divorces.

Adornment After Revocable Divorce and Limitations on the Husband
Ruling on adornment and husband's conduct during revocable divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissibility of adornment for a revocably divorced woman and distinguish between the majority Hanafi view and Zufar's view regarding travel during iddah.

Core Idea
In revocable divorce, the marriage remains; the wife may adorn herself to encourage revocation, and the husband may not travel with her without declaring revocation.

This lesson from Al-Hidayah clarifies that a woman in revocable divorce (talaq rajʿi) is still legally the husband's wife. The text permits her to beautify herself, as this encourages the husband to revoke the divorce. It also addresses the husband's conduct: he should not enter unexpectedly, and he cannot travel with her without witnessing the revocation. The passage includes a minority opinion from Zufar, who allows travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The revocably divorced woman may adorn herself. The reason is that the marriage is still valid and revocation is recommended; adornment incites him to revoke.
The hukm is mubah (permissible) or even mustahab (recommended) as a means to the recommended act of revocation.
2
Analyze the husband's restrictions
The husband should not enter upon her without announcement or without making his presence known, and he may not travel with her until he witnesses (declares) his revocation. This is to avoid accidental revocation that could lead to complications.
The restriction on entry is a recommendation (istihbab), while the prohibition on travel without witnessing is stronger.
3
Examine Zufar's objection
Zufar (a Hanafi disciple) argues that the husband may travel with her because the marriage contract still exists, so she remains his wife.
Zufar's view represents a minority intra-Hanafi opinion.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) responds with Quran 65:1, which prohibits expelling them from their homes – travel is akin to expulsion. Also, if the husband does not revoke until the iddah ends, it shows there was no need to revoke, so the divorce took effect from its occurrence.
The verse is interpreted as a general prohibition of removal, including travel without revocation.
5
Determine the practical difference
Under Zufar's view, the husband could travel with her without witnessing revocation; under the majority view, he cannot. This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence of the dispute).
The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) is the majority view.

والمطلقة الرجعية تتشبوف وتتزين لانها جلال للزوج اذالنكاح قائم بينهماثم الرجعة مستحبة والتزين حامل عليها فيكون مشروعا ويستجب لزوجها ان لايدخل عليها حتى يوذنها او يسمعها خفق نعليه معناه اذالم تكن من قصده المراجعة لانهار بما تكون مجردة فيقع بصره على موضع يصير به مراجعا ثم يطلقها فتطول عليه العدة وليس له ان يسافر بها حتى يشهد على رجعتها وقال زفر له ذلك لقيام النكاح ولهذاله ان يغشاها عندنا ولنا قوله تعالى ولا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن الآية ولان تراخي عمل المبطل لحاجته الى المراجعة فاذا لم يراجعها حتى انقضت المدة ظهر انه لاحاجة فتبين ان المبطل عمل عمله من وقت وجوده ولهذا تحتسب الاقراء من العدة و يتقرر ملك الزوج وقوله حتى يشهد على رجعتها معناه الاستحباب على ما قدمناه
ترجمہ اور مطلقہ رجعیہ (اپنے آپ کو) آراستہ کرے اور مزین کرے کیونکہ یہ عورت اپنے شوہر کے واسطے حلال ہے۔ اس لئے کہ نکاح دونوں میں قائم ہے۔ پھر رجعت کرنا مستحب ہے اور عورت کا سنگار اس پر آمادہ کرنے والا ہے۔ اسلئے سنگار مشروع ہوگا اور اس کے شوہر کے لئے
And the revocably divorced woman adorns herself and beautifies herself because she is permissible for the husband, since the marriage is established between them. Then the revocation is recommended, and beautification incites him to it, so it is legislated. And it is recommended for the husband not to enter upon her until he announces to her or she hears the sound of his sandals, meaning if he does not intend the revocation, because she may be sitting alone, and his gaze may fall on a place that makes him revoke, then he divorces her, and his iddah becomes long. And he may not travel with her until he witnesses his revocation. And Zufar said he may, due to the marriage contract existing. And he has the right to have intercourse with her in our school. And our proof is the saying of Allah, 'Do not expel them from their houses' (65:1), and because the action of the one who invalidates is delayed due to his need for revocation. So if he does not revoke her until the period ends, it becomes clear that there is no need, so it becomes evident that the invalidating action occurred from the time of its occurrence. For this reason, the menstruations are counted from the iddah and the husband's ownership is established. And his saying 'until he witnesses his revocation' means recommendation as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Al-Hidayah on the permissibility of a revocably divorced woman adorning herself, along with guidelines for the husband. It includes a dispute with Zufar. The ruling: A woman in revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) may beautify herself, as the marriage is still valid and revocation is recommended. Adornment encourages the husband to revoke, so it is legislated. The husband should not enter upon her without permission or without making his presence known by the sound of his shoes, unless he intends to revoke. This is to avoid an accidental gaze that might lead to a hasty revocation followed by another divorce, prolonging the iddah. He may not travel with her unless he witnesses (declares) his revocation. Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) differs, allowing travel because the marriage contract still exists. The Hanafi response: The wife may not be taken out of the marital home per Quran 65:1. Also, if the husband delays revocation and the iddah expires, it shows he did not intend to revoke, so the original divorcing action stands. The iddah is completed by three menstruations. The phrase 'witnesses his revocation' is interpreted as recommended, not required. The Urdu commentary briefly repeats the ruling.

Key Terms
مطلقة رجعية (muṭallaqah rajʿiyyah): A woman divorced with one or two revocable divorces, who is still in her iddah and can be taken back without a new contract.
تتشوف (tatashawwaf): To adorn oneself, beautify.
تزين (tazayyun): To adorn, decorate, beautify.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Obtains her consent.
D) Pays her deferred dower (mahr).

Key Takeaway
A revocably divorced woman remains permissible to her husband during iddah; she may adorn herself, and he must not travel with her without formally declaring the revocation.

Conditional Divorce with 'كلما' and Multiple Births
Explains ruling of conditional divorce with three successive births

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a conditional divorce using the word 'كلما' and explain the sequence of divorces and revocable returns in the case of multiple births.

Core Idea
With 'كلما', each birth triggers a divorce, but a revocable return occurs before the next birth via intercourse during iddah.

This passage addresses a classic scenario in Hanafi divorce law: a husband conditionally divorces his wife 'whenever' she gives birth. Because the word 'كلما' implies repetition, each birth results in a separate divorce. However, the husband's revocable return (رجعت) through intercourse during the waiting period intervenes, so the divorces do not accumulate without opportunity for reconciliation. Understanding this ruling clarifies how conditional statements interact with the rules of iddah and ruju'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional phrase and its implication
The husband says 'كلما ولدت ولدا فانت طالق'. The word 'كلما' indicates that the divorce is triggered each time the condition (birth) occurs.
This is a linguistic principle: 'كلما' inherently requires repetition.
2
Trace the sequence of events for three births
With six-month gaps between births, the woman is in iddah after the first divorce. The husband's intercourse during iddah constitutes a revocable return, so before the second birth, ruju' occurs, then the second divorce triggers, and so on.
The birth of a child after six months indicates intercourse during iddah.
3
Understand the role of revocable return (رجعت)
Ruju' is established by intercourse during revocable iddah. It restores the marriage without a new contract. After ruju', the marriage continues, and the next condition triggers another divorce.
Ruju' is a critical concept: it allows the husband to take back his wife without a new marriage contract.
4
Analyze the linguistic proof
The proof is the word 'كلما'. In Arabic, it means 'whenever' and demands repetition of the consequence upon repetition of the condition. This is a recognized rule in Hanafi usul.
The Hanafi school relies on the literal meaning of words in contractual contexts.
5
Note the type of iddah after the third divorce
After the third divorce, the woman is no longer pregnant (the third birth has occurred), so her iddah is three menstrual cycles (iddah by menses).
This is because at the time of the third divorce, she is among those who menstruate.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم بچہ کی ولادت سے دوسری طلاق واقع ہوگی کیونکہ یمین کلمہ کلما کے ساتھ منعقد کی گئی ہے اور عدت واجب ہوگئی اور تیسرے بچہ کے ساتھ وہ مراجعہ کرنے والا ہو گیا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور تیسرے بچہ کی ولادت سے تیسری طلاق واقع ہوگی اور عدت واجب ہوئی حیضوں کے ساتھ کیونکہ یہ عورت حاملہ وقوع طلاق کے وقت ذوات الحیض میں سے ہے۔

دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب پہلا بچہ پیدا ہوا تو ولادت پر طلاق کے معلق ہونے کی وجہ سے طلاق واقع ہوگئی اور عورت معندہ ہو گئی ۔ اس کے بعد جب دوسرا بچہ پیدا ہوا تو رجعت ثابت ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ چھ ماہ بعد دوسرے بچہ کی ولادت اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اس عورت سے عدت میں ولی کی گئی ہے اور عدت میں وطی رجعت کو ثابت کر دیتی ہے اس وجہ سے رجعت ثابت ہوگئی اور دوسرے بچہ کی ولادت سے دوسری طلاق اس لئے واقع ہوگی کہ لفظ کلما کے ساتھ یمین کا منعقد کرنا تکرار شرط کے وقت تکرار جزاء کا تقاضا کرتا ہے اور دوسری طلاق کے بعد پھر عدت واجب ہوگئی۔ اس کے بعد جب تیسرے بچہ کی ولادت اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ اس عورت سے عدت میں وطی کی گئی ہے اور معتدہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ وطی کرنا رجعت کو ثابت کر دیتا ہے۔

Chapter: Divorce of the Sick. 52. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary Hidaya volume five: From the birth of the child, the second divorce will occur because the oath was made with the word كلما, and the waiting period becomes obligatory, and with the third child he becomes the one returning (to the wife) due to the proof we mentioned. And from the birth of the third child, the third divorce will occur, and the waiting period becomes obligatory by menses because this woman at the time of occurrence of divorce is among those who menstruate. Explanation: The case is that if the husband said to his wife: 'Whenever you give birth to a child, you are divorced.' Then this woman gave birth to three children from three separate pregnancies, i.e. between the births of two children there is a gap of six months or more. Its ruling is that from the first child's birth, divorce occurs, and before the second child's birth, revocable return (رجعت) is established. Immediately after that, the second divorce occurs. Similarly, before the third child's birth, revocable return occurs, and then the third divorce occurs. The proof is that when the first child was born, due to the suspension of divorce upon birth, divorce occurred and the woman became in waiting period. Then when the second child was born, revocable return became established because the birth of a child after six months indicates that she was copulated with during the waiting period, and copulation during the waiting period confirms revocable return. For this reason, revocable return became established, and from the second child's birth, the second divorce occurs because the making of an oath with the word كلما requires repetition of the consequence upon repetition of the condition. After the second divorce, the waiting period again becomes obligatory. Then when the third child is born, that indicates that she was copulated with during the waiting period, and copulation with a revocable divorcee establishes revocable return. And from the birth of this third child, the third divorce occurs because the word كلما requires repetition, and now on this woman the waiting period by menses becomes obligatory because at the time of occurrence of the third divorce, she is among those who menstruate.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the chapter on divorce of the sick. The passage explains the Hanafi ruling on a conditional divorce using the word 'كلما' (whenever). The husband says to his wife: 'Whenever you give birth to a child, you are divorced.' The key issue is the effect of the word 'كلما', which implies repetition. The ruling: each birth triggers a divorce, but since the woman is in waiting period after the first divorce, and the husband may have intercourse during that period which counts as a revocable return, the second and third births are preceded by revocable returns. The proof is linguistic: 'كلما' requires that whenever the condition (birth) repeats, the consequence (divorce) repeats. This is a clear example of Hanafi reliance on the literal meaning of words. The text also clarifies that after the third divorce, the waiting period is by menses (three menstrual cycles) because the woman is not pregnant at that point.

Key Terms
كلما (kullamā): An Arabic word meaning 'whenever' that implies repetition of the consequence upon each occurrence of the condition.
رجعت (ruju'): Revocable return to the marriage during the waiting period of a revocable divorce, without a new contract.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Three divorces, one after each birth, with intervening revocable returns.
C) Only two divorces because the third birth occurs after iddah ends.
D) No divorce because the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The word 'كلما' in a conditional divorce mandates the repetition of the divorce upon each occurrence of the condition, and revocable return through intercourse during iddah is a critical intervening step.

Adornment of the Revocable Divorcee and Husband's Conduct
Ruling on adornment, entry, and travel for revocable divorcee with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the revocable divorcee's adornment and apply the Quranic evidence to explain why the husband may not travel with her without witnesses on revocable return.

Core Idea
A revocable divorcee adorns herself to encourage return; the husband must announce entry to avoid inadvertent reconciliation.

A revocable divorcee remains in a partial marital bond during her waiting period. This passage clarifies her right to beautify herself and the husband's obligations when entering upon her or traveling with her. It also addresses an internal Hanafi difference with Imam Zufar, who permitted travel on the basis of the ongoing marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the statement that the revocable divorcee adorns herself. Identify the hukm level (mustahab) and the reason: it encourages revocable return, which is recommended.
The text explicitly says 'فيكون مشروعا' (so it is legislated), indicating desirability.
2
Find the evidence for prohibiting travel
The passage cites the Quranic verse 'لا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن' (Do not expel them from their houses). Understand that traveling is a form of expulsion, thus prohibited.
The verse is directed at revocable divorcees, as context shows.
3
Analyze the husband's entry recommendation
The husband is recommended to inform her or make a sound when entering if he does not intend revocable return. Why? To avoid accidentally seeing her unclothed, which would trigger revocable return and then divorce, prolonging her waiting period.
This shows the school's concern for preventing harm to the woman.
4
Understand the condition for travel
He may only travel with her after taking witnesses on his revocable return. Until then, travel is prohibited based on the Quranic prohibition of expulsion.
Imam Muhammad's saying 'until he testifies' is interpreted as recommended, not obligatory.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Zufar argued that the ongoing marriage allows travel and intercourse. The Hanafi response distinguishes that the prohibition of expulsion is a specific ruling that overrides general analogy.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: Zufar would allow travel without witnesses; the majority prohibits it.

رجعیہ اپنے شوہر کے واسطے حلال ہے۔ اس لئے کہ دونوں کے درمیان نکاح قائم ہے۔ چنانچہ طلاق رجعی کی صورت میں تو ارث اور تمام احکام نکاح قائم رہتے ہیں۔ اسی وجہ سے اگر اس شخص نے کہا کل امراۃ لی طالق تو اس حکم میں یہ مطلقہ بھی داخل ہوگی اور اس پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر کوئی یہ اشکال کر دے کہ جب طلاق رجعی کے بعد نکاح موجود ہے تو اس کے ساتھ سفر کرنا جائز ہونا چاہیے۔ جیسا کہ منکوحہ غیر مطلقہ کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنا جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ آپ جو از مسافرت کے قائل نہیں ہیں۔ جواب۔ مطلقہ رجعیہ کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنے کی ممانعت نص سے ثابت ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد ہے لا تخرجو هن من بيوتهن يعنى مطلقات رجعیہ کو ان کے مسکن سے نہ نکالو اور یہ یعنی آیت مطلقہ رجعیہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے۔ پس اس نص کی وجہ سے مطلقہ رجعیہ کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنے کی ممانعت کی گئی ہے۔ لیکن اگر کوئی شخص اعتراض کر دے کہ نفس مسافرت کو رجعت کی دلیل کیوں نہیں بنایا گیا تو جواب ہوگا کہ اخراج من البیت یعنی مطلقہ رجعیہ کو گھر سے باہر لے جانا منہی عنہ ہے اور رجعت مندوب الیہا ہے اور ان دونوں کے درمیان منافات ہے اور جن دو چیزوں کے درمیان منافات ہو ان میں سے ایک کو دوسرے کے لئے دلیل نہیں بنایا جا سکتا اس لئے نفس مسافرت رجعت کی دلیل نہیں بن سکتا ہے۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ رجعت مستحب ہے اور مزین کرنا رجعت پر شوہر کو آمادہ کرنے والا ہے اس وجہ سے مطلقہ رجعیہ کا اپنے آپ کو مزین کرنا اور آراستہ کرنا مشروع ہے اور مطلقہ رجعیہ کے شوہر کے واسطے مستحب یہ ہے کہ وہ بغیر اطلاع کے اس کے پاس نہ جائے یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جب کہ شوہر کا ارادہ رجعت کرنے کا نہ ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت بسا اوقات گھر میں برہنہ ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس بغیر اطلاع داخل ہونے کی صورت میں شوہر کی نظر ایسے بدن پر پڑ سکتی ہے جس سے رجعت ثابت ہو جائے اور چونکہ اس شخص کا ارادہ رجعت کرنے کا نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ اس کو طلاق دے گا اور طلاق دینے کی صورت میں عورت کی عدت خواہ خواہ دراز ہو گی۔ اس وجہ سے یہ حکم دیا گیا کہ عورت کے پاس جانے سے پہلے اس کو باخبر کر دے۔ یا اپنے جوتوں کی آہٹ سنا دے یا کھنکار کر داخل ہو۔
And the revocable divorcee adorns herself and beautifies herself because she is lawful for the husband, as the marriage tie exists between them. Then revocable return is recommended, and beautification encourages it, so it is legislated. It is recommended for her husband not to enter upon her until he informs her or makes her hear the sound of his sandals. This means when he does not intend revocable return, because she may be unclothed so his sight may fall on a place that would make him return, then he divorces her and her waiting period becomes long. He may not travel with her until he takes witnesses on his revocable return. Zufar said: He may do so because of the existence of marriage, and therefore he may have intercourse with her according to us. Our proof is the verse of Allah: 'Do not expel them from their houses' etc. And because the delaying of the action of the invalidator (divorce) is due to his need for revocable return. So if he does not return to her until the period expires, it becomes clear that he had no need, so it is known that the invalidator acted from the time it occurred, and therefore the menstrual periods are counted from the waiting period, and the husband's ownership is established. And his saying 'until he testifies on her revocable return' means recommendation, as we have mentioned. Translation: And the revocable divorcee should adorn herself and beautify herself because this woman is lawful for her husband, because the marriage remains between them. Then revocable return is recommended, and the woman's adornment encourages it, so adornment is legislated. And it is recommended for her husband not to enter upon her until he informs her or makes her hear the sound of his sandals. The meaning of al-Quduri's statement is when he does not intend revocable return, because the woman may sometimes be unclothed, so his sight may fall on a place that makes him return. Then he will divorce her, so the waiting period becomes long for the woman. And he should take witnesses on revocable return. Imam Zufar said that this is permissible for him, due to the existence of marriage, and for that reason it is permissible for the husband to have intercourse with her in our view. Our proof is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Do not expel them from their houses' etc., meaning do not expel them from their dwellings. And because the delay of the action of the invalidator (divorce) is due to the husband's need for revocable return. So when the husband did not return to her until the waiting period expired, it became apparent that he had no need. So it became clear that the invalidator acted from the time it occurred, and therefore the menstrual periods that have passed will be counted in the waiting period. So the husband does not become owner of taking her out, unless the husband takes witnesses on his revocable return, then the waiting period becomes void and the husband's ownership is established. And Imam Muhammad's statement 'until he testifies on her revocable return' means recommendation, as we have previously stated. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the woman who has been given a revocable divorce should keep herself neat and adorned, i.e., keep her face and cheeks clean. The proof is that the revocable divorcee is lawful for her husband because the marriage tie exists between them. Thus, in the case of revocable divorce, inheritance and all rules of marriage remain. For this reason, if a man said 'every woman of mine is divorced', this revocable divorcee would be included and divorce would occur upon her. And if someone objects that when marriage exists after revocable divorce, traveling with her should be permissible, just as traveling with a non-divorced wife is permissible, yet you (the Hanafis) do not allow traveling. The answer: The prohibition of traveling with a revocable divorcee is established by text. Allah said: 'Do not expel them from their houses', i.e., do not expel revocable divorcees from their dwellings, and this verse was revealed concerning revocable divorcees. So due to this text, traveling with a revocable divorcee is prohibited. But if someone objects why traveling itself is not made a proof of revocable return, the answer is that expulsion from the house (taking the revocable divorcee out) is prohibited, while revocable return is desirable, and there is incompatibility between them. When two things are incompatible, one cannot be taken as proof for the other. So traveling itself cannot be a proof of revocable return. He says that revocable return is recommended, and beautification encourages the husband to return. For this reason, it is legislated for the revocable divorcee to beautify and adorn herself. And it is recommended for the husband of a revocable divorcee not to enter upon her without informing, this ruling is when the husband does not intend revocable return. The proof is that the woman may sometimes be undressed in the house. So if he enters without informing, his sight may fall on a body part that would establish revocable return. And since this person does not intend revocable return, he will divorce her, and in case of divorce, the woman's waiting period will become long. For this reason, it was commanded that before going to the woman, he should inform her, or make her hear the sound of his sandals, or clear his throat when entering.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the chapter on divorce of the sick. The passage discusses the legal status of a revocable divorcee (مطلقة رجعية) regarding her adornment and the husband's conduct. The key point is that although the marriage tie persists during the waiting period of a revocable divorce, the husband cannot simply enter upon her without notice if he does not intend revocable return, because seeing her may inadvertantly trigger revocable return. The text also addresses a disagreement with Imam Zufar, who permitted the husband to travel with her and have intercourse, but the Hanafi position, based on the Quranic verse (65:1), prohibits traveling (as a form of expulsion) but recommends not entering without notice. The proof for the prohibition of travel is the verse 'Do not expel them from their houses,' which indicates that the revocable divorcee must remain in her marital home. The husband may not take her out without witnesses on revocable return. The commentary further clarifies that if the husband does not intend revocable return, it is recommended (mustahab) for him to avoid entering without announcement to prevent unintended revocable return, which would prolong the waiting period if he then divorces her again. This shows the Hanafi concern for preventing harm to the woman.

Key Terms
مطلقة رجعية (muṭallaqah raj'iyyah): A woman divorced by a revocable divorce, meaning her husband may return to her during the waiting period without a new marriage contract.
تتشبوف وتتزين (tatashtabbu wa tatazayyana): She adorns and beautifies herself, meaning she takes care of her appearance and wears attractive clothing/ornaments.
خفق نعليه (khafaq na'layhi): The sound of his sandals or footsteps, used as a way to announce his arrival.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a husband entering upon his revocable divorcee without notice when he does not intend revocable return?
A) It is prohibited (haram) because the marriage is suspended.
B) It is recommended (mustahab) to inform her or make a sound, to avoid accidental revocable return.
C) It is permissible (mubah) because the marriage still exists.
D) It is obligatory (wajib) to give her notice.

Key Takeaway
A revocable divorcee may adorn herself to encourage return, but the husband must avoid inadvertent reconciliation by announcing his entry and must not travel with her without witnesses on revocable return.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Traveling with a Revocably Divorced Wife
Intra-Hanafi dispute on traveling with revocably divorced wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on traveling with a revocably divorced wife, explain the evidence from Quran and rational proof, and distinguish the majority view from Imam Zufar's view.

Core Idea
Traveling with a revocably divorced wife is prohibited unless the husband performs a witnessed ruju' – the marriage is suspended, not dissolved.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a critical dispute within the Hanafi school: may a husband take his revocably divorced wife on a journey during her 'iddah? The majority of the school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani) say no, while Imam Zufar says yes. Understanding their proofs – textual and rational – will deepen your grasp of how the Hanafi school balances Quranic texts with the legal reality of a continuing marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The core question: can a husband travel with his revocably divorced wife (muttallaqa raj'iyya) during the 'iddah period?
The issue arises because revocable divorce does not end the marriage completely; the husband retains the right to return (ruju') without a new contract.
2
State the positions
The majority (three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold it is not permissible until he performs ruju' with witnesses. Imam Zufar holds it is permissible because the marriage continues.
Imam Zufar's view is a minority position within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyse the majority's proof from the Quran
The verse 'Do not expel them from their homes' (Quran 65:1) is cited. It was revealed about revocably divorced women. Travel is considered a form of expulsion, thus prohibited.
The imperative prohibition (nahy) in Hanafi usul indicates haram unless overridden.
4
Examine the rational proof (dalil 'aqli)
Divorce is a nullifier, but its effect is delayed until the end of 'iddah to allow ruju'. If the husband does not return, it becomes clear that the divorce operated from the start, making her like a ba'in (irrevocably divorced) woman – travel prohibited.
This argument shows that the marriage is considered retroactively ended if no ruju' occurs.
5
Understand the exception and istihbab
Once the husband performs witnessed ruju', the marriage is fully restored and travel becomes permissible. Moreover, ruju' itself is mustahabb, not wajib – the husband is not forced to return.
Imam Muhammad's phrase 'until he witnesses his return' indicates recommendation, not obligation.

رہی یہ بات کہ شوہر اپنی مطلقہ رجعیہ کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں۔ اس بارے میں ائمہ ثلاثہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ شوہر کے لئے مطلقہ رجعیہ کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنا جائز نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ اس سے مراجعت کرنے پر گواہ بنا لے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ شوہر کے لئے اس کے ساتھ سفر کرنا جائز ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق رجعی کے بعد عدت پوری ہونے سے پہلے پہلے نکاح قائم رہتا ہے اور اسی قیام نکاح کی وجہ سے ہمارے نزدیک اس سے وطی کرنا جائز ہے پس جس طرح منکوحہ کے ساتھ سفر کرنا شرعاً درست ہے اسی طرح اس کے ساتھ بھی سفر کرنا درست ہو گا۔
اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ خداوند قدوس نے فرمایا ہے "ولا تخر جوهن من بيوتهن" اس آیت کے بارے میں ائمہ تفسیر سے منقول ہے کہ یہ آیت طلاق رجعی کے سلسلہ میں اتری ہے ترجمہ ہوگا نہ نکالو ان عورتوں کو جن کو طلاق رجعی دی گئی ہے ان کے مسکن سے پس اس آیت سے ثابت ہوا کہ شوہر کے لئے ان عورتوں کو نکالنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
اور دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ طلاق ملک نکاح کو باطل کرنے والی ہے۔ لہذا مناسب تو یہ تھا کہ وجود طلاق کے وقت ہی نکاح باطل ہو جائے مگر اس کا حکم انقضاء عدت تک کے لئے موخر ہو گیا۔ تا کہ شوہر اگر رجعت کرنا چاہے تو رجعت کر سکے۔ پس جب شوہر نے رجعت نہیں کی اور عدت گزرگئی تو معلوم ہوگیا کہ شوہر کو رجعت کی حاجت نہیں تھی اور جب رجعت کی حاجت نہیں ہے تو ظاہر ہو گیا کہ مبطل نکاح یعنی طلاق کا عمل اسی وقت سے ہے جس وقت سے طلاق پائی گئی اور اسی وجہ سے وہ حیض جو عدت گزرنے سے پہلے گزر چکے عدت میں محسوب ہوں گے۔ پس جب وجود طلاق کے وقت ہی نکاح منقطع ہو گیا تو یہ عورت بائنہ کے مانند ہوگئی۔ لہذا جس طرح مطلقہ بائنہ کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنا ممنوع ہے۔ اسی طرح اس عورت کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنا ممنوع ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر شوہر نے اس سے رجعت کر لی اور گواہ بنالئے تو عدت باطل ہو جائے گی اور اس عورت کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنا درست ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام محمد کے قول "حتى يشهد على رجعتها" سے استحباب رجعت مراد ہے نہ کہ وجوب رجعت ۔ جیسا کہ شروع باب میں گزر چکا۔
Chapter of Divorce of the Sick. It is mustahabb that he does not go to her until he informs her or makes his shoes heard. The meaning of Quduri's statement is when he does not intend to return (ruju'). Because the woman might sometimes be naked, so his eye may fall on something that would make him return. Then he would divorce her, and the 'iddah would be prolonged for her. And (it is recommended) that he take witnesses upon return. Imam Zufar said: This is permissible for him due to the existence of marriage, and for this reason it is permissible for the husband to have intercourse with her. According to us, our proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And do not expel them' (the verse). Meaning: Do not expel them from their homes. And because the operation of the nullifier (divorce) is delayed due to the husband's need for return. So when the husband does not return until the 'iddah period passes, it becomes clear that he had no need for return. So it becomes clear that the nullifier operated from the time it occurred, and for this reason the menses that passed are counted in the 'iddah. Thus the husband is not entitled to take her out, unless he takes witnesses upon return; then the 'iddah becomes void and the husband's ownership is established. And Imam Muhammad's statement 'until he witnesses his return to her' indicates istihbab (recommendation), not wujub (obligation), as we have mentioned before. Explanation: Sahib Quduri said: The woman who has been given a revocable divorce should adorn and beautify herself, i.e., keep her face and cheeks clean. The proof is that the revocably divorced woman is lawful for her husband because marriage continues between them. Thus in revocable divorce, inheritance and all laws of marriage remain. For this reason, if a man said 'All my women are divorced,' this divorcée would be included and divorce would occur. And if someone objects: When marriage exists after revocable divorce, traveling with her should be permissible, just as it is permissible to travel with a non-divorced wife, but you do not permit travel, the answer: Prohibition of traveling with a revocably divorced woman is established by text. Indeed, the command is 'Do not expel them from their homes' meaning revocably divorced women, and this verse was revealed concerning revocable divorce. So due to this text, traveling with a revocably divorced woman is prohibited. But if someone objects: Why is the act of traveling itself not considered evidence of return? The answer: Expelling from the home, i.e., taking the revocably divorced woman out of the house, is prohibited, while return is recommended (mandub). Between these there is contradiction, and one of two contradictory things cannot be evidence for the other. Therefore, the act of traveling cannot be evidence of return. They say: Return is mustahabb, and adorning oneself induces the husband to return; therefore, it is legislated for the revocably divorced woman to adorn herself. And for the husband of a revocably divorced woman, it is mustahabb that he does not go to her without informing, this ruling applies when he does not intend to return. The proof is that the woman sometimes becomes naked in the house, so if he enters without informing, his eye may fall on a body part that would establish return, and since he does not intend to return, he would divorce her, and thus the 'iddah would be prolonged. Therefore, it is ordered that before going to her, he should inform her or make the sound of his shoes heard or clear his throat upon entering. The remaining point: Whether the husband can take his revocably divorced wife on a journey. On this, the madhhab of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that it is not permissible for the husband to take her on a journey until he takes witnesses upon return. Imam Zufar said: It is permissible for him to travel with her. His proof: After revocable divorce and before the completion of 'iddah, the marriage continues, and due to the continuation of marriage, intercourse is permissible according to us, so just as it is legally valid to travel with a wife, so too it is valid to travel with her. Our proof: Allah Most High said 'And do not expel them from their homes.' It is transmitted from the exegetes that this verse was revealed concerning revocable divorce. The translation: Do not expel the women who have been given revocable divorce from their homes. Thus from this verse it is established that it is not permissible for the husband to expel them. And the rational proof: Divorce is a nullifier of the ownership of marriage. So it would be appropriate that marriage be invalidated at the time of divorce, but its ruling is delayed until the end of 'iddah so that the husband may return if he wishes. So when the husband did not return and the 'iddah passed, it is known that the husband had no need for return, and when there is no need for return, it becomes clear that the nullifier of marriage, i.e., divorce, operated from the time it occurred. For this reason, the menses that passed before the end of 'iddah are counted in the 'iddah. So when marriage is severed from the time of divorce, this woman becomes like a ba'in (irrevocably divorced) woman. Therefore, just as it is prohibited to travel with a ba'in divorcée, so too it is prohibited to travel with this woman. Yes, if the husband returned to her and took witnesses, then the 'iddah becomes void and traveling with her becomes valid. Sahib Hidayah says: Imam Muhammad's statement 'until he witnesses his return to her' indicates istihbab of return, not wujub, as has passed at the beginning of the chapter.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the rulings related to a revocably divorced woman (muttallaqa raj'iyya). The text begins by explaining the mustahabb behavior for the husband: he should not enter upon her without informing her or making his presence known, especially if he does not intend to return (ruju'). The reason is to avoid accidental sight that might compel him to return, leading to a divorce and prolonging the 'iddah. The text then moves to the core issue: can the husband travel with his revocably divorced wife? The majority of the Hanafi school (the three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that it is not permissible to take her on a journey until he has performed a witnessed ruju'. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi imam) disagrees, arguing that since the marriage continues during the 'iddah, traveling should be permissible, just as intercourse is permissible. The majority's primary proof is the Quranic verse 'Do not expel them from their homes' (Surah al-Talaq:1), which is interpreted as a prohibition against taking her out of her residence, including for travel. A rational proof (dalil 'aqli) is also provided: divorce is a nullifier of marriage, but its effect is delayed until the end of the 'iddah to allow for reconciliation. If the husband does not return, it becomes clear that the divorce operated from the moment it was issued, making the woman like a ba'in (irrevocably divorced) woman—traveling with her is thus prohibited. The exception is if he performs ruju' with witnesses, which restores the marriage fully. The text also notes that Imam Muhammad's phrase 'until he witnesses his return' indicates that return is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory. Additionally, earlier parts discuss the woman's duty to adorn herself to encourage return, and the husband's duty to avoid entering without notice to prevent accidental ruju'.

Key Terms
طلاق رجعي (talaq raj'i): A revocable divorce where the husband has the right to return to the wife during the 'iddah without a new marriage contract.
رجعت (ruju'): The act of the husband taking back his revocably divorced wife during the 'iddah, which restores the marriage.
مبطل (mubtil): That which nullifies (the marriage), i.e., the divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of the Hanafi school (the three imams), when is it permissible for a husband to travel with his revocably divorced wife?
A) At any time during the 'iddah, because marriage continues.
B) Only after he has returned to her (ruju') and taken witnesses on the return.
C) Only after the 'iddah has expired.
D) It is never permissible, even after ruju'.

Key Takeaway
Traveling with a revocably divorced wife is prohibited unless the husband performs ruju' with witnesses; the Quranic prohibition overrides the general continuance of marriage.

Revocable Divorce Does Not Forbid Intercourse
Hanafi ruling with Shafi'i dispute and rational evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that revocable divorce does not prohibit intercourse and distinguish the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Revocable divorce does not fully sever the marital bond; the right of return proves its continuation.

When a husband pronounces a revocable divorce, does the marriage end immediately in all respects? Imam al-Shafi'i argues that divorce is a nullifier that severs the bond, making intercourse unlawful. But the Hanafi school looks at the practical reality: the husband can take his wife back without her consent. This lesson unpacks that evidence and the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what each school rules about intercourse during the 'iddah of a revocable divorce. Hanafi says permissible; Shafi'i says prohibited.
2
Analyse the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i argument is that divorce is a nullifier (qati') that eliminates marital authority (zawjiyya). Understand why this seems logical at first glance.
3
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi school points to the husband's right to return (haqq al-raj'a) without the wife's consent. This right shows that the marital bond remains intact during the 'iddah.
The key concept: return is a continuation (istidama) not a new creation (insha').
4
Reconcile the nullifier with the continuation
How can divorce be a nullifier yet the marriage continues? The Hanafi response is that the nullifier's effect is delayed until the 'iddah expires, by consensus or for the husband's benefit.
5
Identify the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Hanafi husband may have intercourse during the 'iddah without a new contract; a Shafi'i husband cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طلاق رجعی وطی کو حرام نہیں کرتی ، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
والطلاق الرجعي لا يحرم الوطى وقال الشافعي يحرمه لان الزوجية زائلة لوجود القاطع وهو الطلاق ولنا انها قائمة حتى يملك مراجعتها من غير رضاها لان حق الرجعة ثبت نظرا للزوج ليمكنه التدارك عند اعتراض الندم وهذا المعنى يوجب استبداده وذلك يؤذن بكونه استدامة لا انشاء اذ الدليل ينافيه والقاطع اخر عمله الى مدة اجماعا او نظرا له على ما تقدم
ترجمہ اور طلاق رجعی وطی کو حرام نہیں کرتی ہے اور امام شافی نے فرمایا کہ اسکو حرام کر دیتی ہے۔ کیونکہ زوجیت زائل ہوگئی قاطع کے پائے جانے کی وجہ ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زوجیت موجود ہے ۔ حتی کہ اس سے مراجعت کا مالک ہے۔ بغیر اس کی رضامندی کے کیونکہ رجعت کا حق شوہر کے لحاظ سے ثابت ہوا ہے۔ تا کہ ندامت پیش آنے کے وقت شوہر کو تدارک کرنا ممکن ہو اور یہ معنی حق رجعت کے ساتھ شوہر کے مستقل ہونے کو واجب کرتے ہیں اور شوہر کا خود مستقل ہونا آگاہ کرتا ہے کہ رجعت ملک نکاح کو برابر باقی رکھنا ہے نہ کہ از سرنو پیدا کرنا۔ کیونکہ دلیل اس کی منافی ہے اور قاطع نے اپنا عمل ایک مدت تک کے لئے بالا جماع موخر کر دیا یا شوہر پر نظر کرتے ہوئے اس بناء پر جو پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
Revocable Divorce Does Not Prohibit Intercourse, Imam Shafi'i's View. And revocable divorce does not prohibit intercourse. Al-Shafi'i said: It prohibits it because marital authority (zawjiyya) is removed due to the existence of the nullifier (qati'), which is divorce. Our evidence: It (marital authority) remains, such that he has the right to return to her without her consent. Because the right of return (haqq al-raj'a) is established for the sake of the husband, so that he may remedy (the situation) when regret occurs. This meaning necessitates his independence, and that indicates that it (return) is a continuation (istidama) not a new creation (insha'), because evidence opposes it (i.e., the idea that it is new). And the nullifier (divorce) delayed its operation for a period, by consensus, or had regard for him (the husband) as has preceded.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) prohibits sexual intercourse. The Hanafi position is that it does not prohibit intercourse, while al-Shafi'i holds that it does. The Shafi'i argument is that divorce is a 'nullifier' (qati') that severs the marital bond, so the marriage is dissolved and intercourse becomes unlawful. The Hanafi response is that the marital bond (zawjiyya) continues during the 'iddah, as evidenced by the fact that the husband has the right to return (ruju') to his wife without her consent. This right of return is established for the husband's benefit, allowing him to rectify the situation if he regrets the divorce. This demonstrates that the marriage is ongoing—it is a continuation (istidama) of the existing marriage, not a new creation. The nullifier (divorce) has delayed its effect until the end of the 'iddah by consensus (ijma') or out of consideration for the husband, as previously explained. Therefore, intercourse remains permissible.

Key Terms
قاطع (qati'): The nullifier, i.e., divorce, which severs the marriage bond.
استدامة (istidama): Continuation of the existing marriage, as opposed to a new creation (insha').
حق الرجعة (haqq al-raj'a): The husband's right to return to his revocably divorced wife during the 'iddah without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does revocable divorce not prohibit intercourse?
A) Because the divorce is not effective until the 'iddah ends.
B) Because the husband's right to return without consent shows the marriage continues.
C) Because the Quran explicitly allows it.
D) Because the wife can give her consent.

Key Takeaway
Revocable divorce does not fully dissolve the marriage; the right of return proves the bond continues, making intercourse permissible.

Traveling with a Revocably Divorced Wife: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on traveling with a revocably divorced wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on traveling with a revocably divorced wife and explain why Imam Zufar differed, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A revocably divorced wife cannot be taken on travel unless the husband makes a formal return with witnesses.

This lesson explores a subtle dispute among Hanafi imams: may a husband travel with his wife after giving her a revocable divorce? The three major Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) prohibit it, while Imam Zufar permits it. We will examine the proofs from Quran and reason, and understand the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognize that the issue is traveling with a revocably divorced wife (talaq raj'i) during the iddah period, and note that there is disagreement within the Hanafi school.
The dispute is between the three Imams and Imam Zufar.
2
State the majority Hanafi position and its proof
The three Imams hold that it is not permissible until the husband makes a revocable return (raj'ah) with witnesses. Their proof is the Quranic verse (65:1) and a rational argument about the delayed effect of divorce.
The verse prohibits expelling her; traveling is a form of expulsion.
3
State Imam Zufar's position and his proof
Imam Zufar permits travel because the marriage continues during the iddah period, so she is like a married wife, with whom travel is allowed.
He relies on the continuity of nikah for inheritance and other rulings.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the majority view, the husband must first make a witnessed return before travel; under Imam Zufar's view, he may travel at any time during iddah without witnesses.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہی یہ بات کہ شوہر اپنی مطلقہ رجعیہ کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں۔ اس بارے میں ائمہ ثلاثہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ شوہر کے لئے مطلقہ رجعیہ کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنا جائز نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ اس سے مراجعت کرنے پر گواہ بنا لے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ شوہر کے لئے اس کے ساتھ سفر کرنا جائز ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق رجعی کے بعد عدت پوری ہونے سے پہلے پہلے نکاح قائم رہتا ہے اور اسی قیام نکاح کی وجہ سے ہمارے نزدیک اس سے وطی کرنا جائز ہے پس جس طرح منکوحہ کے ساتھ سفر کرنا شرعاً درست ہے اسی طرح اس کے ساتھ بھی سفر کرنا درست ہو گا۔
اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ خداوند قدوس نے فرمایا ہے ولا تخر جوهن من بيوتهن اس آیت کے بارے میں ائمہ تفسیر سے منقول ہے کہ یہ آیت طلاق رجعی کے سلسلہ میں اتری ہے ترجمہ ہوگا نہ نکالو ان عورتوں کو جن کو طلاق رجعی دی گئی ہے ان کے مسکن سے پس اس آیت سے ثابت ہوا کہ شوہر کے لئے ان عورتوں کو نکالنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ طلاق ملک نکاح کو باطل کرنے والی ہے۔ لہذا مناسب تو یہ تھا کہ وجود طلاق کے وقت ہی نکاح باطل ہو جائے مگر اس کا حکم انقضاء عدت تک کے لئے موخر ہو گیا۔ تا کہ شوہر اگر رجعت کرنا چاہے تو رجعت کر سکے۔ پس جب شوہر نے رجعت نہیں کی اور عدت گزرگئی تو معلوم ہوگیا کہ شوہر کو رجعت کی حاجت نہیں تھی اور جب رجعت کی حاجت نہیں ہے تو ظاہر ہو گیا کہ مبطل نکاح یعنی طلاق کا عمل اسی وقت سے ہے جس وقت سے طلاق پائی گئی اور اسی وجہ سے وہ ایام جو عدت گزرنے سے پہلے گزر چکے عدت میں محسوب ہوں گے۔ پس جب وجود طلاق کے وقت ہی نکاح منقطع ہو گیا تو یہ عورت بائنہ کے مانند ہوگئی۔ لہذا جس طرح مطلقہ بائنہ کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنا ممنوع ہے۔ اسی طرح اس عورت کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنا ممنوع ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر شوہر نے اس سے رجعت کر لی اور گواہ بنالئے تو عدت باطل ہو جائے گی اور اس عورت کو ساتھ لے کر سفر کرنا درست ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام محمد کے قول حتى يشهد على رجعتها سے استحباب رجعت مراد ہے نہ کہ وجوب رجعت ۔ جیسا کہ شروع باب میں گزر چکا۔
The matter remains whether the husband can travel taking his revocably divorced wife with him. Regarding this, the doctrine of the three Imams is that it is not permissible for the husband to travel taking his revocably divorced wife with him until he makes witnesses for her return. And Imam Zufar said that it is permissible for the husband to travel with her. The proof is that after revocable divorce, before the completion of the waiting period, the marriage continues, and due to the continuance of marriage, intercourse with her is permissible according to us. So just as it is lawful to travel with a married woman, similarly it would be lawful to travel with her. And our proof is that Almighty Allah said: 'Do not expel them from their houses.' Regarding this verse, it is narrated from the exegetes that this verse was revealed about revocable divorce. The translation: 'Do not expel the women who have been given revocable divorce from their dwellings.' Thus it is established from this verse that it is not permissible for the husband to expel them. And the rational proof is that divorce is something that nullifies the ownership of marriage. Hence it was appropriate that the marriage would be void at the time of divorce, but its effect is delayed until the end of the waiting period so that the husband may take her back if he wishes. When the husband did not take her back and the waiting period passed, it is known that the husband had no need for return. And when there is no need for return, it becomes evident that the nullifier of marriage, i.e., the act of divorce, is effective from the time it occurred. Therefore, the days that passed before the waiting period are counted in the waiting period. Since the marriage was severed at the time of divorce, this woman becomes like an irrevocably divorced woman. Just as traveling with an irrevocably divorced woman is prohibited, similarly traveling with this woman would be prohibited. Yes, if the husband takes her back and makes witnesses, the waiting period becomes null and traveling with her becomes permissible. The author of Hidayah says that from Imam Muhammad's statement 'until he makes witnesses for her return', the recommendation of return is intended, not the obligation, as has passed at the beginning of the chapter.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute among Hanafi imams regarding whether a husband may travel with his revocably divorced wife. The three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that it is not permissible until the husband takes witnesses for the return (raj'ah). Imam Zufar disagrees, relying on the continuity of marriage during the waiting period. The text presents the Hanafi proof from the Quranic verse (65:1) 'Do not expel them from their houses,' which prohibits the husband from expelling his revocably divorced wife, implying that traveling with her (a form of expulsion) is also prohibited. It then provides a rational proof: the effect of divorce is delayed to allow return; if return does not occur, the divorce is effective from the beginning, making the woman like an irrevocably divorced woman (ba'in). Thus, traveling with her is prohibited. However, if the husband makes a revocable return with witnesses, the prohibition is lifted. The commentary by the author of Hidayah clarifies that Imam Muhammad's phrase 'until he makes witnesses for her return' indicates recommendation (istihbab), not obligation (wujub).

Key Terms
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): Revocable divorce where the husband has the right to take back his wife without a new marriage contract during the waiting period.
رجعت (raj'ah): The husband's act of taking back his revocably divorced wife within the waiting period, re-establishing marital rights.
ائمہ ثلاثہ (a'immah thalathah): The three Imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani – the core authorities of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the three Imams, when may a husband travel with his revocably divorced wife?
A) At any time during iddah.
B) Only after making a revocable return with witnesses.
C) Only after iddah ends.
D) Never, because she becomes completely forbidden.

Key Takeaway
The three Imams prohibit traveling with a revocably divorced wife until the husband makes a formal return with witnesses, based on Quran 65:1 and the delayed effect of divorce.

Intercourse with a Revocably Divorced Wife: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on revocable divorce and intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that revocable divorce does not prohibit intercourse and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of deferred effect (ta'khir al-‘amal).

Core Idea
In revocable divorce, the marriage bond remains; the right of return without consent proves intercourse is lawful.

When a husband pronounces one or two revocable divorces, does the marriage continue or end? The answer determines whether intercourse during the waiting period is lawful. The Hanafi school, based on the husband's exclusive right of return, maintains the bond persists. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that divorce severs the bond immediately. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: revocable divorce does not make intercourse unlawful. The husband may have intercourse with his wife during the waiting period.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds intercourse becomes unlawful because divorce (the 'cutter') removes the marital bond. Locate this argument in the text.
Also attributed to Ahmad in one transmission.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The husband's right to take back his wife without her consent demonstrates the marriage continues. If the bond were severed, she would be a stranger and return would require her consent.
This is the core istidlal (legal reasoning) of the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the Hidayah's talil
The author explains that the right of return is given for the husband's benefit to rectify regret. His independence in returning shows it is a continuance, not a new marriage.
This reinforces the idea that the marriage persists.
5
Evaluate the response to Shafi'i
The text answers: the effect of the 'cutter' is deferred until the end of the waiting period (by consensus) or is delayed considering the husband's interest. Thus the marital bond remains during the 'iddah.
This addresses the Shafi'i objection that divorce severs immediately.

Source Text

والطلاق الرجعي لا يحرم الوطء وقال الشافعي يحرمه لان الزوجية زائلة لوجود القاطع وهو الطلاق ولنا انها قائمة حتى يملك مراجعتها من غير رضاها لان حق الرجعة ثبت نظرا للزوج ليمكنه التدارك عند اعتراض الندم وهذ المعنى يوجب استبداده و ذلك يوذن بكونه استدامة لا انشاء اذ الدليل ينافيه والقاطع اخر عمله الى مدة اجماعا او نظراله على ما تقدم

تشریح اس حکم میں اختلاف ہے کہ طلاق رجعی وطی کو حرام کر دیتی ہے یا نہیں۔ احناف کے نزدیک طلاق رجعی وطی کو حرام نہیں کرتی ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے مطلقہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ شوہر کا وطی کرنا حرام ہے اور یہی امام احمد سے ایک روایت ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رشتہ زوجیت کی وجہ سے وطی حلال تھی اور قاطع زوجیت یعنی طلاق کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے زوجیت ختم ہوگئی اس وجہ سے مطلقہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ وطی کرنا حرام ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق رجعی کے پائے جانے کے بعد بھی زوجیت قائم ہے اور اسی وجہ سے بغیر عورت کی رضا مندی کے بالاتفاق اس سے مراجعت کرنے کا اختیار ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر زوجیت ختم ہو گئی ہوتی تو یہ عورت اجنبیہ ہوتی اور بغیر اس کی رضا مندی کے رجعت درست نہ ہوتی۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے قیام زوجیت پر استدلال کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ شوہر کو رجعت کا حق اس لئے دیا گیا ہے تا کہ وہ ندامت اور شرمندگی کے وقت اپنی غلطی کا تدارک کر سکے۔ حاصل یہ کہ شوہر کو رجعت کا حق دینے میں شریعت نے اس کا لحاظ رکھا ہے اور شوہر کے ساتھ شفقت کا معاملہ کیا ہے اور شوہر کو رجعت کا حق دینے میں اس کا لحاظ رکھنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ شوہر رجعت کے سلسلہ میں مستقل ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر شوہر رجعت کے حق میں مستقل نہ ہوتا تو اس پر نظر و شفقت مکمل نہ ہوتی ۔ اس لئے کہ کبھی عورت رجعت پر راضی نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس حق رجعت ، رجعت کرنے میں شوہر کے مستقل ہونے کو ثابت کرتا ہے اور رجعت کرنے میں شوہر کا مستقل ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ رجعت بقاء نکاح کا نام ہے نہ کہ ابتداء نکاح کا۔ اس لئے کہ جو دلیل شوہر کے رجعت کرنے میں مستقل ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہے وہ رجعت کے ابتداء نکاح ہونے کے منافی ہے۔ کیونکہ شوہر ابتداء نکاح میں منفرد اور مستقل نہیں ہوتا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ رجعت بقاء نکاح کا نام ہے اور بقاء نکاح کے لئے قیام نکاح ضروری ہے اور قیام نکاح اور وجود نکاح کی صورت میں وطی حرام نہیں ہوتی ۔ اس وجہ سے ہمارا مذہب یہ ہے کہ طلاق رجعی وطی کو حرام نہیں کرتی۔ والقاطع اخرہ الی آخرہ سے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب ہے جو اب یہ ہے کہ قاطع یعنی طلاق کا پایا جانا قیام زوجیت کے منافی ہے۔ کیونکہ قاطع یعنی طلاق کا عمل بالا جماع انقضاء عدت تک کے لئے مؤخر ہو گیا ہے۔ یا شوہر پر نظر کرتے ہوئے قاطع کا عمل موخر ہو گیا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
And revocable divorce does not make intercourse unlawful. And al-Shafi'i said: It makes it unlawful because the marital bond is removed due to the existence of the cutter (divorce). And our proof is that it remains, such that he has the right to take her back without her consent, because the right of return is established for the benefit of the husband so that he can rectify when regret occurs, and this meaning necessitates his independence. And that indicates that it is a continuance, not a new creation, because the evidence contradicts it, and the cutter delayed its effect for a period unanimously, or considering the husband as previously mentioned. Explanation: There is disagreement in this ruling whether revocable divorce prohibits intercourse. According to the Hanafis, revocable divorce does not prohibit intercourse. And al-Shafi'i said that intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is prohibited, and this is also one transmission from Ahmad. Al-Shafi'i's proof: intercourse was lawful due to the marital bond, and with the existence of the cutter (divorce), the marital bond ends, so intercourse becomes prohibited. Our proof: after revocable divorce, the marital bond remains, and therefore he has the right to take her back without her consent by consensus. If the marital bond had ended, she would be a stranger, and return without her consent would not be valid. The author of Hidayah, arguing for the continuance of the marital bond, said: The right of return was given to the husband so that he can rectify his mistake when regret occurs. The conclusion is that in granting the right of return, the Shariah considered the husband and treated him with kindness. And considering him in granting the right is proof that the husband is independent in the matter of return, because if he were not independent, the consideration and kindness would not be complete. So the right of return proves the husband's independence in making return, and his independence is proof that return is a continuation of the marriage, not a new beginning. Because the evidence indicating his independence contradicts it being a new marriage, since in a new marriage the husband is not alone and independent. Thus it is established that return is a continuation of marriage, and for continuation, the existence of marriage is necessary, and with the existence of marriage, intercourse is not prohibited. Therefore our doctrine is that revocable divorce does not prohibit intercourse. And the statement 'and the cutter delayed its effect...' is a response to al-Shafi'i's proof, that the cutter (divorce) is deferred until the end of the waiting period by consensus, or it is deferred considering the husband as already mentioned. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage addresses the disagreement between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) makes intercourse unlawful. The Hanafi position is that it does not; al-Shafi'i says it does. The Shafi'i proof is that divorce severs the marital bond, so intercourse becomes unlawful. The Hanafi proof centers on the husband's exclusive right of return (raj'ah) without the wife's consent, which indicates the marital bond continues. If the bond were severed, the wife would become a stranger and return would require her consent. The commentary from the author of Hidayah elaborates that the right of return is given for the husband's benefit so he can rectify a hasty divorce. The husband's independence in making return shows that return is a continuation, not a new marriage. The final response to al-Shafi'i is that the effect of divorce is deferred until the end of the waiting period (by consensus) or considering the husband's interest, so the marital bond remains during the waiting period.

Key Terms
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): Revocable divorce where the husband can take back his wife without a new contract during the waiting period.
قاطع (qati'): The cutter; refers to the divorce that severs the marital bond, but its effect is delayed in revocable divorce according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the divorce was not pronounced three times

Key Takeaway
Revocable divorce does not break the marriage bond; the husband's exclusive right of return demonstrates the marriage continues, making intercourse lawful during the waiting period.

Remarrying a Ba'in Divorcee (Less Than Three)
Introduction to a new section on when a divorced woman becomes lawful for remarriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding the remarriage of a ba'in divorcee (less than three) and explain the rationale given in the Hanafi text.

Core Idea
A ba'in divorce of less than three does not extinguish the right to remarry; the husband may remarry during or after the iddah.

This lesson introduces a new section (fasl) on when a divorced woman becomes lawful for her former husband. The text clarifies that a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce with less than three pronouncements does not permanently sever the marriage bond. The husband retains the right to remarry her, subject to certain restrictions. Understanding this ruling is crucial for distinguishing between the effects of different types of divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of divorce
Note that the passage specifically addresses a ba'in divorce (irrevocable) where the number of divorces given is less than three.
Ba'in divorce means the husband cannot take her back without a new contract.
2
State the ruling
The text states that the husband may marry her during the waiting period (iddah) or after its expiry.
3
Understand the rationale
The reason given is that the lawfulness of marriage with her remains intact until the third divorce occurs. Since the third has not occurred, the right to remarry persists.
This is based on the principle that the marriage bond is not fully severed until the third divorce.
4
Note the exception for others
The text adds that other men are prohibited from marrying her during the iddah due to potential confusion of lineage (if she becomes pregnant), but this does not apply to the original husband.

ترجمہ (یہ) فصل ایسے امور کے بیان میں ہے جن سے مطلقہ حلال ہو جاتی ہے
مطلقہ بائنہ سے جبکہ طلاقیں تین سے کم ہوں عدت اور عدت کے بعد تجدید نکاح کر سکتا ہے
اذا كان الطلاق بائنادون الثلث فله ان يتزوجها فى العدة وبعد انقضائها لان حل المحلية باق لان زواله معلق بالطلقة الثالثة فينعدم قبله ومنع الغير فى العدة لاشتباه النسب و لا اشتباه في اطلاقه
Chapter: What makes the divorced woman lawful. Translation: This chapter is about matters by which a divorced woman becomes lawful. If the divorce is irrevocable (ba'in) and less than three, he may marry her during the waiting period and after its expiry, because the lawfulness of marriage [with her] remains, since its removal is suspended upon the third divorce, so it does not occur before that. And others are prevented during the waiting period due to confusion of lineage, but there is no confusion in his marrying her.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This is the beginning of a new section (fasl) in the chapter on divorce of a sick person. It states the ruling that if a man gives an irrevocable divorce (ba'in) with less than three divorces, he may remarry her during the waiting period or after its expiry. The reason given is that the lawfulness of marriage with her is not completely removed until the third divorce. The prohibition for others to marry her during the waiting period is due to potential confusion of lineage (if she becomes pregnant). However, the original husband is exempt from this prohibition because there is no such confusion for him.

Key Terms
بائنہ (ba'inah): Irrevocably divorced woman, where the husband has no right to take her back without a new marriage contract
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only after she marries another man
D) Never, because ba'in divorce is final

Key Takeaway
A ba'in divorce of less than three does not make remarriage impossible; the husband may remarry her during or after the iddah period.
