Raj'i Talaq and the Permissibility of Intercourse: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on effect of raj'i talaq on intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether sexual intercourse is permitted after raj'i talaq and explain how the right of raj'ah proves the continuity of the marriage bond.

Core Idea
Raj'i talaq does not sever the marriage; the husband's unilateral right of return proves the bond persists.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether a husband may have intercourse with his wife after issuing a revocable (raj'i) divorce. The answer hinges on the legal nature of raj'i talaq: does it immediately end the marriage or merely suspend it? We will follow the reasoning of al-Hidayah and its commentary, focusing on the key proof of the husband's right to take back his wife without her consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What exactly is being disputed? The hukm of sexual intercourse (wati') between a husband and his wife after he has issued a raj'i talaq, during the 'iddah period.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Hanafis say it is halal. Their main proof: the husband has the right of raj'ah (return) without the wife's consent, which proves the marriage bond continues. If the marriage had ended, she would be a stranger and returning would require a new contract.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i says it is haram. His proof: talaq is a severer (qati') of the marital bond, so the wife is no longer lawful for intercourse.
4
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response argues that the severing effect of talaq is postponed. By consensus, the marriage survives until the 'iddah expires. Alternatively, the postponement is out of consideration for the husband's interests.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Hanafi, a husband may have intercourse during the 'iddah, and this counts as a raj'ah, ending the 'iddah and restoring full marital relations. Under Shafi'i, he cannot, and if he wishes to reconcile, he must remarry her with a new contract.

Source Text

باب طلاق المريض
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم تشریح اس حکم میں اختلاف ہے کہ طلاق رجعی وطی کو حرام کر دیتی ہے یا نہیں۔ احناف کے نزدیک طلاق رجعی وطی کو حرام نہیں کرتی ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے مطلقہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ شوہر کا وطی کرنا حرام ہے اور یہی امام احمد سے ایک روایت ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رشتہ زوجیت کی وجہ سے وطی حلال تھی اور قاطع زوجیت یعنی طلاق کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے زوجیت ختم ہوگئی اس وجہ سے مطلقہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ وطی کرنا حرام ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق رجعی کے پائے جانے کے بعد بھی زوجیت قائم ہے اور اسی وجہ سے بغیر عورت کی رضا مندی کے بالاتفاق اس سے مراجعت کرنے کا اختیار ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر زوجیت ختم ہو گئی ہوتی تو یہ عورت اجنبیہ ہوتی اور بغیر اس کی رضا مندی کے رجعت درست نہ ہوتی۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے قیام زوجیت پر استدلال کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ شوہر کو رجعت کا حق اس لئے دیا گیا ہے تا کہ وہ ندامت اور شرمندگی کے وقت اپنی غلطی کا تدارک کر سکے۔ حاصل یہ کہ شوہر کو رجعت کا حق دینے میں شریعت نے اس کا لحاظ رکھا ہے اور شوہر کے ساتھ شفقت کا معاملہ کیا ہے اور شوہر کو رجعت کا حق دینے میں اس کا لحاظ رکھنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ شوہر رجعت کے سلسلہ میں مستقل ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر شوہر رجعت کے حق میں مستقل نہ ہوتا تو اس پر نظر و شفقت مکمل نہ ہوتی۔ اس لئے کہ کبھی عورت رجعت پر راضی نہیں ہوتی۔ پس حق رجعت، رجعت کرنے میں شوہر کے مستقل ہونے کو ثابت کرتا ہے اور رجعت کرنے میں شوہر کا مستقل ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ رجعت بقاء نکاح کا نام ہے نہ کہ ابتداء نکاح کا۔ اس لئے کہ جو دلیل شوہر کے رجعت کرنے میں مستقل ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہے وہ رجعت کے ابتداء نکاح ہونے کے منافی ہے۔ کیونکہ شوہر ابتداء نکاح میں منفرد اور مستقل نہیں ہوتا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ رجعت بقاء نکاح کا نام ہے اور بقاء نکاح کے لئے قیام نکاح ضروری ہے اور قیام نکاح اور وجود نکاح کی صورت میں وطی حرام نہیں ہوتی۔ اس وجہ سے ہمارا مذہب یہ ہے کہ طلاق رجعی وطی کو حرام نہیں کرتی۔ والقاطع آخرہ الی آخرہ سے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب ہے جو اب یہ ہے کہ قاطع یعنی طلاق کا پایا جانا قیام زوجیت کے منافی ہے۔ کیونکہ قاطع یعنی طلاق کا عمل بالاجماع انقضاء عدت تک کے لئے مؤخر ہو گیا ہے۔ یا شوہر پر نظر کرتے ہوئے قاطع کا عمل موخر ہو گیا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Chapter of the Sick Person's Divorce. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 5. Explanation: There is disagreement in this ruling whether raj'i talaq makes intercourse forbidden or not. According to the Hanafis, raj'i talaq does not make intercourse forbidden. Imam al-Shafi'i has stated that for the husband to have intercourse with his raj'i divorcée is forbidden. This is also one narration from Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that intercourse was lawful due to the marital bond, and due to the occurrence of the severer of marriage, i.e., talaq, the marriage ended, therefore intercourse with the raj'i divorcée is forbidden. Our proof is that after the occurrence of raj'i talaq, marital relationship still exists, and for that reason, without the woman's consent, the husband has the right to take her back (raj'ah) by consensus. Thus if marriage had ended, she would be a stranger (ajnabiyyah) and taking her back without her consent would not be valid. The author of al-Hidayah, in proving the continued existence of marriage, has stated that the husband has been given the right of raj'ah so that he can remedy his mistake at the time of regret and shame. The gist is that in giving the husband the right of raj'ah, the Shariah has considered his interest and dealt with him with kindness, and considering that in giving the right of raj'ah indicates that the husband is independent in the matter of raj'ah. Because if the husband were not independent in the right of raj'ah, then consideration and kindness for him would not be complete, for sometimes the woman does not consent to raj'ah. So the right of raj'ah proves the husband's independence in doing raj'ah, and the husband's independence in doing raj'ah is proof that raj'ah is a continuation of marriage, not a new marriage. Because the proof that indicates the husband's independence in doing raj'ah is contrary to raj'ah being a new marriage, since in a new marriage the husband is not alone and independent. So it is established that raj'ah is a continuation of marriage, and for continuation of marriage, the existence of marriage is necessary, and in the presence of marriage, intercourse is not forbidden. For this reason, our madhhab is that raj'i talaq does not make intercourse forbidden. And 'al-qati' akharahu' etc. is a response to Imam al-Shafi'i's proof, which is that the existence of the severer (i.e., talaq) is contrary to the continuance of marriage. Because the operation of the severer (talaq) is postponed by consensus until the end of the 'iddah, or postponed out of consideration for the husband. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the effect of a revocable (raj'i) divorce on the permissibility of sexual intercourse during the 'iddah period. The Hanafi position, supported by the author, is that raj'i talaq does not render intercourse haram because the marriage bond remains intact until the 'iddah expires. The proof is that the husband can take back his wife without her consent (raj'ah), which would be impossible if the marriage had fully dissolved. The opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i is that since talaq severs the marital bond, intercourse becomes forbidden. The commentator, following al-Hidayah, provides a detailed rational argument: the right of raj'ah is given to benefit the husband, implying his independence in returning to his wife, which confirms that raj'ah is a continuation of the existing marriage, not a new contract. Therefore, since the marriage persists, intercourse remains halal. The response to the Shafi'i argument is that the severing effect of talaq is postponed, either by consensus until the 'iddah ends or due to consideration for the husband's interests. The discussion is confined to this specific legal issue and does not address other forms of talaq.

Key Terms
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): A revocable divorce where the husband can take back his wife during the 'iddah without a new contract.
زوجیت (zawjiyyah): The marital bond or relationship between husband and wife.
رجعت (raj'ah): The husband's act of taking back his wife during the 'iddah after a raj'i talaq, without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling on sexual intercourse with a woman who has been given a raj'i talaq during her 'iddah?
A) It is haram because the talaq severs the marriage.
B) It is halal because the marriage bond continues until the 'iddah expires.
C) It is makruh tahrimi and requires kaffarah.
D) It is permissible only if the wife consents.

Key Takeaway
Raj'i talaq does not sever the marriage during the 'iddah; the husband's unilateral right of return proves the bond persists, making intercourse permissible.

Talaq — Divorce

Conditions for a Divorcée to Become Halal for Remarriage
Rulings on remarriage after talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two scenarios of ba'in talaq and state the conditions under which a divorced woman becomes halal for remarriage, applying the Hanafi ruling and proof.

Core Idea
After three talaqs (or two for a slave), remarriage to the first husband requires a genuine intermediate marriage; after fewer, it does not.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the critical distinction in the ruling of remarriage after divorce. While a woman divorced fewer than three times remains halal for her former husband, a woman divorced three times becomes absolutely prohibited until she marries another man and consummates the marriage. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the Quranic verse 2:230.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and identify the two distinct divorce situations discussed: (a) ba'in talaq less than three, and (b) three talaqs for a free woman (or two for a slave).
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For scenario (a), the ruling is that the former husband may remarry her during or after 'iddah without any intermediary. For scenario (b), she is completely haram to the first husband until she marries another man, consummates, and then is divorced or widowed.
3
Locate the primary proof
Identify Quran 2:230 as the primary proof: 'فان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتى تنكح زوجا غيره'. Explain that this verse suspends hulliyyah (permissibility) on the third talaq; before that, it remains.
This verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the objection
The passage responds to the objection from Quran 2:235 (prohibiting marriage contracts during 'iddah). The Hanafi response: the prohibition applies only to outsiders, not the former husband, because the rationale is avoiding lineage confusion – absent in the husband's case.
The key is the 'illah (reason) of the prohibition: confusion of lineage.
5
Derive the condition of consummation
The passage states that for the second marriage to be effective, the second husband must 'enter upon her' (dukhul). This condition is derived from the verse's context to give meaningful effect: otherwise, the marriage alone would not be sufficient.
This is based on isharat al-nass (indication of the text).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مطلقہ بائنہ سے جبکہ طلاقیں تین سے کم ہوں عدت اور عدت کے بعد تجدید نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔
اذا كان الطلاق بائنادون الثلث فله ان يتزوجها فى العدة وبعد انقضائها لان حل المحلية باق لان زواله معلق بالطلقة الثالثة فينعدم قبله ومنع الغير فى العدة لاشتباه النسب و لا اشتباه في اطلاقه.
ترجمہ اور جب تین سے کم طلاق بائن ہو تو شوہر کو اختیار ہے کہ اس عورت سے عدت میں اور عدت گزر جانے کے بعد نکاح کرلے۔ کیونکہ محل کا حلال ہونا باقی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حلت کا زائل ہونا تیسری طلاق پر معلق ہے اور عدت میں غیر ( سے نکاح ) کا ممنوع ہونا نسب کے مشتبہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے اور شوہر سے نکاح کو جائز قرار دینے میں کوئی اشتباہ نہیں ہے۔
تشریح مصنف نے سابق میں ان صورتوں کو بیان فرمایا ہے جن سے طلاق رجعی کا تدارک کیا جا سکتا ہے اور اس علیحدہ فصل میں ان صورتوں کو بیان فرمایا ہے جن کے ذریعہ طلاق رجعی کے علاوہ دوسری طلاقوں کا تدارک کیا جا سکے۔ چنانچہ پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ اگر تین سے کم طلاق بائن ہو، مثلاً ایک بائنہ یا دو بائنہ تو شوہر کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اپنی اس معتدہ سے عدت میں نکاح کرے یا عدت کے بعد دونوں صورتیں صحیح ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ محل (عورت کا بنات آدم میں سے ہونا اور محرمات میں سے نہ ہونا ) کا حلال ہونا باقی ہے کیونکہ حلت کا زائل ہونا تیسری طلاق پر معلق ہے باری تعالیٰ کے قول فان طلقها فلا تحل لہ کی وجہ سے اور معلق بالشرط وجود شرط سے پہلے معدوم ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا تیسری طلاق سے پہلے حلت کا زوال معدوم ہو گا۔ پس جب محل کا حلال ہونا ثابت ہے تو شوہر کیلئے عدت میں نکاح کرنا بھی حلال ہوگا۔
و منع الغير سے اشکال کا جواب ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ آپ نے معتدہ سے نکاح کرنے کی جو علت بیان کی ہے وہ نص کے مقابلہ میں ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے ولا تعزموا عقدة النكاح حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجله ۔ اس آیت میں معتدہ کے ساتھ نکاح کا ارادہ کرنے سے مطلقا منع کیا گیا ہے اور نص کے مقابلہ میں علت قابل قبول نہیں ہوتی، لہذا شوہر کے لئے بھی معتدہ کے ساتھ نکاح کرنا ممنوع ہونا چاہئے۔
جواب: آیت میں معتدہ کے ساتھ نکاح کا ارادہ کرنے سے شوہر کے علاوہ کو منع کیا گیا ہے نہ کہ شوہر کو۔ اس پر قرینہ یہ ہے کہ معدہ کے ساتھ نکاح کی ممانعت اشتباہ نسب کی وجہ سے ہے اور شوہر کے واسطے معدہ کے ساتھ نکاح کو جائز رکھنے میں کوئی اشتباہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مختلف پانیوں کے جمع ہونے سے اشتباہ نسب متحقق ہوگا اور مختلف پانیوں کا جمع ہونا اس وقت ہوگا جب کہ معتدۃ الغیر کے ساتھ نکاح کیا جائے پس معلوم ہوگا کہ اپنی معتدہ کے ساتھ نکاح کرنے میں کوئی قباحت نہیں ہے۔
حرہ کو تین طلاقیں یا باندی کو دو طلاقیں دیدیں حلالہ شرعیہ کے بغیر پہلے شوہر کیلئے حلال نہیں ہوگی زوج آخر دخول کے بعد طلاق دیدے یا فوت ہو جائے تو پہلے شوہر کیلئے عورت حلال ہو جائے گی۔

Section concerning that by which the divorced woman becomes halal. Translation: This section explains matters by which a divorced woman becomes halal. A woman given a ba'in divorce, when the divorces are less than three, he (the husband) can marry her during the 'iddah and after its completion. Arabic text: 'When the divorce is ba'in less than three, he has the right to marry her during the 'iddah and after its expiration, because the lawfulness of the mahall (the woman being legally permissible) remains, since its removal is suspended upon the third divorce, so it is non-existent before that. And the prohibition of others (marrying her) during the 'iddah is due to confusion of lineage, and there is no confusion in her marriage to her (former) husband.' Commentary: The author previously explained the cases by which a raj'i talaq can be remedied, and in this separate section he explains the cases by which other talaqs besides raj'i can be remedied. So the first case: if the talaq is ba'in less than three, e.g., one ba'in or two ba'in, the husband has the option to marry this woman in her 'iddah or after the 'iddah; both are valid. The proof is that the lawfulness of the mahall (the woman being from the category of permissible women and not from the prohibited ones) remains, because the removal of lawfulness is suspended upon the third divorce, as per Allah's statement [Quran 2:230], and that which is suspended upon a condition is non-existent before the condition occurs. So before the third divorce, the removal of lawfulness is non-existent. Thus when the lawfulness of the mahall is established, it becomes halal for the husband to marry her during the 'iddah. 'And the prohibition of others' is a response to an objection. The objection: The cause ('illah) you mentioned for marrying a woman in 'iddah contradicts the text (Quran 2:235), which absolutely prohibits resolving the marriage contract until the prescribed term reaches its end, and a cause cannot be accepted against the text. Therefore, even the husband should be prohibited from marrying his former wife during her 'iddah. The answer: The verse prohibits the resolution of marriage contract with a woman in 'iddah by someone other than the husband, not the husband himself. The indicator is that the prohibition of marriage to a woman in 'iddah is due to the confusion of lineage, and there is no confusion in allowing the husband to marry her, because confusion of lineage occurs when sperm from different men mix; this happens only when a man other than the husband marries her. So it becomes clear that there is no harm in the husband marrying his own former wife in her 'iddah. If he gives a free woman three divorces or a slave woman two, she will not become halal for the first husband without a shari'i halalah (intermediary marriage). After the second husband consummates the marriage, if he divorces her or dies, then the woman becomes halal for the first husband. Arabic text: 'And if the divorce is three in case of a free woman, or two in case of a slave woman, she will not be halal for him until she marries another husband with a valid marriage and he enters upon her, then he (the second husband) divorces her or dies from her. The basis for this is Allah's statement [Quran 2:230]. The intended meaning is the third divorce; and two divorces for a slave woman are like three for a free woman because slave status halves the [limit of] permissible mahalliyyah as has been established. Then the goal (ghayah) is marriage with a husband in absolute terms, and absolute marriage is only established by a valid marriage. The condition of consummation (dukhul) is established by an indication of the text, which is that marriage should be interpreted as [implying] natural intercourse, so that the words produce benefit instead of being redundant, since the contract is already beneficial.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section (Fasl) detailing the circumstances under which a divorced woman becomes legally permissible (halal) for her former husband to remarry. The author distinguishes between two scenarios. First, if the divorce is ba'in but less than three (e.g., one or two ba'in talaqs), the husband may remarry her during her 'iddah or after it without needing an intermediary. The proof is that the woman's essential permissibility (hulliyyah) remains intact because it is only removed by the third talaq, as per Quran 2:230. The objection from verse 2:235 (prohibiting marriage contracts with women in 'iddah) is addressed: that prohibition applies only to men other than the former husband, as the rationale is to avoid confusion of lineage—a concern absent when the former husband marries her. Second, if a free woman receives three talaqs or a slave woman two, she becomes absolutely prohibited to the first husband until she marries another man in a valid marriage, consummates it, and then is divorced or widowed. This is directly based on Quran 2:230, with the slave woman's limit reduced to two due to her status (al-riqq yunassif). The condition of consummation (dukhul) is derived from the Quranic context to give meaningful effect to the verse rather than redundancy.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage contract.
حلت (hulliyyah): The legal permissibility of a woman for a man to marry. It is removed only by the third talaq (or second for a slave).
حلالہ شرعیہ (halalah shar'iyyah): A valid marriage with another man intended to make a woman permissible for her first husband after three talaqs, but without prior agreement to divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, after how many talaqs does a free woman need an intermediary marriage to become halal for her first husband?
A) After any divorce.
B) After two talaqs.
C) After three talaqs.
D) After four talaqs.

Key Takeaway
The essential legal point: the third talaq removes hulliyyah; a genuine intermediate marriage with consummation restores it; fewer talaqs leave hulliyyah intact.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Remarrying the Wife After Less Than Three Revocable Divorces
States ruling that husband may remarry wife during iddah after less than three bā'in divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on remarrying a wife after less than three bā'in divorces and explain the proof from the Quran and the response to the objection.

Core Idea
A husband may remarry his wife during iddah after fewer than three bā'in divorces.

This passage addresses a specific case in divorce law: when a husband pronounces fewer than three bā'in (irrevocable) divorces, does he retain the right to remarry his wife during her waiting period (iddah)? The Hanafi ruling permits it, based on a careful reading of Quranic verses and the rationale behind the prohibition on marriage during iddah. We will explore the proof, the objection, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that after less than three bā'in divorces, the husband may remarry the wife during iddah or after. Note that this applies only to bā'in divorces (not revocable ones) and only when the count is less than three.
The ruling does not apply if the divorce was the third, which makes the wife permanently prohibited unless she marries another.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The author cites Quran 2:230 ('Then if he divorces her, she is not lawful to him after that until she marries another husband') to argue that lawfulness is only removed by the third divorce. The word 'after' indicates a condition — the prohibition is contingent on the third occurrence.
This is a dalīl from the Quran, a primary source.
3
Address the counter-evidence
An objector raises Quran 2:235 ('nor resolve on the marriage contract until the book reaches its term') which seems to prohibit all marriages during iddah. The Hanafi response distinguishes between a stranger and the original husband.
The key move is to limit the general verse by the underlying rationale (ʿillah).
4
Understand the rationale (ʿillah)
The prohibition on marrying a woman in iddah is due to confusion of lineage (ikhtilāṭ al-nasab). This only arises if a stranger (ghayr) marries her, as the mixing of different men's sperm (māʾ) could confuse paternity. For the original husband, there is no such confusion.
Thus the ʿillah (reason) restricts the general verse to non-husbands.
5
Conclude and note the practical effect
Since the wife remains lawful (ḥill) until the third divorce, and the prohibition during iddah is inapplicable to the husband, the remarriage is permissible (jāʾiz). The ḥukm is mubāḥ (permissible).
This ruling is muftā bihī in the Hanafi school.

Chapter on the divorce of the sick. 56. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Five. Translation: And when there is less than three revocable divorces, the husband has the option to marry this woman during the iddah and after the iddah passes. Because the lawfulness of the subject (the woman) remains. This is because the removal of lawfulness is contingent upon the third divorce, and the prohibition of marriage (to another) during iddah is due to the confusion of lineage, and there is no confusion in permitting marriage to the husband. Explanation: The author has previously mentioned the cases by which a revocable divorce can be rectified, and in this separate section he mentions the cases by which divorces other than revocable can be rectified. So the first case is that if the revocable divorce is less than three, e.g. one or two revocable divorces, then the husband has the option to marry his wife during iddah or after iddah; both cases are valid. The proof is that the lawfulness of the subject (the woman being from the children of Adam and not from the prohibited) remains, because the removal of lawfulness is contingent upon the third divorce, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then if he divorces her, she is not lawful to him after that...' and a contingent upon a condition is non-existent before the existence of the condition. Therefore before the third divorce, the removal of lawfulness is non-existent. So when the lawfulness of the subject is proven, then for the husband it will also be lawful to marry during iddah. And 'the prohibition of another' is an answer to an objection. The objection is that the cause you mentioned for marrying the woman undergoing iddah is against the text (nass), because Allah Most High said: 'And do not determine the marriage contract until the book reaches its term.' In this verse, intending marriage with a woman undergoing iddah is absolutely prohibited, and a cause against the text is not acceptable, so for the husband also, marrying a woman undergoing iddah should be prohibited. The answer: In the verse, intending marriage with a woman undergoing iddah is prohibited for someone other than the husband, not for the husband. The evidence for this is that the prohibition of marriage with a woman undergoing iddah is due to confusion of lineage, and for the husband, there is no confusion in permitting marriage with the woman undergoing iddah because confusion of lineage occurs due to the collection of different waters, and the collection of different waters occurs when one marries a woman undergoing iddah of another. So it is known that there is no defect in marrying one's own woman undergoing iddah.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and rational deduction. The author first states the ruling: if a husband gives fewer than three revocable (bā'in) divorces, he may remarry his wife during her iddah or after it. The reason given is that the wife's lawfulness (ḥill) remains because the removal of lawfulness is tied to the third divorce. The author then addresses an objection based on the verse 'nor resolve on the marriage contract until the book reaches its term' (2:235). The objector claims this prohibits any marriage during iddah, even to the original husband. The answer distinguishes between a stranger and the original husband: the prohibition is due to confusion of lineage (which only occurs if a stranger marries her), so the husband is exempt. This follows the Hanafi position that the verse applies to others, not the original husband. The proof uses the principle that a condition (third divorce) before its occurrence is non-existent.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (ṭalāq bā'in): A divorce that is not revocable (rajʿī), meaning the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage and consent, but if fewer than three, remarriage is possible.
عدت (ʿiddah): The waiting period after divorce or death during which a woman cannot remarry; for a divorced woman, it is three menstrual cycles or three months.
محل (maḥall): The subject of the ruling, here the woman, indicating her basic lawfulness for marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a husband remarry his wife during her iddah after giving one revocable (bā'in) divorce?
A) No, because the verse prohibits all marriage during iddah.
B) Yes, because the prohibition is only for a stranger to avoid confusion of lineage.
C) Yes, but only after the iddah ends.
D) No, because the wife becomes permanently forbidden.

Key Takeaway
A husband may remarry his wife during her iddah after less than three bā'in divorces because the Quranic prohibition is limited to non-husbands to avoid lineage confusion.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for Halalah After Three Divorces
Explains ruling with proofs and a minor ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a woman divorced thrice to become lawful for her first husband and explain the primary proofs (Quran and hadith) used to derive these conditions.

Core Idea
Three divorces require halalah: valid marriage, consummation, and separation from a second husband.

The finality of three divorces in the Hanafi school creates a severe prohibition (ḥurmat ghalīẓah). Remarriage with the first husband is impossible unless a specific legal process—ḥalālah—is completed. This lesson unpacks the conditions derived from the Quran, hadith, and scholarly consensus, clarifying what is required and what is not, and addresses a minor dissenting view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine the legal situation: a free woman divorced three times or a slave woman divorced twice. The ruling is that she becomes unlawful (ḥarām) for the first husband until certain conditions are met.
The number differs due to slavery halving the 'lawfulness' of the subject.
2
List the conditions for halalah
The conditions are: (1) a valid marriage (nikāḥ ṣaḥīḥ) with a second husband, (2) actual consummation (dukhūl/īlāj) in that marriage, and (3) separation from the second husband by divorce or death. Note that ejaculation (inzāl) is not required.
The condition of consummation is derived via ishārat al-naṣṣ from the Quranic word 'tankīḥ' (marry) interpreted as intercourse.
3
Examine the primary proofs
The Quranic proof is verse 2:230: 'fain tallaqahā fala taḥillu lahu min ba‘du ḥattā tankiḥa zawjan ghayrah.' The hadith proof is the famous hadith: 'lā taḥillu li-l-awwal ḥattā tadhūqa ‘usaylata al-ākhar.' Both establish the necessity of a second marriage and consummation.
The hadith is mutawātir in meaning (ma‘nawī) and agreed upon except by Sa‘īd ibn al-Musayyib.
4
Analyze the derivation for a slave woman
For a slave woman, two divorces create the same severe prohibition as three for a free woman. This is based on qiyās from the principle that slavery halves punishment (Quran 4:25) and similarly halves the number of divorces required for the prohibition.
Since divorce cannot be fractional, two complete divorces are required.
5
Address the minor scholarly disagreement
Sa‘īd ibn al-Musayyib held that halalah is not required. The Hanafi school rejects his view as non-binding (ghayr mu‘tabar), relying on the consensus of the majority and the clear texts.
Even if a judge rules by his opinion, the ruling is not enforceable.

دیدے یا مر جائے ۔
اس مسئلہ میں دلیل قرآن پاک کی آیت فان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتی تنکح زوجا غیرہ ہے اور اس آیت میں اکثر مفسرین کے نزدیک تیسری طلاق مراد ہے اور باندی کے حق میں دو طلاقیں ایسی ہیں جیسے آزاد عورت کے حق میں تین طلاقیں یعنی جس طرح آزاد عورت میں تین طلاقوں سے حرمت غلیظہ ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اس طرح باندی میں دو طلاقوں سے حرمت غلیظہ ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رقیق ہونے کی وجہ سے عذاب نصف رہ جاتا ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشا در بانی ہے فان اتین بفاحشة فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب - یعنی اگر وہ باندیاں زنا کا ارتکاب کریں تو ان پر اس عذاب یعنی سزا کا نصف ہوگا جو آزاد عورتوں پر ہے۔ پس جس طرح رقیق ہونا عذاب اور سزا کو نصف کر دینے کا سبب ہے۔ اسی طرح رقیق ہونا نعمت کو آدھا کر دینے کا بھی سبب ہے اور محل کا جلال ہو نا نعمت ہے۔ لہذا باندی کیلئے صرف ایک اور آدھی طلاق دینے سے حرجت غلیظہ ثابت ہوئی چاہیے تھی ۔ مگر چونکہ طلاق متجری نہیں ہوتی اس لئے وہ آدھی بھی پوری ہو جائے گی اور باندی کا شو ہر دو
طلاقوں کا مالک ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ زوج ثانی کے ساتھ نکاح صحیح کا ہونا اس لئے ضروری ہے آیت حتی تنکح زوجا غیرہ میں
If a free woman is given three divorces or a slave woman two, she will not be lawful for the husband without a legal halalah. The last husband divorces after consummation or dies, then the woman becomes lawful for the first husband. And if the divorce is three for a free woman or two for a slave woman, she is not lawful for him until she marries another husband a valid marriage and he enters upon her (consummates), then he divorces her or dies from her. The basis of this is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him after that until she marries another husband.' And what is meant is the third divorce. And two in the case of a slave woman are like three in the case of a free woman, because being a slave halves the lawfulness of the subject (mahall), as known. Then the ultimate object is the marriage of the husband absolutely, and absolute marriage is only established by a valid marriage. And the condition of consummation is proven by the indication of the text (ishārat al-nass), which is that marriage should be interpreted as intercourse (watanī), carrying the speech for benefit, not repetition, because the contract is already understood from the word 'husband'. Or there is an addition to the text by the famous hadith, which is his saying (peace be upon him): 'She is not lawful for the first until she tastes the sweetness of the other.' It is related in multiple narrations, and there is no disagreement about it except from Sa'īd ibn al-Musayyib (may Allah be pleased with him), and his saying is not considered; even if a judge rules by it, it is not enforceable. And the condition is insertion (īlāj) not ejaculation (inzāl), because ejaculation is completeness and intensification, and completeness is an extra condition. Translation: And if a free woman has three divorces or a slave woman two, then she is not lawful for the husband until she makes a valid marriage with another husband and he performs consummation with her. Then he divorces her or dies leaving her. And the proof in this issue is the saying of Allah Most High, i.e. 'Then if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him after that until she marries another husband.' And in the verse the third divorce is meant, and for a slave woman two are like three for a free woman. Because being a slave halves the lawfulness of the subject. As is known in the principles. Then the ultimate object is absolutely the marriage of another husband, and absolute marriage is only established by a valid marriage. And the condition of consummation is proven by ishārat al-nass, which is that marriage should be interpreted as intercourse, interpreting the speech for benefit, not repetition. Because the contract is already derived from the word 'husband'. Or there is an addition to the text by the famous hadith, the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'She is not lawful for the first until she tastes the sweetness of the other.' This hadith is narrated in multiple ways and there is no disagreement about it except from Sa'īd ibn al-Musayyib (may Allah be pleased with him), and his saying is not considered; even if a judge rules by it, it is not enforceable. And the condition is insertion (īlāj) not ejaculation (inzāl), because ejaculation is completeness and intensification, and completeness is an extra condition. Explanation: The issue is that if a person gives his free wife three divorces or his married slave woman two divorces, then this woman will not be lawful for him until she makes a valid marriage with another husband and that other husband consummates with her, then he divorces her or dies. In this issue, the proof is the Quranic verse 'fain tallaqahā...' and in this verse, according to most commentators, the third divorce is meant. And for a slave woman, two divorces are like three for a free woman, i.e. just as three divorces for a free woman establish severe unlawfulness (ḥurmat ghalīẓah), similarly two divorces for a slave woman establish severe unlawfulness. The proof is that due to being a slave, punishment is halved. As Allah says: 'And if they commit indecency, then on them is half the punishment of what is on the free women.' So just as being a slave causes punishment to be halved, similarly being a slave also causes a blessing to be halved, and the lawfulness of the subject (maḥall) is a blessing. Therefore, for a slave woman, it should have taken one and a half divorces to establish severe unlawfulness. But since divorce is not divisible, that half becomes a whole, and the husband of a slave woman owns two divorces. The author of Hidayah says that a valid marriage with the second husband is necessary because of the verse 'until she marries another husband'.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and the famous hadith, along with an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf. The ruling: after three divorces (for a free woman) or two divorces (for a slave woman), the wife is not lawful for the first husband until she marries another husband in a valid marriage, that husband consummates the marriage (dakhūl), and then he divorces her or dies. The primary proof is the Quranic verse 2:230 ('fain tallaqahā...'), interpreted as the third divorce. For a slave woman, the number is halved to two because slavery halves the lawfulness of the subject (qawl: al-raqq munṣif). This is derived from the principle that punishment is halved for slaves (Quran 4:25). Since divorce cannot be fractional, two are required. The condition of consummation (dakhūl) is established by ishārat al-nass: the word 'marry' in the verse is interpreted as sexual intercourse to give benefit to the speech, not mere repetition. The famous hadith 'lā taḥillu li-l-awwal...' is cited as additional support, and it is agreed upon except for Sa'īd ibn al-Musayyib, whose opinion is disregarded. The condition is limited to insertion (īlāj), not ejaculation (inzāl), because ejaculation is an extra perfection.

Key Terms
حلالہ شرعیہ (ḥalālah sharʿiyyah): The legal process by which a woman divorced three times becomes lawful for her first husband by marrying another husband, consummating, and separating.
دخول (dukhūl): Sexual intercourse (actual penetration) between the second husband and the wife.
اشارة النص (ishārat al-naṣṣ): An implicit indication in the text (Quran) that the word 'marriage' (nikāḥ) is interpreted as sexual intercourse (waṭʾ) to give benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum condition for consummation (dakhūl) in the halalah marriage?
A) Ejaculation (inzāl)
B) Insertion (īlāj) with or without ejaculation
C) Both insertion and ejaculation
D) Mere marriage contract without consummation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a valid marriage, consummation, and separation for halalah after three divorces; ejaculation is not required.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Conditions for Tahlīl: Quran and Hadith Proofs
Ruling with proof: conditions for tahlīl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for tahlīl (valid marriage and consummation) and derive them from the Quran (2:230) and the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
Tahlīl requires both valid marriage and consummation; the Qur'an and hadith together establish this.

The Hanafi school holds that a woman divorced three times cannot return to her first husband until she marries another man, consummates the marriage, and then separates. This lesson unpacks the two proofs—the Quranic verse and the famous hadith—that establish the condition of intercourse, and explains why the opposing view of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab is rejected.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its conditions
Identify the core ruling: a thrice-divorced free woman (or twice-divorced slave woman) is not lawful for her first husband until she marries another man with a valid marriage and performs intercourse. Note the two conditions: (1) valid marriage, (2) consummation.
The ruling itself is not in dispute; the condition of consummation is what requires proof.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Refer to Quran 2:230: 'And if he divorces her, then she is not lawful for him after that until she marries another husband.' The word 'nikah' (marriage) is absolute, implying a valid marriage. The condition of intercourse is derived via 'isharat al-nass'.
The verse itself does not explicitly mention intercourse; it is derived from the implication that 'nikah' here means intercourse to avoid repetition.
3
Analyze the derivation of intercourse from 'isharat al-nass'
The word 'zawj' (husband) already implies a marriage contract, so interpreting 'nikah' as contract would be repetition. Instead, 'nikah' is interpreted as intercourse to give new benefit (ta'sis). This is the Hanafi method of 'isharat al-nass'.
The rule: 'al-ifada khayr min al-i'ada' (benefit is better than repetition).
4
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'No, until you taste his sweetness and he tastes your sweetness' (mashhur hadith). This explicitly requires intercourse. The hadith is widely transmitted and allows adding a condition to the Quranic text.
The hadith is considered mashhur (well-known) and thus can be used to add to the Quran in Hanafi usul.
5
Understand the dispute and its resolution
Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab did not require consummation. The Hanafi response: his opinion is non-credible because the hadith is clear. A judge's verdict based on it is void, and a mufti giving such a fatwa is cursed.
The practical consequence: the Hanafi position is the only enforceable one in Hanafi courts.
6
Specify the minimum of consummation
The condition is insertion of the glans (ilaj al-hashafa), not ejaculation. Ejaculation is perfection (kamaal) and not required.
The text emphasizes that the minimum is insertion, as perfection is an extra condition not proven by the dalil.

اور زوج ثانی کا اس عورت کے ساتھ وطی کرنا شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے اشارۃ النص سے یا حدیث مشہور سے اشارۃ النص کی صورت میں تقریر یہ ہوگی کہ آیت حتی تنکح زوجا غیرہ میں لفظ نکاح کو وطی کے معنی پر محمول کیا جائے نہ کہ عقد کے معنی پر کیونکہ آیت میں عقد کے معنی زو جا غیرہ سے مستفاد ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ کوئی شخص بغیر عقد کے زوج نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ پس اگر لفظ تشلح میں نکاح سے عقد کے معنی مراد لئے جائیں تو کلام میں تاکید ہوگی اور اگر نکاح کو ولی پر محمول کریں تو کلام میں تاسیس ہوگی اور قاعدہ ہے الافادة خير من الاعادة یعنی تاسیس بہتر ہے تاکید سے اس لئے آیت میں نکاح کو وطی کے معنی پر محمول کریں گے پس اس تقریر پر زوج نانی کا وطی کرنا ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
اور حدیث سے شرط دخول اس طرح ثابت ہوگی کہ رفاعہ نے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانے میں اپنی بیوی کو تین طلاق دیں ۔ پھر اس نے عبدالرحمن بن زبیر سے شادی رچالی ۔ پھر حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس آکر کہنے لگی کہ اے اللہ کے رسول رفاعہ نے مجھ کو تین طلاقیں دیں پھر میں نے عبدالرحمن سے نکاح کر لیا مگر میں نے عبدالرحمن کو نا مرد پایا۔ آپ نے فرمایا اتريدين ان تعودي الى رفاعة - اس نے کہا جی ہاں میرا ارادہ یہی ہے آپ نے فرمایا لا حتى تذوقی عسلیته و يذوق عسیلتک یعنی نہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ تو اس کا مزہ چکھ لے اور وہ تیرا مزہ چکھ لے۔ اس سے کنایہ وطی مراد ہے پس اس حدیث سے ثابت ہو گیا ہے کہ حلالہ کے لئے زوج ثانی کا وطی کرنا شرط ہے اور یہ حدیث مشہور ہے اور حدیث مشہور سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی کرنا جائز ہے۔ لہذا اگر آیت حتی تنکے میں نکاح سے ولی کے معنی مراد نہ لئے جائیں تو اس آیت کو اس حدیث مشہور کے ساتھ مقید کر دیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ دخول کی شرط لگانے میں علاوہ سعید بن المسیب کے کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے اور حدیث مشہور کی وجہ سے سعید بن المسیب کا قول غیر معتبر ہے ۔ حتی کہ اگر کسی قاضی نے سعید بن المسیب کے قول پر فیصلہ صادر کیا تو اس فیصلہ کو نافذ نہیں کیا جائے گا اور اگر کسی مفتی نے اس پر فتوی دیا تو اس پر اللہ کی لعنت ملائکہ کی لعنت اور تمام لوگوں کی لعنت ۔ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ) اور زوج اول کے واسطے مطلقہ ثلاثہ کے حلال ہونے کی شرط زوج نانی کا عورت کی شرمگاہ میں حشفہ کا داخل کرنا ہے انزال یعنی منی کا پکا نا شرط نہیں ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ انزال ادخال میں کمال اور مبالغہ ہے اور کمال قید زائد ہے بغیر دلیل کے ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Chapter of the Sick Person's Divorce. Ashraf al-Hidayah commentary in Urdu on al-Hidayah, Volume 5. With the utterance of the husband's name or increase upon the text by the famous hadith, which is his statement, peace be upon him: 'She is not lawful for the first until she tastes the sweetness of the other.' It is narrated with multiple chains and there is no disagreement in it except from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, may Allah be pleased with him, and his statement is not considered, even if a judge passes a verdict based on it, it is not executed. The condition is insertion without ejaculation because it is perfection and exaggeration, and perfection is an extra restriction. Translation: And if a free woman has three divorces or a slave woman has two, then she is not lawful for the husband until she marries another husband with a valid marriage and he performs intercourse with her. Then he divorces her or dies. The proof in this matter is the statement of Allah Most High: 'And if he divorces her, then she is not lawful for him after that until she marries another husband.' (Quran 2:230). And in the verse, the third divorce is meant. And for a slave woman, two are like three for a free woman, because being a slave halves the lawfulness of the place, as is known in the principles. Then the extreme limit is absolutely the marriage of another husband, and the absolute is established by valid marriage. And the condition of intercourse is established by indication of the text (isharat al-nass). And the indication of the text is that marriage (nikah) is interpreted as intercourse (wati), carrying the speech for benefit not repetition, because the contract is derived from the utterance of 'husband' (zawj). Or increase upon the text by the famous hadith, and the famous hadith is the statement of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'She is not lawful for the first' i.e., the thrice-divorced woman will not be lawful for the first husband until she tastes the sweetness of another. This hadith is transmitted with multiple narrations and there is no disagreement in it except from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, and Sa'id's statement is not considered. Even if a judge passes a verdict based on it, it will not be executed. And the condition is insertion, not ejaculation, because ejaculation is perfection and exaggeration in intercourse, and perfection is an extra restriction. Explanation of the issue: If a person gives his free wife three divorces or his married slave woman two divorces, then this woman will not be lawful for the husband until she marries another husband with a valid marriage and the second husband performs intercourse with her, then he divorces her or dies. The proof in this issue is the Quranic verse: 'And if he divorces her, then she is not lawful for him after that until she marries another husband.' And most commentators interpret this verse as referring to the third divorce. And for a slave woman, two divorces are like three for a free woman, i.e., just as severe prohibition (hurmat ghaliza) is established by three divorces for a free woman, similarly for a slave woman, severe prohibition is established by two divorces. The proof is that due to being a slave, punishment is halved. As Allah says: 'And if they commit immorality, then for them is half the punishment of that for free women.' (Quran 4:25). So just as being a slave causes punishment to be halved, similarly being a slave also causes the blessing to be halved, and the lawfulness of the place is a blessing. Therefore, for a slave woman, severe prohibition should have been established by one and a half divorces, but since divorce is not divisible, that half becomes whole, and the husband of a slave woman owns two divorces. The author of al-Hidayah says: The necessity of a valid marriage with the second husband is because in the verse 'until she marries another husband', the extreme limit (ghaya) i.e., the marriage of the second husband is absolute, not restricted by validity or invalidity. And when an absolute is uttered, it means the perfect individual. Therefore, here absolute matrimony means perfect matrimony, and perfect matrimony is established by a valid marriage. For this reason, we have made valid marriage a condition for tahlil. And the condition of intercourse with the woman by the second husband is established either by indication of the text or by the famous hadith. In the case of indication of the text, the explanation is that in the verse 'until she marries another husband', the word 'nikah' is to be interpreted in the meaning of intercourse, not in the meaning of contract, because the meaning of contract is already derived from the word 'husband' (zawj). Since no one can be a husband without a contract, if we interpret 'nikah' as contract, it would be a repetition (ta'kid) in the speech. If we interpret 'nikah' as intercourse, then it is a new benefit (ta'sis). And the rule is: 'al-ifada khayr min al-i'ada' (benefit is better than repetition). Therefore, we interpret 'nikah' as intercourse, and thus the condition of intercourse by the second husband is proven. And from the hadith, the condition of intercourse is established as follows: Rifa'ah divorced his wife three times during the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him. Then she married 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr. Then she came to the Prophet and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, Rifa'ah divorced me three times, then I married 'Abd al-Rahman, but I found him impotent.' The Prophet said: 'Do you want to return to Rifa'ah?' She said: 'Yes, that is my intention.' He said: 'No, until you taste his sweetness and he tastes your sweetness.' This is a metaphor for intercourse. Thus, this hadith proves that for tahlil, intercourse by the second husband is a condition. And this hadith is mashhur (widely transmitted), and it is permissible to increase upon the Book of Allah with a mashhur hadith. Therefore, if we do not interpret 'nikah' in the verse as intercourse, then this verse is restricted by this mashhur hadith. The author of al-Hidayah said: In establishing the condition of intercourse, there is no disagreement except from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, and due to the mashhur hadith, Sa'id's statement is not considered. Even if a judge passes a verdict based on Sa'id's statement, that verdict will not be executed. And if a mufti gives a fatwa based on it, then upon him is the curse of Allah, the curse of the angels, and the curse of all people. (From 'Ayni's commentary on al-Hidayah). And the condition for the thrice-divorced woman to become lawful for the first husband is that the second husband inserts the glans (hashafa) into the woman's vagina. Ejaculation (inzal) is not a condition. The proof is that ejaculation is perfection and exaggeration in insertion, and perfection is an extra restriction that cannot be established without proof. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and Hadith on the conditions for a woman divorced three times to become lawful again for her first husband (tahlil). The author begins by stating the ruling: a free woman divorced thrice or a slave woman divorced twice is not lawful for her husband until she marries another man and consummates the marriage. The Quranic proof is from Surah al-Baqara 2:230, where 'until she marries another husband' is interpreted by most commentators as referring to the third divorce. For a slave woman, two divorces establish the same severe prohibition (hurmat ghaliza) because being a slave halves matters, as seen in the Quranic verse on punishment (4:25). The author then explains two proofs for the condition of intercourse: (1) isharat al-nass: the word 'nikah' in the verse is interpreted as intercourse rather than contract, since the contract is already implied by the word 'husband'. This yields a new benefit (ta'sis) rather than repetition (ta'kid). (2) The famous hadith of the Prophet where he told a woman she must taste the sweetness of her second husband before returning to the first. This hadith is mashhur (widely transmitted) and allows adding a condition (intercourse) to the Quranic text. The author refutes the opinion of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, who apparently did not require intercourse. The author declares his opinion non-credible, citing that even a judge's verdict based on it would not be enforced. Finally, the condition is specified as insertion of the glans (ilaj), not ejaculation (inzal), since ejaculation is merely perfection. The commentary follows the order of the original text: first the ruling, then the Quranic proof, the slave woman analogy, the two proofs for intercourse, the refutation of the opposing view, and the precise definition of the condition.

Key Terms
تحلیل (tahlīl): The process by which a thrice-divorced woman becomes lawful to her first husband by marrying and consummating with a second husband, who then divorces her or dies.
حرمت غلیظہ (hurmat ghalīẓa): Severe prohibition that prevents a husband from remarrying his wife after three divorces (or two for a slave woman) without tahlil.
اشارۃ النص (ishārat al-naṣṣ): An implied indication from the text (Quran) that yields a ruling without being the primary meaning; here, the word 'nikah' implies intercourse.
حدیث مشہور (hadīth mashhūr): A widely transmitted hadith that is below mutawatir but above ahad; it can be used to add to the Quran according to Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum condition for consummation in tahlil according to the Hanafi school?
A) Ejaculation (inzal)
B) Insertion of the glans (ilaj al-hashafa)
C) Both insertion and ejaculation
D) Any form of intimacy

Key Takeaway
Tahlīl requires both a valid marriage and consummation (insertion of the glans) based on the Quran and the mashhur hadith; the opinion of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab is rejected.

The Murahiq Boy in Tahlīl: Consummation Over Adulthood
Ruling with proof on the murahiq boy in tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a murahiq boy in tahlil and explain why the condition of consummation is fulfilled regardless of the husband's age.

Core Idea
A murahiq boy is like an adult in tahlil because consummation, not adulthood, is the condition.

The Hanafi school holds that the condition for tahlil (making a thrice-divorced woman lawful to her first husband) is actual consummation in a valid marriage, not the husband's age. This lesson examines how a minor boy who is close to puberty (murahiq) fulfills this condition, leading to a valid tahlil. We will also explore the disagreement of Imam Malik and the Hanafi proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is tahlil: a second marriage with consummation that makes the woman halal for her first husband. The ruling is that a murahiq boy is like an adult in effecting this.
2
Locate the Condition (Shart)
The condition is dukhul (penetration) in a valid nikah, established by the text (nas). The text does not specify an age requirement.
3
Note the Ikhtilaf
Imam Malik disagrees, possibly requiring the second husband to be an adult. The Hanafi response is based on the same textual evidence.
4
Follow the Proof from Al-Jami' al-Saghir
The author cites al-Jami' al-Saghir: if a boy like him (capable) consummates, ghusl becomes obligatory on the woman due to the meeting of the circumcised parts, and she becomes lawful to the first husband. This shows the condition is fulfilled.
Ghusl here indicates consummation, not the boy's age.
5
Confirm the Practical Outcome
Thus, under Hanafi fiqh, a woman can become halal to her first husband by marrying a murahiq boy and consummating.

Source Text

والصبي المراهق في التحليل كالبالغ لوجود الدخول فى نكاح صحيح وهو شرط بالنص ومالك يخالفنا فيه والحجة عليه ما بيناه وفسره فى الجامع الصغير وقال غلام لم يبلغ ومثله يجامع جامع امرأة وجب عليها الغسل واحلها على الزوج الاول ومعنى هذا الكلام ان يتحرك الله ويشتهى وانما وجب الغسل عليها لالتقا الختانين وهو سبب لنزول مائها والحاجة الى الايجاب فى حقها امالا غسل على الصبى وان كان
And the minor boy approaching puberty (sabi murahiq) in tahlil is like an adult because intercourse exists in a valid marriage, and it is a condition by the text. And Malik differs with us in it, and the proof against him is what we have explained. And he (the author) explained it in al-Jami' al-Saghir and said: A boy who has not reached puberty but someone like him engages in intercourse with a woman, then ghusl becomes obligatory on her and she becomes lawful for the first husband. The meaning of this statement is that he moves (?) and desires. And ghusl is obligatory on her only due to the meeting of the circumcised parts, which is a cause for the descent of her fluid. And the need for obligation is on her part, but there is no ghusl on the boy even if...

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that a minor boy on the verge of puberty (sabi murahiq) is like an adult in effecting tahlil (making a thrice-divorced woman lawful to her first husband). The reason is that the condition for tahlil is consummation (dukhul) in a valid marriage, and this condition is established by the text (Quran and Hadith). Even if the boy has not reached puberty, if he is capable of intercourse (i.e., he is a murahiq, close to puberty, and has sexual desire), his consummation fulfills the condition. The author mentions that Imam Malik disagrees with the Hanafi position on this point. The Hanafi proof against Malik is what was already explained in the previous discussion (the hadith and Quranic interpretation). The author then refers to al-Jami' al-Saghir, where it is explained that if a boy who has not reached puberty but is similar (i.e., capable) engages in intercourse with a woman, ghusl becomes obligatory on her, and she becomes lawful for the first husband. The reason ghusl becomes obligatory on her is the meeting of the circumcised parts (i.e., penetration), which causes her fluid to descend. However, ghusl is not obligatory on the boy, even if (the text cuts off). The commentary follows the order: first the ruling, then the condition (dukhul in a valid marriage), then the ikhtilaf with Malik, then the explanation from al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Key Terms
صبی مراہق (ṣabī murāhiq): A boy who is close to puberty (usually aged 12-15) and shows signs of sexual desire, capable of intercourse.
دخول (dukhūl): Penetration, specifically the insertion of the glans into the vagina, which is the minimum requirement for consummation.

Key Takeaway

The Condition of Du Khul for Tahlil: Quranic and Hadith Proofs
Establishing through Quran and hadith that penetration is required for tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for tahlil and explain the Quranic and hadith evidences that establish it.

Core Idea
Only penetration (du khul) is required for tahlil, not emission — established by Quran and hadith through the principle that ta'sis is preferred over ta'kid.

Tahlil, the process by which a thrice-divorced woman becomes halal for her first husband, requires a valid marriage and consummation with a second husband. The Hanafi school uniquely specifies that consummation means actual penetration (du khul), not merely emission. This ruling is derived from a careful interpretation of the Quranic verse and a well-known hadith. Understanding the proofs and the interpretative principle involved strengthens your ability to trace a fiqh ruling back to its sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the passage addresses the condition for tahlil — what precisely the second husband must do for the woman to become halal for the first husband.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence and interpretative principle
Examine the verse 'until she marries another husband' (2:230). The Hanafis interpret 'nikah' as intercourse rather than contract because the word 'zawj' already implies a contract. This follows the principle that establishing a new meaning (ta'sis) is better than emphasis (ta'kid).
The rule 'al-ifadah khayr min al-i'adah' (bringing benefit is better than repetition) is used.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
Study the hadith of Rifa'ah where the Prophet ﷺ said 'No, until you taste his sweetness and he tastes your sweetness.' This metaphor for intercourse establishes du khul as a condition. The hadith is well-known (mashhur) and can add to the Quranic text.
Well-known hadiths (mashhur) are considered strong enough to specify or qualify Quranic generalities.
4
Note the dissenting opinion and Hanafi response
Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib differed, but his view is rejected because it contradicts the well-known hadith. A judge or mufti acting on his opinion faces severe censure.
The passage emphasizes that only Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib held this view; all others agree with the Hanafi position.
5
Determine the precise condition
The condition is insertion of the glans (hashafah), not emission. Emission is a perfection that cannot be required without proof.
This distinction is important for practical application.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
غایت یعنی نکاح زوج ثانی مطلق ہے صحت یا فساد کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے اور مطلق جب بولا جاتا ہے تو اس سے فرد کامل مراد ہوتا ہے لہذا یہاں زوجیت مطلقہ سے زوجیت کا ملہ مراد ہوگی اور زوجیت کاملہ نکاح صحیح سے ثابت ہوتی ہے اس وجہ سے ہم نے حلالہ کے لیے نکاح سیح کو شرط قرار دیا۔
اور زوج ثانی کا اس عورت کے ساتھ وطی کرنا شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے اشارۃ النص سے یا حدیث مشہور سے اشارۃ النص کی صورت میں تقریر یہ ہوگی کہ آیت حتی تنکح زوجا غیرہ میں لفظ نکاح کو وطی کے معنی پر محمول کیا جائے نہ کہ عقد کے معنی پر کیونکہ آیت میں عقد کے معنی زو جا غیرہ سے مستفاد ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ کوئی شخص بغیر عقد کے زوج نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ پس اگر لفظ تشلح میں نکاح سے عقد کے معنی مراد لئے جائیں تو کلام میں تاکید ہوگی اور اگر نکاح کو ولی پر محمول کریں تو کلام میں تاسیس ہوگی اور قاعدہ ہے الافادة خير من الاعادة یعنی تاسیس بہتر ہے تاکید سے اس لئے آیت میں نکاح کو وطی کے معنی پر محمول کریں گے پس اس تقریر پر زوج نانی کا وطی کرنا ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
اور حدیث سے شرط دخول اس طرح ثابت ہوگی کہ رفاعہ نے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانے میں اپنی بیوی کو تین طلاق دیں ۔ پھر اس نے عبدالرحمن بن زبیر سے شادی رچالی ۔ پھر حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس آکر کہنے لگی کہ اے اللہ کے رسول رفاعہ نے مجھ کو تین طلاقیں دیں پھر میں نے عبدالرحمن سے نکاح کر لیا مگر میں نے عبدالرحمن کو نا مرد پایا۔ آپ نے فرمایا اتريدين ان تعودي الى رفاعة - اس نے کہا جی ہاں میرا ارادہ یہی ہے آپ نے فرمایا لا حتى تذوقي عسلیته و يذوق عسیلتک یعنی نہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ تو اس کا مزہ چکھ لے اور وہ تیرا مزہ چکھ لے۔ اس سے کنایہ وطی مراد ہے پس اس حدیث سے ثابت ہو گیا ہے کہ حلالہ کے لئے زوج ثانی کا وطی کرنا شرط ہے اور یہ حدیث مشہور ہے اور حدیث مشہور سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی کرنا جائز ہے۔ لہذا اگر آیت حتی تنکے میں نکاح سے ولی کے معنی مراد نہ لئے جائیں تو اس آیت کو اس حدیث مشہور کے ساتھ مقید کر دیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ دخول کی شرط لگانے میں علاوہ سعید بن المسیب کے کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے اور حدیث مشہور کی وجہ سے سعید بن المسیب کا قول غیر معتبر ہے ۔ حتی کہ اگر کسی قاضی نے سعید بن المسیب کے قول پر فیصلہ صادر کیا تو اس فیصلہ کو نافذ نہیں کیا جائے گا اور اگر کسی مفتی نے اس پر فتوی دیا تو اس پر اللہ کی لعنت ملائکہ کی لعنت اور تمام لوگوں کی لعنت ۔ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ) اور زوج اول کے واسطے مطلقہ ثلاثہ کے حلال ہونے کی شرط زوج نانی کا عورت کی شرمگاہ میں حشفہ کا داخل کرنا ہے انزال یعنی منی کا پکا نا شرط نہیں ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ انزال ادخال میں کمال اور مبالغہ ہے اور کمال قید زائد ہے بغیر دلیل کے ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Chapter of the divorce of the ill. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya, volume five. The point is that the marriage of the second husband is absolute, not qualified by validity or invalidity. When something is said absolutely, its perfect individual is meant. Therefore, here absolute marriage means perfect marriage, and perfect marriage is established by a valid marriage. For this reason, we have made a valid marriage a condition for tahlil. And the second husband's intercourse with this woman is made a condition by indication of the text or by the well-known hadith. The explanation by indication of the text is that in the verse 'until she marries another husband', the word 'nikah' is to be interpreted in the meaning of intercourse, not in the meaning of contract, because the meaning of contract is derived from the word 'zawj' (husband) itself. For no person can be a husband without a contract. Therefore, if in the word 'nikah' the meaning of contract is intended, there would be emphasis in the speech; but if we interpret 'nikah' as intercourse, there would be establishment of a new meaning. The rule is: bringing benefit is better than repetition, i.e. establishing a new meaning is better than emphasis. For this reason, we interpret 'nikah' in the verse as intercourse. Thus, by this explanation, the intercourse of the second husband is established. And from the hadith, the condition of penetration is established as follows: Rifa'ah divorced his wife three times in the time of the Prophet ﷺ. Then she married 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr. Then she came to the Prophet ﷺ and said: O Messenger of Allah, Rifa'ah divorced me three times, then I married 'Abd al-Rahman, but I found him impotent. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Do you want to return to Rifa'ah?' She said: Yes, that is my intention. He said: 'No, until you taste his sweetness and he tastes your sweetness.' This is a metaphor for intercourse. So this hadith proves that for tahlil, the second husband's intercourse is a condition. And this is a well-known hadith, and it is permissible to add to the Book of Allah by a well-known hadith. Therefore, if the word 'nikah' in the verse 'until she marries' is not interpreted as intercourse, then this verse would be restricted by this well-known hadith. The author of Hidayah said: In imposing the condition of penetration, there is no difference except from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib; and due to the well-known hadith, the statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib is not reliable. So much so that if a judge passes a verdict based on the statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, that verdict will not be enforced, and if a mufti gives a fatwa on it, then upon him is the curse of Allah, the angels, and all people. (Ayni's commentary on Hidayah) And for the woman divorced three times to become halal for the first husband, the condition is the insertion of the glans of the second husband into her private part; emission (the spilling of semen) is not a condition. The proof is that emission is a perfection and exaggeration of insertion, and a perfection is an additional restriction which cannot be established without proof. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof regarding the condition of du khul (penetration) for tahlil (making a thrice-divorced woman halal for her first husband). The commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains that the condition is established from two sources: indication from the Quran and the well-known hadith of Rifa'ah. The Quranic verse 'until she marries another husband' uses the word 'nikah', which could mean either contract or intercourse. The Hanafi scholars argue that since the word 'zawj' already implies a contract, interpreting 'nikah' as intercourse (ta'sis) is better than interpreting it as contract (ta'kid), following the principle that establishing a new meaning is superior to mere repetition. The hadith of Rifa'ah clearly states that the woman must 'taste his sweetness' which is a metaphor for intercourse, making du khul a condition. The passage also notes that the only dissenter is Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, but his opinion is rejected because it contradicts the well-known hadith; a judge or mufti acting on it would be cursed. Finally, the condition is specified as mere insertion of the glans (ilaj al-hashafah), not emission (inzal), because emission is an additional perfection that lacks proof. The reasoning follows Hanafi principles of textual interpretation and legal theory.

Key Terms
تحليل (tahlil): The process by which a woman divorced three times becomes halal for her first husband after marrying and consummating a marriage with a second husband.
دخول (dukhul): Penetration, specifically the insertion of the glans (hashafah) into the woman's private part.
حنفي (hanafi): Refers to the Hanafi school as the authority in this commentary.
تأسیس (ta'sis): Establishing a new meaning, as opposed to ta'kid (emphasis). The principle that when a word can bear two interpretations, one adding new meaning is preferred.
تأکید (ta'kid): Emphasis, repeating the same meaning. Considered weaker than ta'sis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, tahlil requires actual penetration by the second husband; emission is not a condition.

Tahlil by a Murahiq: Hanafi vs Maliki Dispute
Determining that a minor near puberty is like an adult in tahlil if he can penetrate, with dispute with Malik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the tahlil of a murahiq, explain the Hanafi dalil, and compare it with the Maliki position.

Core Idea
A murahiq can perform tahlil if he can penetrate — emission is not required.

This passage addresses a nuanced fiqh issue: whether a minor nearing puberty can serve as a muhallil for a thrice-divorced woman. The Hanafi school, based on the primary texts, holds that the condition for tahlil is penetration (dukhul) alone, not emission. Imam Malik disagrees, requiring emission. The passage clarifies the Hanafi view and the implications for a murahiq.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that a murahiq (adolescent boy) is like an adult in tahlil because penetration in a valid marriage suffices.
Penetration is the condition by text (nass).
2
Identify the opposing view
Note that Imam Malik rejects this, requiring emission (inzal) for tahlil.
Emission is unlikely from a murahiq, so Maliki view invalidates his tahlil.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Recall that the primary texts (Quran 2:230 and hadith of Rifa'ah) mention only marriage and consummation, not emission.
The hadith 'taste its sweetness' is interpreted as intercourse, not emission.
4
Analyse the Maliki objection and Hanafi response
Maliki requires inzal; Hanafi response: emission is a perfection (kamal), not a condition. The apparent cause (iltaqa al-khitanan) stands for the inner cause.
This is based on the earlier discussion in the text.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If a murahiq with desire penetrates a thrice-divorced woman, she becomes halal for the first husband in Hanafi; in Maliki, she does not.
The dispute has direct application in marriage and talaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صبی مراحق تحلیل میں بالغ کی طرح ہے
والصبي المراهق في التحليل كالبالغ لوجود الدخول فى نكاح صحيح وهو شرط بالنص ومالك يخالفنا فيه والحجة عليه ما بيناه وفسره فى الجامع الصغير وقال غلام لم يبلغ ومثله يجامع جامع امرأة وجب عليها الغسل واحلها على الزوج الاول ومعنى هذا الكلام ان يتحرك الله ويشتهى وانما وجب الغسل عليها لالتقا الختانين وهو سبب لنزول مائها والحاجة الى الايجاب فى حقها امالا غسل على الصبى وان كان يؤمر به تخلقا

ترجمہ اور جو بچہ قریب البلوغ ہو وہ حلالہ کرنے میں بالغ کی طرح ہے۔ نکاح صحیح میں دخول کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور یہی شرط ہے نص حدیث سے اور مراہق کے مسئلہ میں امام مالک ہمارے مخالف ہیں اور ان کے خلاف حجت وہی دلیل ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے اور امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں مراہق کی تفسیر کی اور کہا کہ لڑکا جو بالغ نہیں ہوا حالانکہ ایسا لڑ کا جماع کر سکتا ہے۔ اس نے کسی عورت سے جماع کیا تو اس عورت پر غسل واجب ہوگا اور اس عورت کو پہلے شوہر پر حلال کر دیا اور (امام محمد کے ) اس کلام کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس کا عضو تناسل حرکت کرتا اور خواہش کرتا ہو اور عورت ہی پر غسل واجب ہوا دونوں ختان کے مل جانے کی وجہ سے اور یہی عورت کی منی اترنے کا سبب ہے اور (غسل) واجب کرنے کی ضرورت صرف عورت کے حق میں ہے لیکن ( مراہق ) لڑکے پر غسل (واجب) نہیں ہے۔ اگر چہ اس کو عادت ڈالنے کے لئے حکم دیا جائے گا۔
تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ مراہق لڑکا مطلقہ ثلاثہ کو زوج اول کے واسطے حلال کرنے میں بالغ کے حکم میں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح صحیح میں دخول پایا گیا اور تحلیل کے لئے نص یعنی حتی تنکح زوجا غیرہ سے یہی شرط ہے اور مراہق کے مسئلہ میں امام مالک ہماری مخالفت کرتے ہیں یعنی امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ مراہق کا حلالہ کرنا معتبر نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کہ ان کے نزدیک حلالہ میں ادخال کافی نہیں بلکہ انزال شرط ہے اور انزال مراہق سے متصور نہیں۔ اس لئے حلالہ کرنے میں مراہق لڑ کا بالغ کے حکم میں نہیں ہو گا مگر امام مالک کے خلاف وہ دلیل حجت ہوگی جو ہم سابق میں بیان کر چکے۔ دلیل سابق سے مراد مصنف کا قول لانه كمال و مبالغة اورا ترازی نے کہا کہ امام مالک کے خلاف حجت آیت حتی تنکح زوجا غیرہ ہے اور کا کئی نے فرمایا کہ امام مالک کے خلاف حجت حدیث عملہ ستر کی تفسہ جامع صغیر میں امام محمد نے مراہق کی تغییر یہ کی ہے کہ وہ لڑکا جو ابھی تک بلوغ کو نہیں پہنچا، حالانکہ اس جیسا لڑکا جماع کر سکتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مراہق نے کسی عورت سے جماع کیا تو اس عورت پر غسل واجب ہوگا اور اگر وہ کسی کی مطلقہ ثلاثہ تھی تو مراہق کے جماع کے بعد زوج اول کے لئے حلال ہو جائے گی بشرطیکہ مراہق کی طرف سے اس پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے اور یہ عورت عدت پوری کرلے مراہق کی تفسیر میں حضرت امام محمد کے قول کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ مراہق کا عضو تناسل حرکت کرتا اور جماع کی طرف راغب ہوتا ہو اور یہ شرط اس لئے لگائی گئی ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے دونوں طرف سے ذوق کی شرط لگائی ہے اور ذوق ( چکھنا) بغیر اشتہا اور رغبت کے نہیں ہو سکتا ۔
اور عورت پر خاص طور سے غسل واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ انتقا تا نین پایا گیا اور یہ ہی سبب ہے عورت کی منی کے اترنے کا۔ پس سبب ظاہر ( التقاء ختانین ) کو سبب باطن (انزال) کے قائم مقام بنا کر غسل کا حکم لگا دیا گیا۔ ر غسل واجب کرنے کی ضرورت عورت کے حق میں ہے اور رہا مراہق تو اس پر غسل واجب نہیں ۔ کیونکہ وہ احکام شرع کا مخاطب نہیں ہے اگر چہ اس کو غسل کا حکم دیا جائے گا تا کہ اس کو غسل کرنے کی عادت پڑے۔
اور
An adolescent boy near puberty is like an adult in tahlil because penetration occurs in a valid marriage, which is the condition by text. Imam Malik disagrees with us on this, and the proof against him is what we have explained. He interpreted it in al-Jami' al-Saghir and said: A boy who has not reached puberty but who can have intercourse, if he has intercourse with a woman, ghusl becomes obligatory on her, and he makes her halal for the first husband. The meaning of this statement is that his penis moves and he desires. And ghusl is obligatory on her only because of the meeting of the two circumcised parts, which is the cause of her fluid descending. The need for making it obligatory is only in her case. But there is no ghusl on the boy, although he is commanded to do it for habituation. 

Translation: And the boy who is close to puberty is like an adult in performing tahlil due to the presence of penetration in a valid marriage, and this is the condition from the text of hadith. In the matter of the murahiq, Imam Malik is our opponent, and the proof against him is the same evidence we have already stated. Imam Muhammad interpreted the murahiq in al-Jami' al-Saghir and said: A boy who has not reached puberty, yet such a boy can copulate. If he copulates with a woman, ghusl becomes obligatory on that woman, and he makes her halal for the first husband. The meaning of Imam Muhammad's statement is that his penis moves and he has desire. Ghusl is obligatory on the woman only due to the meeting of the two circumcised parts, which is the cause of the woman's fluid descending. The need for making ghusl obligatory is only in her right, but ghusl is not obligatory on the boy (murahiq), although he is commanded to do it for habituation.

Explanation: It is stated that the murahiq boy is in the same ruling as an adult in making the thrice-divorced woman halal for the first husband. The proof is that penetration occurs in a valid marriage, and for tahlil, the text (i.e., 'until she marries another husband') establishes this condition. In the matter of the murahiq, Imam Malik opposes us. That is, Imam Malik says that the tahlil of the murahiq is not valid because, in his view, mere insertion is not sufficient; rather, emission is a condition, and emission from the murahiq is not conceivable. Therefore, the murahiq boy is not like an adult in tahlil. But the proof against Imam Malik is what we have previously stated. 'Previous proof' refers to the author's statement: 'because it is perfection and exaggeration.' And al-Attazi said that the proof against Imam Malik is the verse 'until she marries another husband.' And some said that the proof against Imam Malik is the hadith of 'taste his sweetness.' In al-Jami' al-Saghir, Imam Muhammad defined the murahiq as a boy who has not yet reached puberty, yet such a boy can copulate. The author of Hidayah says: If a murahiq copulates with a woman, ghusl becomes obligatory on her, and if she was a thrice-divorced woman of someone, she becomes halal for the first husband after the murahiq's copulation, provided that divorce occurs from the murahiq and she completes her 'iddah. The meaning of Imam Muhammad's definition of murahiq is that the boy's penis moves and he is inclined toward copulation. This condition is imposed because the Prophet ﷺ imposed the condition of tasting from both sides, and tasting cannot occur without inclination and desire.

And ghusl becomes obligatory specifically on the woman because the meeting of the two circumcised parts has occurred, and this is the cause of the woman's fluid descending. Thus, the apparent cause (meeting of circumcised parts) is made to stand in place of the inner cause (emission) to apply the ruling of ghusl. The need for making ghusl obligatory is only in the woman's right. As for the murahiq, ghusl is not obligatory on him because he is not addressed by the rulings of Shari'ah, although he is commanded to do it so that he acquires the habit of performing ghusl.

And
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling regarding a sabi murahiq (a boy nearing puberty) in the context of tahlil. The author states that such a boy, though not yet baligh, is equivalent to an adult for the purpose of tahlil because he can achieve penetration (du khul) in a valid marriage, which is the condition established by the text (the Quran and hadith). The passage then introduces the dispute with Imam Malik, who requires emission (inzal) as a condition for tahlil. Since emission is unlikely from a minor, Malik considers the murahiq's tahlil invalid. The Hanafi response, building on the earlier discussion, argues that only penetration is needed, not emission, because emission is a perfection beyond the requirement. The text then explains Imam Muhammad's definition of the murahiq in al-Jami' al-Saghir: a boy who has not reached puberty but can have intercourse, indicated by movement and desire. The application is that if such a boy penetrates a woman, ghusl becomes obligatory on her due to the meeting of the circumcised parts (iltaqa al-khitanan), even if no emission occurs. This same condition (penetration with desire) suffices for tahlil. The passage also clarifies that the boy himself is not obligated to perform ghusl because he is not legally responsible, though he is encouraged to do so for habituation. The overall ruling reinforces that the Hanafi school focuses on the external act of penetration (khalwah or actual du khul) rather than internal emission.

Key Terms
صبي مراهق (sabi murahiq): A boy who is near puberty (i.e., has reached the age where he can have intercourse, typically about 12-15 years old, but still below the age of legal majority).
تحليل (tahlil): The process of making a thrice-divorced woman halal for her first husband through a valid marriage and consummation with a second husband.
إنزال (inzal): Emission of semen. In this context, it is not required for tahlil according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the key condition for a murahiq boy to perform valid tahlil?
A) He must have reached puberty
B) He must have emission of semen
C) He must be able to penetrate and have sexual desire
D) He must be at least 15 years old

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the condition for tahlil is penetration (du khul) with desire, not emission, so a murahiq who meets this condition can make a thrice-divorced woman halal.
